Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh and Its Qualifiers
Explaining the qayd in the Hanafi definition of fiqh and critiquing Ibn Hajib's addition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain each qayd in the Hanafi definition of fiqh and evaluate Ibn Hajib's addition of 'al-istidlal'.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of Shari'ah's practical rulings from detailed evidences; each qualifier excludes non-fiqh knowledge.

The Hanafi school defines fiqh with precision: each restriction (qayd) in the definition removes a category that might otherwise be included. This lesson walks through those qualifiers and also addresses a refinement proposed by the Maliki scholar Ibn Hajib, which the Hanafi commentator argues is unnecessary. Understanding these boundaries is essential for grasping the scope of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentiae
The definition starts with the genus 'knowledge' and then adds differentiae (qualifiers) to narrow fiqh to its correct scope. Your task is to list each qualifier in order and note what it excludes.
The qualifiers are: al-shar'iyyah, al-'amaliyyah, min adillatiha, al-tafṣīliyyah.
2
Analyze each qualifier's function
For each qualifier, state what category of knowledge it excludes and give an example from the text.
E.g., al-shar'iyyah excludes intellectual and sensory rulings.
3
Understand the exclusion of taqlid
The qualifier 'min adillatiha' excludes taqlid (following a mujtahid). Explain why the muqallid's knowledge is not fiqh according to this definition.
The muqallid does not have detailed evidence; he relies on the mujtahid's statement, which is not among the four sources.
4
Evaluate Ibn Hajib's addition
Ibn Hajib added 'al-istidlal' (inference) to exclude taqlid explicitly. Determine from the text whether this addition is necessary or redundant, and provide the Hanafi reasoning.
The Hanafi argument: taqlid is already excluded by 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah'; adding 'istidlal' is redundant.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence of this difference: the Hanafi definition is more concise and avoids redundancy.
No change in the scope of fiqh; both definitions exclude taqlid.

تو بریقات کا علم رہ جائے گا اور الشرعیہ کی قید سے ان احکام کا علم نکل جائے گا جو شریعت کی جانب سے نہیں ہیں یعنی احکام [؟] عقلیہ اور احکام حسیہ نکل جائیں گے حکم عقلی کی مثال جیسے العالم حادث اور حکم حسی کی مثال النار حارة النار محرقہ اور اگر حکم سے دوسرا معنی مراد لیا جائے تو احکام کی قید سے وہ علوم خارج ہو جائیں گے جن کا تعلق اللہ تعالیٰ کے خطاب کے ساتھ نہیں ہے اور پھر چونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے خطاب میں بعض وہ ہیں جو شریعت پر موقوف ہیں جن کو احکام شرعیہ کہا جاتا ہے اور بعض وہ ہیں جو شریعت پر موقوف نہیں ہیں جن کو احکام غیر شرعیہ کہا جاتا ہے جیسے ایمان کا واجب ہونا اور نبی علیہ السلام کی تصدیق کرنا یہ احکام شریعت پر موقوف نہیں ہیں بلکہ شریعت ان پر موقوف ہے تو احکام میں یہ دونوں ( حکم شرعی ، غیر شرعی ) داخل تھے اس لئے الشرعیہ کی قید لگا کر احکام غیر شرعیہ کو فقہ کی تعریف سے خارج کر دیا کیونکہ ان کے علم کو فقہ نہیں کہا جاتا اور پھر شرعی میں وہ احکام بھی داخل تھے جن کا تعلق فکر و نظر کے ساتھ ہے یعنی احکام نظریہ جیسے کہ الا جماع حجتہ ، اور وہ احکام بھی داخل تھے جن کا تعلق ت عمل کے ساتھ ہے یعنی احکام عملیہ ،تو العملیہ کی قید سے احکام نظریہ کو خارج کر دیا کیونکہ ان کے علم کو بھی فقہ نہیں کہتے پھر احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کے حصول کے دو طریقے ہیں ایک تو یہ ہے کہ ادلہ اربعہ (جن پر احکام کا مدار ہے ) سے حاصل ہوں اور دوسرا یہ کہ مجتہد کے اقوال سے حاصل ہوں اور مجتہد کے اقوال سے احکام کے جاننے کو تقلید کہتے ہیں فقہ نہیں کہتے کیونکہ علم فقہ کا مدار ادلہ اربعہ میں سے ہے اور مجتہد کا قول اگر چہ مقلد کے لئے دلیل ہوتا ہے لیکن وہ ادلہ اربعہ میں سے نہیں ہے تو اس سے تقلید کو خارج کرنے کے لئے تعریف میں من ادلتہا کی قید لگائی کیونکہ اس سے مراد ادلہ اربعہ ہیں لہذا اس سے تقلید خارج ہوگئی اور ا تفصیلیہ کی قید سے اس علم کو نکال دیا جو ادلہ اربعہ تفصیلیہ سے حاصل نہیں ہوتا ہے جیسے مقتضی کہ یہ مقتضی پر دلیل ہوتا ہے اور نانی [؟] کہ یہ منفی پر دلیل ہوتا ہے لیکن یہ اولہ [؟] اجمالیہ میں سے ہیں تفصیلیہ میں نہیں نہیں اس لئے تفصیلیہ کی قید سے ان کو خارج کر دیا۔ علامہ ابن حاجب پررد
و قد زاد ابن حاجب:۔ یہاں سے ماتن علامہ ابن حاجب پر رد فرمارہے ہیں تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ علامہ ابن حاجب نے فقہ کی تعریف پر الاستدلال کی قید کا اضافہ کیا ہے ماتن فرماتے ہیں استدلال کی قید سے مقلد کے علم کو خارج کرنا چاہتے ہیں حالانکہ مقلد کا علم تو من اولتها التفصیلیہ کی قید سے خارج ہو چکا ہے جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل گذر چکی لید الیقینا [؟] بالاستدلال کی قید میں تکرار ہے۔
Then the knowledge of [؟] remains, and by the restriction of 'al-shar'iyyah', the knowledge of those rulings that are not from the side of Shari'ah exits, meaning the intellectual rulings and sensory rulings exit. Example of an intellectual ruling: the universe is originated; example of a sensory ruling: fire is hot, fire burns. And if another meaning is taken from 'ruling', then by the restriction of 'rulings', those knowledges exit that are not related to the address of Allah. Then, since in the address of Allah there are some that are dependent on Shari'ah, called Shari rulings, and some that are not dependent on Shari'ah, called non-Shari rulings, such as the obligation of faith and affirming the Prophet (peace be upon him); these rulings are not dependent on Shari'ah, rather Shari'ah depends on them. So in 'rulings', both (Shari and non-Shari) were included. Thus, by adding the restriction of 'al-shar'iyyah', non-Shari rulings are excluded from the definition of fiqh, because their knowledge is not called fiqh. Then in 'Shari', those rulings were also included that are related to thought and consideration, i.e., theoretical rulings, such as consensus is an evidence, and those rulings related to action, i.e., practical rulings. So by the restriction of 'al-'amaliyyah', theoretical rulings are excluded, because their knowledge is also not called fiqh. Then there are two ways to obtain Shari practical rulings: one is that they are obtained from the four evidences (on which rulings depend), and the second is that they are obtained from the statements of a mujtahid. Knowing rulings from the statements of a mujtahid is called taqlid, not fiqh, because the basis of the knowledge of fiqh is among the four evidences. The statement of a mujtahid, although it is a proof for the muqallid, is not among the four evidences. So to exclude taqlid, the restriction of 'min adillatiha' was placed in the definition, because by it is meant the four evidences. Thus taqlid is excluded. And by the restriction of 'al-tafṣīliyyah', that knowledge is removed which is not obtained from the detailed four evidences, like [؟] that it is a proof for its [؟] and [؟] that it is a proof for the negative. But these are from the general [؟] evidences, not from the detailed. So by the restriction of 'al-tafṣīliyyah', they are excluded. Refutation of Allamah Ibn Hajib.
And Ibn Hajib added: From here, the matn refutes Allamah Ibn Hajib. The detail is that Allamah Ibn Hajib added the restriction of 'al-istidlal' to the definition of fiqh. The matn says: By the restriction of 'istidlal', he intends to exclude the knowledge of the muqallid, whereas the knowledge of the muqallid has already been excluded by the restriction of 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah', as its detail has passed. Thus, there is redundancy in the restriction of 'lil-istiqlal [؟] bi al-istidlal'.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Hanafi definition of fiqh. The author systematically explains each qualifier (qayd) in the definition: 'al-shar'iyyah' excludes non-Shari rulings derived from reason or senses; 'al-'amaliyyah' excludes theoretical rulings (like the evidential value of consensus); 'min adillatiha' excludes taqlid (following a mujtahid without knowing the evidence); and 'al-tafṣīliyyah' excludes knowledge from general evidence (like the general principles 'every obligation is indicated by a proof'). The passage then addresses a critique by Ibn Hajib, who added 'al-istidlal' (inference) to the definition. The author argues this is redundant because the muqallid's knowledge is already excluded by the previous qualifier. The discussion follows the order of the definition: first the genus (knowledge), then the differentia (restrictions), finishing with the refutation of an alternative formulation.

Key Terms
حکم عقلی (hukm 'aqli): A ruling derived from reason alone, e.g., that the universe is originated.
حکم حسی (hukm hissi): A ruling derived from the senses, e.g., that fire burns.
ادله اربعه (adillah arba'ah): The four sources of evidence: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
تقلید (taqlid): Accepting the ruling of a mujtahid without knowing the evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how does the Hanafi definition exclude the knowledge of the muqallid?
A) By adding the qualifier 'al-istidlal'.
B) By the qualifier 'al-shar'iyyah'.
C) By the qualifier 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah'.
D) By the qualifier 'al-'amaliyyah'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh uses multiple qualifiers to precisely exclude non-fiqh knowledge, and the addition of 'istidlal' by Ibn Hajib is considered redundant.

The Shafi'i Definition of Fiqh: Exclusions and Agreement
Shafi'i definition with exclusions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five categories of knowledge excluded from the Shafi'i definition of fiqh and explain how the Hanafi and Shafi'i definitions are structurally identical yet differ in the scope of 'detailed evidences'.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of practical Shari rulings from detailed evidences; all else is excluded.

Al-Talwih quotes the Shafi'i definition of fiqh, which performs a systematic breakdown by exclusion. Though the wording matches the Hanafi definition you have already studied, the Shafi'i school excludes istihsan-derived rulings from fiqh. This lesson dissects the definition and its exclusions, sharpening your ability to classify knowledge within usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Isolate the core definition
Identify the defining phrase: 'knowledge of the Shari practical rulings from their detailed evidences.' This is the nucleus. All other parts are exclusions.
The definition is a genus (knowledge) plus differentiae (subject: ahkam shar'iyyah 'amaliyyah, source: adillah tafṣīliyyah).
2
Map the exclusion sequence
Follow the logical tree: object of knowledge → ruling or non-ruling. Then ruling → Shari or non-Shari. Then Shari → practical or theoretical. Then practical → derived from detailed evidence or not. Each branch yields an exclusion.
The passage explicitly excludes: non-rulings, non-Shari rulings, theoretical Shari rulings, and knowledge not from detailed evidences (Allah, angels, prophets, muqallid).
3
Compare with the Hanafi definition
Note that the wording is identical to the Hanafi definition from the previous lesson. The only difference is in the interpretation of 'detailed evidences': Shafi'i restricts to Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas; Hanafi includes istihsan, 'urf, and others.
This difference has practical consequences: e.g., rulings based on istihsan are fiqh for Hanafis but not for Shafi'is.
4
Apply the definition to an example
Take the ruling 'the 'Asr prayer is obligatory.' Knowledge of this from the Quran and Sunnah (detailed evidence) is fiqh. Knowledge of the same ruling via taqlid (accepting a scholar's opinion without evidence) is not fiqh according to the definition.
This illustrates why the muqallid's knowledge is excluded: it is not derived directly from detailed evidences.

Source Text

قَوْلُهُ ) وَقِيلَ الْعِلْمُ) عَرَّفَ أَصْحَابُ الشَّافِعِي رَحِمَهُمُ اللهُ تَعَالَى الْفِقْه بأنَّهُ الْعِلْمُ بِالأحْكَامِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ الْعَمَلِيَّةِ مِنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ وَبَيَّانُ ذَلِكَ أَنَّ مُتَعَلَّقَ الْعِلْمِ إِمَّا حُكُمْ أَوْ غَيْرُهُ وَالْحُكْمُ إِمَّا مَأْخُودٌ مِنَ الشَّرْعِ أَوْلَا وَالْمَأْعُوذُ مِنَ الشَّرْعِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِكَيْفِيَّةِ الْعَمَلِ أَوْ لَا وَالْعَمَلُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْعِلْمُ بِهِ حَاصِلًا مِنْ دَلِيلِهِ التَّفْصِيلِيِّ الَّذِي نِيطَ بِهِ الْحُكْمُ أَوْ لَا فَالْعِلْمُ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِجَمِيعِ الأحكام الشَّرْعِيَّةِ الْعَمَلِيَّةِ الحَاصِلُ مِنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ هُوَ الْفِقْهُ وَخَرَجَ الْعِلْمُ بِغَيْرِ الْأَحْكَامِ مِنْ الدَّوَاتِ وَالصَّفَاتِ وَالْعِلْمُ بِالأحْكامِ الْغَيْرِ الْمَأْخُودَةِ مِنَ الشَّرْعِ كَالْأحْكَامِ الْمَأْخُودَةِ مِنْ الْعَقْلِ كَالْعِلْمِ بِأَنَّ الْعَالَمَ حَادِتْ أَوْ مِنْ الْحِسْ كَالْعِلْمِ بِأَنَّ النَّارَ مُحْرِقَةٌ أَوْ مِنْ الْوَضْعِ وَالاصْطِلاحِ كَالْعِلْمِ بِأَنَّ الْفَاعِلَ مَرْفُوعٌ وَخَرَجَ الْعِلْمُ بالأحكام الشَّرْعِيَّة النَّظَرِيَّةِ وَتُسَمَّى اعْتِقَادِيَّةٌ وَأَصْلِيَّةٌ كَكَوْنِ الْإِجْمَاعِ حُجَّةً وَالْإِيمَانِ وَاجِبًا وَخَرَجَ أَيْضًا عِلْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَعِلْمُ جِبْرِيلَ وَالرَّسُولِ عَلَيْهِمَا الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ وَكَذَا عِلْمُ الْمُقَلّدِ ; لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْصُلُ مِنْ الَّا دِلَّةِ التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ.
ترجمہ: ۔ تعریف کی ہے اصحاب شافعی نے فقہ کی بائیں طور کہ وہ جاننا ہے احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کو ادلہ تفصیلیہ سے اور تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ کہ علم کا متعلقیا تو حکم ہے یا اس کے علاوہ ہے اور حکم یا تو ماخوذ ہوگا شریعت سے یا نہیں اور وہ جو ماخوذ ہوگا شریعت سے یا تو متعلق ہوگا کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ یا نہیں اور عمل یا تو اس کا علم حاصل ہوگا ایسی دلیل تفصیلی سے جس پر مدار رکھا گیا ہے حکم کا یا نہیں پس وہ علم جو متعلق ہوتا ہے تمام احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کے ساتھ اور جو حاصل ہوتا ہے ادلہ تفصیلیہ سے وہ فقہ ہے اور خارج ہو جائے گا علم غیر احکام کا یعنی جو ذوات وصفات میں سے ہو اور علم ان احکام کے ساتھ جو نہیں ہوتے ماخوذ شریعت سے مثل ان احکام کے جو ماخوذ ہوتے ہیں عقل سے جیسے جاننا اس بات کا کہ عالم حادث ہے یا ماخوذ ہوں جس سے جیسے جاننا اس بات کا کہ آگ جلانے والی ہے یا ماخوذ ہوں وضع سے اور اصطلاح سے جیسے جاننا اس بات کا کہ فاعل مرفوع ہوتا ہے اور نکل جائے گا وہ علم جو حاصل ہوتا ہے احکام شرعیہ نظریہ کے ساتھ اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے ان کا اعتقاد یہ اور اصلیہ مثل اجتماع کا حجت ہونا اور ہونا رسول ایمان کا واجب ہونا اور نکل جائے گا اللہ تعالیٰ کا علم بھی اور جبریل علیہ السلام کا علم بھی اور رسول اللہ اللہ کا علم بھی اور اسی طرح مقلد کا علم بھی اس لئے کہ وہ نہیں حاصل ہوتا ادلہ تفصیل یہ ہے۔
His statement: 'And it was said: Knowledge.' The companions of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) defined fiqh as: knowledge of the Shari practical rulings from their detailed evidences. And the explanation of that is that the object of knowledge is either a ruling or other than it. The ruling is either taken from the Shari'ah or not. What is taken from the Shari'ah either relates to the modality of action or not. And action: either its knowledge is obtained from its detailed evidence upon which the ruling depends, or not. So the knowledge that relates to all Shari practical rulings and is obtained from their detailed evidences is fiqh. And knowledge of other than rulings exits, i.e., of substances and attributes; and knowledge of rulings not taken from the Shari'ah, such as rulings taken from reason, like knowledge that the universe is originated, or from sense, like knowledge that fire burns, or from convention and terminology, like knowledge that the agent (grammatical subject) is raised; and knowledge of Shari theoretical rulings exits, called belief-based and fundamental, like that consensus is a proof and that faith is obligatory; and also the knowledge of Allah, the knowledge of Jibra'il, and the Messenger (peace be upon them) exits, and likewise the knowledge of the muqallid, because it is not obtained from the detailed evidences.
Translation: The Shafi'i scholars defined fiqh as: knowing the Shari practical rulings from detailed evidences. And its detail is that the object of knowledge is either a ruling or something else. The ruling is either taken from Shari'ah or not. That which is taken from Shari'ah either relates to the modality of action or not. Action: either its knowledge is obtained from a detailed evidence on which the ruling depends, or not. So that knowledge which relates to all Shari practical rulings and is obtained from detailed evidences is fiqh. And knowledge of non-rulings exits, i.e., what is among substances and attributes; and knowledge of rulings that are not taken from Shari'ah, like rulings taken from reason, such as knowing that the universe is originated, or taken from sense, such as knowing that fire burns, or taken from convention and terminology, such as knowing that the agent is raised; and that knowledge which is obtained about Shari theoretical rulings exits, and they are called belief-based and fundamental, like that consensus is a proof and that faith is obligatory; and the knowledge of Allah, the knowledge of Jibra'il, and the knowledge of the Messenger of Allah exit, and similarly the knowledge of the muqallid, because it is not obtained from detailed evidences.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage from Al-Talwih presents the Shafi'i definition of fiqh. It follows the same structural breakdown as the Hanafi definition but is attributed to the Shafi'i school. The passage systematically excludes: (1) knowledge of non-rulings (e.g., substances and attributes), (2) rulings from reason or senses (e.g., 'the universe is originated'), (3) conventional rulings (e.g., grammar), (4) theoretical Shari rulings (like 'ijma is a proof'), and (5) the knowledge of Allah, angels, prophets, and muqallids. The core idea remains: fiqh is knowledge of practical Shari rulings derived from the specific detailed evidences. This mirrors the Hanafi definition, showing agreement on the core, though the Shafi'i school may differ in the epistemological weight of those evidences.

Key Terms
احکام شرعیہ عملیہ (ahkam shar'iyyah 'amaliyyah): Rulings from Shari'ah that relate to practical actions of the mukallaf.
ادلة تفصیلیة (adillah tafṣīliyyah): Specific detailed evidences (Quranic verses, hadith, etc.) that indicate a particular ruling.
احکام نظریہ (ahkam nazariyyah): Theoretical rulings, like the evidential value of consensus or the obligation of faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shafi'i definition as quoted, which of the following is NOT excluded from the definition of fiqh?
A) Knowledge that the universe is originated.
B) Knowledge that fire burns.
C) Knowledge that Zakat is obligatory based on detailed evidence.
D) Knowledge of the muqallid.

Key Takeaway
The Shafi'i definition of fiqh is structurally identical to the Hanafi definition; the only disagreement is over what constitutes 'detailed evidences', affecting which rulings are classified as fiqh.

The Problem of Dawr: Do All Rulings Depend on Shari'ah?
Debates whether rulings like wujub al-iman depend on shari'ah, refuting circularity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why wujub al-iman is excluded from the definition of shar'i hukm and evaluate the circularity argument that supports this exclusion.

Core Idea
If wujub al-iman depended on shari'ah, circularity would result; hence it is not 'shar'i' in that sense.

This passage tackles a foundational question in usul al-fiqh: Are all rulings dependent on the Shari'ah? The author argues that rulings like the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman) cannot be dependent on Shari'ah because establishing the Shari'ah itself requires prior faith. This leads to a logical problem of circularity (dawr). Let us dissect the argument and the subsequent objections.

Guided Path
1
Define 'shar'i hukm'
Identify the definition the author critiques: a shar'i ruling is one that depends on the Shari'ah and cannot be known without divine address.
2
Categorize rulings
Distinguish between rulings that depend on Shari'ah (e.g., prayer) and those that do not (e.g., obligation of faith).
3
Trace the circularity argument
Understand the logic: if wujub al-iman depended on Shari'ah, then Shari'ah would depend on it (since Shari'ah requires faith), causing dawr.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Examine the objection
The objector says Shari'ah depends on actual faith, not its obligation; thus no circularity.
They distinguish between iman (actual faith) and wujub al-iman (its obligation).
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that dependence on actual faith does not negate that the obligation itself may still depend on Shari'ah, upholding the principle 'no obligation except through revelation'.
This reinforces the distinction between ontological dependence and epistemic obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَذَهَبَ إِلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالشَّرْعِيِّ مَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى الشَّرْعِ وَلَا يُدْرَكُ لَوْلَا خِطَابُ الشَّارِعِ وَالْأَحْكَامُ مِنْهَا مَا هُوَ خِطَابٌ بِمَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى الشَّرْعِ كَوُجُوبِ الصَّلَاةِ وَالصَّوْمِ وَمِنْهَا مَا هُوَ خِطَابٌ بِمَا لَا يَتَوَفَّفُ عَلَيْهِ كَوُجُوبِ الْإِيمَان بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَوُجُوبِ تَصْدِيقِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ؛ لأنَّ ثُبُوتَ الشَّرُعَ مَوْقُوفٌ عَلَى الْإِيمَانِ بِوُجُودِ الْبَارِى تَعَالَى وَعِلْمِهِ وَقُدْرَتِهِ وَ كَلَامِهِ وَعَلَى التَّصْدِيقِ بِنُبُوَّةِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِدَلَالَةِ مُعْجِزَاتِهِ فَلَوْ تَوَفَّفَ شَيْءٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَحْكَام عَلَى الشَّرُع لَزِمَ الدَّوْرُ فَالتَّقْسِيدُ بِالشَّرْعِيَّةِ يُخْرِجُ هَذِهِ الْأَحْكامَ ؛ لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ شَرْعِيَّةٌ بِمَعْنَى التَّوَقُفِ عَلَى الشَّرْعِ ، وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ الْخِطَابُ بمَا يَتَوَقَّفُ أَوْ لَا يَتَوَفَّف ؛ لأنَّ الْحُكْمَ الْمُفَسَّرَ بِالْخِطَابَ قَدِيمٌ عِندَهُمْ فَكَيْفَ يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى الشَّرْعِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَمْنَعَ تَوَقُفَ الشَّرْعِ عَلَى وُجُوبِ الْإِيمَانِ وَنَحْوِهِ سَوَاءٌ أُرِيدَ بِالشَّرْعِ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ شَرِيعَةُ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَتَوَقُفُ التَّصْدِيقِ بِثْبُوتِ شَرْعِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى الْإِيمَانِ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَصِفَاتِهِ وَعَلَى التَّصْدِيقِ بِنُبُوَّةِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَدَلَالَةِ مُعْجِزَاتِهِ لَا يَقْتَضِي تَوَقَّفَهُ عَلَى وُجُوبِ الْإِيمَانِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ وَلَا عَلَى الْعِلْمِ بِوُجُوبِهِمَا غَايَتُهُ أَنَّهُ يَتَوَفَّفُ عَلَى نَفْسِ الْإِيمَانِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ ، وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مُفيدٍ وَلَا مُنَافِ لِتَوَقُفِ وُجُوبِ الْإِيمَانِ وَنَحْوِهِ عَلَى الشَّرُعَ كَمَا هُوَ الْمَذْهَبُ عِنْدَهُمْ مِنْ أَنْ لَا وُجُوبَ إِلَّا بِالسَّمْعِ
He went to the view that what is meant by 'shar'i' is that which depends on the Shari'ah and cannot be known without the address of the Lawgiver. Some rulings are an address regarding what depends on the Shari'ah, like the obligation of prayer and fasting. And some are an address regarding what does not depend on it, like the obligation of faith in God and the obligation of affirming the Prophet ﷺ, because the establishment of the Shari'ah depends on faith in the existence of God, His knowledge, power, and speech, and on affirming the prophethood of the Prophet ﷺ by the evidence of his miracles. So if any of these rulings depended on the Shari'ah, circularity would occur. Therefore, the restriction to 'shar'iyyah' excludes these rulings because they are not shar'i in the sense of depending on the Shari'ah. He said 'the address regarding what depends or does not depend' because the ruling that is interpreted as address is eternal in their view, so how could it depend on the Shari'ah? But one may object by denying the dependence of the Shari'ah on the obligation of faith and the like, whether by 'Shari'ah' is meant the address of God or the law of the Prophet ﷺ. The dependence of affirming the establishment of the Prophet's law on faith in God and His attributes and on affirming the prophethood of the Prophet ﷺ and the evidence of his miracles does not entail its dependence on the obligation of faith and affirmation, nor on knowing their obligation. At most, it depends on the actual faith and affirmation, which neither benefits nor contradicts the dependence of the obligation of faith and the like on the Shari'ah, as is their school that there is no obligation except through divine revelation (sam').
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a disputation (ikhtilaf) regarding the definition of 'shar'i hukm' and whether all rulings depend on shari'ah. The author (probably al-Quduri or the commentator) argues that some rulings like wujub al-iman (obligation of faith) must precede shari'ah because proving the truth of the shari'ah itself requires prior belief in God and the Prophet. If these rulings depended on shari'ah, circularity (dawr) would result: shari'ah would depend on them and they on shari'ah. Hence, the qualifier 'shar'iyyah' in the definition of hukm excludes such rulings. The commentator also notes that the ruling as khitab (divine address) is eternal (qadim) for the Hanafis, so it cannot be temporally dependent on shari'ah. He then addresses an objection: one might argue that shari'ah does not depend on the obligation of faith but on actual faith, so circularity is avoided. The commentator counters that dependence on actual faith does not negate that the obligation of faith itself may depend on shari'ah, as the Hanafi principle holds that no obligation exists without revelation (la wujuba illa bi al-sam'). This is a nuanced discussion of the usul principle that some rational obligations (like belief in God) are known by reason but their obligation in the shar'i sense requires revelation.

Key Terms
الدَّوْر (al-dawr): Circular reasoning or dependency where A depends on B and B depends on A.
السَّمْع (al-samʿ): Revelation; divine communication that establishes obligation.
الْإِيمَان (al-īmān): Faith in God and His attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman) not considered a shar'i ruling in the sense of depending on shari'ah?
A) Because it is impossible to know
B) Because shari'ah itself depends on faith, leading to circularity
C) Because the text does not mention it
D) Because Prophet ﷺ did not command it

Key Takeaway
Wujub al-iman is excluded from the definition of shar'i hukm because its dependence on Shari'ah would create circularity, yet its obligation still requires revelation.

The Three Meanings of Hukm and Which Is Intended in the Definition of Fiqh
Determining which meaning of hukm is intended in the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three meanings of hukm and determine which meaning is intended in the Hanafi definition of fiqh, applying the reasoning against tahsil al-hasil and redundancy.

Core Idea
Hukm in fiqh definition means customary relation, not divine address or logical judgment, or the definition collapses into circularity or redundancy.

This passage clarifies a foundational point in Hanafi usul: what does 'hukm' mean in the classic definition of fiqh? Without this precision, the definition becomes logically flawed. The author distinguishes three possible meanings and eliminates two, leaving only the customary sense. Understanding this analysis sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi scholars define their subject matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three meanings of hukm
List the three meanings: customary (ascribing one thing to another), terminological (Allah's address concerning actions), and logical (perception of a relation/tasdiq).
These are the standard categories in Hanafi usul for analyzing the term hukm.
2
Understand the logical meaning objection
If hukm means logical perception (tasdiq), then it becomes a type of knowledge. The definition of fiqh would then be 'knowledge of shari'ah sciences,' which is circular (tahsil al-hasil).
Tahsil al-hasil is a fallacy: acquiring what is already acquired.
3
Understand the terminological meaning objection
If hukm means Allah's address, then the restrictions 'shari'ah' and 'practical' in the definition would be redundant because the address is inherently shari'ah and connected to actions.
Redundancy makes the definition imprecise.
4
Conclude the intended meaning
The only meaning that avoids both objections is the customary meaning: a complete relation between two matters. This is what is intended in the definition of fiqh.
Customary hukm is a simple relation, not a divine command or logical judgment.
5
Note the implication for fiqh definition
The definition of fiqh now reads: 'knowledge of the practical shari'ah rulings derived from detailed evidences,' where 'rulings' (ahkam) refers to customary relations, not divine addresses.
This precision prevents misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم كے تين معانى آتے ہيں (1) عرفى (2) اصطلاحى (3) منطقى۔ عرفى معنى: اسناد امر الى امر آخر يعنى ايك امر كا دوسرے امر كى طرف نسبت كرنا۔ اصطلاحى معنى: اصطلاح اصوليين ميں حكم كا معنى ہے خطاب اللہ المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخيير۔ منطقى معنى: ادراك النسبة واقعة اوليست بواقعة يعنى دو امروں كے درميان نسبت كے وقوع يالا وقوع كے ادراك كا نام حكم ہے اور يہى ادراك تصديق كہلاتا ہے۔ يہاں حكم كا كونسا معنى مراد ہے؟ و هو ليس المراد ههنا: يہ شرح كى عبارت كا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ اس سے غرض شارح اس بات كى تعيين كرنا ہے كہ حكم كا كونسا معنى يہاں مراد ہے اور كونسا معنى مراد نہيں ہے۔ تو فرمايا كہ فقہ كى تعريف ميں حكم سے مراد منطقى معنى نہيں لے سكتے كيونكہ اس معنى ميں نسبت كے ادراك كو حكم كہا گيا ہے اور يہ ادراك تصديق ہے اور تصديق علم ہے تو حكم سے مراد علم ہوا۔ اب تعريف يہ ہوگى: الفقہ علم بالعلوم الشرعيہ كہ فقہ علوم شرعيہ كے علم كا نام ہے اور يہ درست نہيں كيونكہ اس صورت ميں تحصيل حاصل لازم آتا ہے۔ اور اصطلاحى معنى بھى مراد نہيں لے سكتے اس ليے كہ اگر اصطلاحى معنى مراد ليں تو تعريف ميں "الشرعيہ" اور "العمليہ" كى قيد كا تكرار ہوگا۔ وہ اس طرح كہ حكم سے مراد خطاب اللہ الخ ہے اور خطاب اللہ شرعى ہوتا ہے غير شرعى نہيں ہوتا تو حكم كے شرعى ہونے كى قيد يہيں سے سمجھ ميں آ رہى ہے۔ اس طرح خطاب اللہ المتعلق ميں افعال مكلفين كى قيد ہے اور افعال اور اعمال ايك ہى شے ہيں، لہذا عمليہ كى قيد بھى يہاں سے سمجھ ميں آگئى۔ تو جب دونوں قيديں حكم ميں ماخوذ ہيں تو مستقل طور پر ان كو دوبارہ ذكر كرنا محض تكرار ہے۔ لہذا يہ معنى بھى مراد نہيں لے سكتے۔ تو متعين ہو گيا كہ حكم سے مراد عرفى معنى ہے يعنى نسبت تامہ بين الامرين۔
Hukm has three meanings (1) customary (2) terminological (3) logical. Customary meaning: ascribing one matter to another, i.e., relating one matter to another. Terminological meaning: in the terminology of usuliyyin, the meaning of hukm is the address of Allah the Exalted connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons by way of requirement or option. Logical meaning: the perception of a relationship as actual or not actual; this perception is called tasdiq. Which meaning of hukm is intended here? 'And it is not intended here': this is the second part of the sharh's sentence. The commentator's purpose is to determine which meaning of hukm is intended here and which is not. He says: In the definition of fiqh, the logical meaning cannot be taken, because in that meaning perception of a relationship is called hukm, and this perception is tasdiq, and tasdiq is knowledge; thus hukm would mean knowledge. Then the definition would become: fiqh is knowledge of the shari'ah sciences, which is incorrect because it would lead to tahsil al-hasil (acquiring what is already acquired). The terminological meaning also cannot be taken because if it is taken, then the restrictions 'shari'ah-related' and 'practical' would be redundant. This is because hukm meaning the address of Allah etc. is inherently shari'ah, so the restriction 'shari'ah' is already understood. Similarly, the address of Allah connected to actions of the legally responsible persons includes the restriction of actions, so 'practical' is also understood. Thus, repeating both restrictions would be pure redundancy. Hence, that meaning cannot be intended. So it is determined that what is intended by hukm is the customary meaning, i.e., the complete relation between two matters.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a definitional analysis of the term 'hukm' (حكم) as it appears in the classical definition of fiqh. The author explains that 'hukm' has three distinct meanings: (1) customary (عرفي): simply ascribing one thing to another, (2) terminological (اصطلاحي) in usul al-fiqh: the address of Allah concerning the actions of the mukallafin by way of requirement or option, and (3) logical (منطقي): the perception of a relation (tasdiq). The purpose of the passage is to determine which of these is intended in the definition of fiqh. The commentator argues that the logical meaning is invalid because it would make fiqh a knowledge of other shari'ah sciences, which is circular (tahsil al-hasil). The terminological meaning is also invalid because the restrictions 'shari'ah' and 'practical' would be redundant: the first is inherent in 'address of Allah', and the second is inherent in 'actions of the mukallafin'. Thus, the only intended meaning is the customary one: a complete relation between two matters. This analysis is crucial for understanding the foundational definition of fiqh and exemplifies the precision of Hanafi usul al-fiqh methodology.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this passage, the author determines that 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh means the customary sense: a complete relation between two matters.
تصديق (tasdiq): The logical meaning of hukm: the perception of a relation as actual or not actual; equivalent to judgment.
تحصيل الحاصل (tahsil al-hasil): Acquiring what is already acquired; a logical fallacy that occurs if the definition of fiqh includes knowledge of knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the terminological meaning of hukm rejected in the definition of fiqh?
A) It is invalid because it leads to tahsil al-hasil.
B) It is invalid because the restrictions 'shari'ah' and 'practical' would be redundant.
C) It is invalid because it contradicts ijma.
D) It is invalid because it is not from the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The definition of fiqh uses hukm in its customary sense (a complete relation), not as divine address or logical judgment, to avoid logical fallacies and redundancy.

The Three Meanings of Hukm and Its Role in Defining Fiqh
Analyzing the three meanings of hukm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three meanings of hukm (linguistic, technical, logical) and justify why the linguistic meaning is the correct one in the definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
Hukm in fiqh definition means linguistic relation, not technical or logical, to avoid redundancy.

This passage from Sharh al-Talweeh unpacks the term 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh. The commentator identifies three distinct meanings, then eliminates two of them to focus on the linguistic meaning. Understanding this choice is crucial for grasping the precise definition of fiqh and avoiding tautology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three meanings of hukm
List the linguistic (ascribing one matter to another), technical (Allah's address related to actions of mukallafin by demand or choice), and logical (perception of occurrence/non-occurrence of a relation) meanings as defined in the passage.
The linguistic meaning is also called 'urfi, technical is 'istilahi, and logical is 'mantiqi.
2
Examine why the logical meaning is rejected
If 'hukm' meant logical perception (tasdiq), then fiqh would be knowledge of Shariah sciences, leading to tahsil al-hasil (acquisition of what is already obtained) — a redundancy.
3
Examine why the technical meaning is rejected
If 'hukm' meant the technical address, then the restrictions 'Shariah' and 'practical' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant, as they are already implied in the technical meaning.
4
Confirm the linguistic meaning as intended
The only remaining meaning is the linguistic one: a complete relation between two matters. This leads to the refined definition: fiqh is the affirmation (tasdiq) of practical Shariah propositions derived from detailed evidence.
This avoids redundancy and makes the definition precise.
5
Analyze the objections and responses
The commentator addresses two objections: (1) why 'propositions' (qadaya) instead of 'relation' (nisba) — answered as part-for-whole metonymy; (2) how the benefits of the restrictions are handled under both meanings of hukm — showing a subtle critique of the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح احكام الخ. يہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض: حکم کے تین معانی کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ حکم کے تین معانی آتے ہیں (۱) عرفی (۲) اصطلاحی (۳) منطقی۔ (1) عرفی معنی استاد امرالی امر آخر ایک امر کی دوسرے امر کی طرف نسبت کرنا۔ (۲) اصطلاحی معنی اصطلاح اصولیین میں حکم کا معنی ہے خطاب اللہ المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء أو التخيير۔ (۳) منطقی معنی اور اک ان النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة یعنی دو امروں کے درمیان نسبت کے وقوع یالا وقوع کے ادراک کا نام حکم ہے اور یہی اور اک تصدیق کہلاتا ہے۔
يہاں حکم کا کونسا معنی مراد ہے
وہوليس المراد هھنا : ۔ يہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس سے غرض شاریخ اس بات کی تعیین کرنا ہے کہ حکم کا کون سا معنی يہاں مراد ہے اور کون سا معنی مراد نہیں ہے تو فرماتے ہیں کہ کہ فقہ کی تعریف میں حکم سے مراد منطقی معنی نہیں لے سکتے کیونکہ اس معنی میں نسبت کے اور اک کو حکم کہا گیا ہے اور یہ اور اک تصدیق ہے اور تصدیق علم ہے تو حکم سے مراد علم ہوا اب تعریف یہ ہوگی الفقہ علم بعلوم الشرعيہ کہ فقہ علوم شرعيہ کے علم کا نام ہے اور یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ اس صورۃ میں تحصیل حاصل لازم آتا ہے اور اصطلاحی معنی بھی مراد نہیں لے سکتے اس لئے کہ اگر اصطلاحی معنی مراد لیں تو تعریف میں الشرعيہ اور العمليہ کی قید کا تکرار ہو گا وہ اس طرح کہ حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ الخ ہے اور خطاب اللہ شرعی ہوتا ہے غیر شرعی نہیں ہوتا تو حکم کے شرعی ہونے کی قيد يہیں سے سمجھ میں آرہی ہے اس طرح خطاب اللہ المتعلق میں افعال مکلفین کی قید ہے اور افعال اور اعمال ایک ہی شئی ہیں لہذا عمليہ کی قید بھی يہاں سے سمجھ میں آگئی تو جب دونوں قید میں الا حکام میں مأخوذ ہیں تو مستقل طور پر ان کو دوبارہ ذکر کرنا محض تکرار ہے لہذا يہ معنی بھی مبرا نہیں لے سکتے تو متعین ہو گیا کہ حکم سے مراد عرفی معنی ہے یعنی نسبت تامہ بین الأمرین تو تقدیر عبارت ہوگی الفقہ ہو العلم بالنسبہ اور نسبت تامہ کے علم کو تصدیق کہتے ہیں تو علم سے مراد تصدیق ہو گا لہذا اس سے تصورات خارج ہو جائیں گے تو اب تعریف کا خلاصہ يہ ہوا کہ الفقہ عبارة عن التصديق بالقضايا الشرعية العملية حاصل من الادلة التفصيلية التي نصبت في الشرع على تلك القضایا کہ وہ قضا یا شرعيہ جن کا تعلق کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ ہے ان قضایا کی تصدیق جوان أولر تفصیلیہ سے حاصل ہونے والی ہے جو شرع میں ان قضایا کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہے اس تصدیق کا نام فقہ ہے۔
اعتراض: حکم سے مراد آپ نے نسبت تامہ لی ہے تو تعریف کے خلاصہ میں بھی آپ کو التصدیق بالنسبہ کہنا چاہیئے تھا نا کہ التصديق بالقضايا ۔
جواب:۔ يہاں نسبت پر ہی قضایا کا اطلاق کیا گیا ہے اور یہ تسمیہ الجز باسم الکل کے قبیل سے ہے۔
اعتراض قضایا محکوم به أو محکوم عليه کے مجموعہ کا نام ہے حالانکہ نسبت وقوع ولا وقوع سے مراد وہ اجزاء ہوتے ہیں جو قضایا کے آخری اجزاء واقع ہوتے ہیں تو يہاں احکام کو قضایا کے ساتھ کیسے تعبیر کر دیا؟
جواب (۱):۔ یہ حذف مضاف کے قبیل سے ہے اصل میں تھا تصدیق احکام القضایا اور یہ احکام قضایا کے آخری جزء ( محکوم به ) واقع ہوتے ہیں۔
جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ ذکر قضایا کا ہے لیکن مراد اس سے آخری اجزاء (احکام) ہیں یعنی يہاں ذکر کل کا اور ارادہ جز کا ہے۔
وفوائد القیود ظاہر پر شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس کی غرض میں دو تقریریں ہیں (۱) سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال:۔ سائن نے فقہ کی تعریف میں کہا کہ حکم کے دو معنی مراد لئے جاسکتے ہیں اور پھر فوائد قیود بیان کرتے وقت دوسرے معنی (خطاب اللہ اتعلق الخ) کے مطابق تو مکمل فوائد قیود بیان کئے گئے ہیں لیکن پہلے معنی (اسناد امرالی امر آخر ) کے مطابق فوائد قیود بیان نہیں کئے ایسا کیوں کیا ؟
اب: پہلے معنی کے اعتبار سے فوائد قیود ظاہر تھے اس لئے ان کو بیان نہیں کیا لیکن عرض میں یہ تقریر بیان کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ مائن نے دونوں معنوں کے اعتبار سے فوائد قیود بیان کئے ہیں وہ اس طرح کہ پہلی دو قیدوں (احکام شرعیہ ) کے فوائد دونوں معنوں میں الگ الگ بیان کئے ہیں اور آخری دو قیود کے فوائد ا کٹھے بیان کر دئے کیونکہ ان دونوں سے خارج ہونے والی چیزیں دونوں معنوں کے اعتبار سے ایک ہی تھیں لہذا يہ تقریر درست نہیں بلکہ اس عبارت سے شاریخ کی غرض ماتن پر اعتراض کرتا ہے۔
Explanation of rulings etc. This is the first part of the commentary. Purpose: To explain the three meanings of hukm. The three meanings of hukm are: (1) Linguistic: ascribing one matter to another, i.e., relating one matter to another. (2) Technical: In the terminology of usul scholars, the meaning of hukm is 'the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible persons, requiring a command, prohibition, or option.' (3) Logical: The perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of a relation between two things; this is called tasdiq (affirmation).
Which meaning of hukm is intended here?
'And the intended here is not...' This is the second part of the commentary. The commentator's purpose is to determine which meaning of hukm is intended here and which is not. He says: In the definition of fiqh, the logical meaning cannot be intended because in that meaning, the perception of the relation is called hukm, and this perception is tasdiq, and tasdiq is knowledge. So hukm would mean knowledge, and the definition would become 'fiqh is knowledge of the Shariah sciences' — that is incorrect because it would entail the acquisition of what is already obtained (tahsil al-hasil). The technical meaning also cannot be intended because if we take the technical meaning, there would be repetition of the restrictions 'Shariah' and 'practical' in the definition. This is because hukm in the technical sense means 'the address of Allah' which is inherently Shariah, so the restriction of 'Shariah' is already understood. Similarly, 'related to the actions of the legally responsible persons' already implies 'practical'. So mentioning these restrictions separately would be redundant. Hence, this meaning also cannot be taken. Therefore, it is determined that the intended meaning is the linguistic meaning, i.e., the complete relation between two matters. So the definition would be: 'Fiqh is knowledge of the relation' — and knowledge of the complete relation is called tasdiq. Thus, by 'knowledge' tasdiq is meant, which excludes concepts (tasawwurat). So the summary of the definition is: 'Fiqh is the affirmation of the practical Shariah propositions derived from the detailed evidences that the Shariah has established for those propositions.' That is, the affirmation of those Shariah propositions that relate to the quality of actions, obtained from the detailed premises derived from the Shariah for those propositions, is called fiqh.
Objection: You took the meaning of hukm as the complete relation, so in the summary of the definition, you should have said 'the affirmation of the relation', not 'the affirmation of the propositions'.
Answer: Here, 'propositions' are applied to the relation, and this is of the type of naming the part with the name of the whole (tasmia al-juz' bi ism al-kull).
Objection: 'Propositions' is the name of the collection of the subject and predicate (mahkum bihi and mahkum alayh), whereas the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation refers to the final parts of the proposition. So how are the rulings expressed as propositions?
Answer (1): This is of the type of elision of the genitive (hazf al-mudaf). The original was 'affirmation of the rulings of the propositions', and these rulings are the final part (mahkum bihi) of the propositions.
Answer (2): It is that the mention of 'propositions' is made, but what is intended is the final parts (the rulings) — i.e., mentioning the whole and intending the part.
'And the benefits of the restrictions are apparent' is the third part of the commentary. Its purpose contains two expositions: (1) It is an answer to a hypothetical question. Question: The author (matn) said in the definition of fiqh that two meanings of hukm could be intended, and then when mentioning the benefits of the restrictions, he explained the benefits according to the second meaning (the address of Allah etc.) but did not explain the benefits according to the first meaning (ascribing one matter to another). Why?
Answer: According to the first meaning, the benefits of the restrictions were apparent, so he did not mention them. But this exposition is incorrect because the author did mention the benefits of the restrictions according to both meanings, as follows: For the first two restrictions (Shariah rulings), he mentioned their benefits separately according to both meanings, and for the last two restrictions, he mentioned their benefits together because the things excluded by them were the same according to both meanings. Hence, this exposition is incorrect. Rather, from this phrase, the commentator's purpose is to object to the author (matn).
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the definition of fiqh, specifically analyzing the term 'hukm' (حكم). The commentator begins by identifying three distinct meanings of 'hukm': linguistic (عرفي), technical/terminological (اصطلاحي), and logical (منطقي). The linguistic meaning is simple: relating one thing to another. The technical meaning, as used in usul al-fiqh, is 'the address of Allah connected to the actions of legally responsible persons, requiring either compliance or choice'. The logical meaning, common in philosophy, is the perception of whether a relation exists or not between two concepts — this is essentially what is called 'tasdiq' (affirmation/judgment). The core question is: which of these is meant when 'hukm' appears in the definition of fiqh? The commentator first excludes the logical meaning because it would reduce 'hukm' to mere knowledge, making the definition of fiqh 'knowledge of Shariah sciences', which would be redundant (tahsil al-hasil). Then he excludes the technical meaning because it would cause repetition of the restrictions 'Shariah' and 'practical' in the definition of fiqh — since the technical 'hukm' already implies both. Therefore, the intended meaning is the linguistic one: a complete relation between two matters. This leads to a refined definition: fiqh is the affirmation (tasdiq) of practical Shariah propositions derived from detailed evidence. The commentator then addresses an objection about the use of 'propositions' (qadaya) instead of 'relation' (nisba), explaining it as part-for-whole metonymy. Finally, he discusses the third part of the commentary regarding the benefits of the restrictions (fawa'id al-quyud), clarifying that the author actually accounted for both meanings of hukm when explaining the benefits, and the apparent discrepancy is actually a subtle critique by the commentator against the matn.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this passage, three meanings are given: (1) linguistic: ascribing one matter to another; (2) technical: Allah's address related to actions of mukallafeen by demand or choice; (3) logical: perception of occurrence or non-occurrence of a relation (tasdiq).
تصديق (tasdiq): Logical: affirmation or judgment that a relation exists or does not exist. It is the result of the logical meaning of hukm.
قضية (qadiyya (pl. qadaya)): A proposition consisting of subject and predicate; in the definition of fiqh, it refers to the practical Shariah rulings that are the content of affirmation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the logical meaning of 'hukm' not suitable for the definition of fiqh?
A) It leads to redundancy (tahsil al-hasil) because it would make fiqh merely knowledge of Shariah sciences.
B) It is too vague and not commonly used.
C) It would include non-Shariah matters.
D) It contradicts the linguistic meaning.

Key Takeaway
To avoid tautology and ensure precision, 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh must mean the linguistic relation (nisba) rather than the technical or logical meanings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh and Its Components
Definition of fiqh with linguistic objections and commentary on benefits of restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh, identify its key components (tasdiq, qadaya amaliyyah, adillah tafsiliyyah), and explain the linguistic objections and responses regarding the term qadaya.

Core Idea
Fiqh is verification of practical rulings from detailed evidence, not mere conceptual knowledge.

The Hanafi school defines fiqh as a specific type of knowledge: verification (tasdiq) of practical shari'ah propositions derived from detailed evidences. This lesson unpacks that definition, showing how each restriction excludes something else, and addresses subtle objections about the term 'qadaya' (propositions) in the definition. By understanding these nuances, you will grasp not only what fiqh is but also why the Hanafis structured their definition so carefully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentia
The definition starts with 'al-fiqh huwa al-ilm' (fiqh is knowledge). Identify the genus (ilm) and the restrictions that narrow it down to fiqh.
Knowledge here is specifically tasdiq (verification), not tasawwur (conception).
2
Analyze each restriction (qayd)
The passage mentions several restrictions: the knowledge must be of practical shari'ah propositions (qadaya shari'iyyah amaliyyah), derived from detailed evidences (adillah tafsiliyyah). Note what each restriction excludes.
For example, 'shari'iyyah' excludes rulings of reason; 'amaliyyah' excludes doctrinal beliefs.
3
Examine the objection about 'qadaya'
The first objection points out that since 'hukm' means the complete relation (nisbah), the definition should say 'al-tasdiq bi al-nisbah' not 'bi al-qadaya'. Understand the response that 'qadaya' is used metonymically for the relation.
This is a linguistic argument: part named after the whole (tasmīyah al-juz' bi-ism al-kull).
4
Address the second objection: whole-part relation
The second objection argues that 'qadaya' includes both subject and predicate, whereas the ruling is only the predicate. Two answers are given: omission of the genitive (hadhf mudāf) or mentioning the whole intending the part. Understand the difference.
Both answers resolve the tension between the comprehensive term and the intended specific component.
5
Evaluate the benefits of restrictions according to both meanings of hukm
The passage discusses why certain benefits were explained separately or together when considering the customary meaning vs the technical meaning of hukm. Note the commentator's objection to the author's approach.
The commentator argues that taking the technical meaning leads to complications; the customary meaning makes the benefits apparent.

الفقہ ھو العلم بالنسبہ اور نسبت تامہ کے علم کو تصدیق کہتے ہیں تو علم سے مراد تصدیق ہو گا لہذا اس سے تصورات خارج ہو جائیں گے تو اب تعریف کا خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ الفقہ عبارت عن التصدیق بالقضایا الشرعیۃ العملیۃ حاصل من الادلۃ التفصیلیۃ التی نصبت فی الشرع علی تلک القضایا کہ وہ قضا یا شرعیہ جن کا تعلق کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ ہے ان قضایا کی تصدیق جوان اولر تفصیلیہ سے حاصل ہونے والی ہے جو شرع میں ان قضایا کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہے اس تصدیق کا نام فقہ ہے۔ اعتراض: حکم سے مراد آپ نے نسبت تامہ لی ہے تو تعریف کے خلاصہ میں بھی آپ کو التصدیق بالنسبہ کہنا چاہیئے تھا نا کہ التصدیق بالقضایا ۔ جواب:۔ یہاں نسبت پر ہی قضایا کا اطلاق کیا گیا ہے اور یہ تسمیہ الجز باسم الکل کے قبیل سے ہے۔ اعتراض قضایا محکوم به او محکوم عالیہ کے مجموعہ کا نام ہے حالانکہ نسبت وقوع ولا وقوع سے مراد وہ اجزاء ہوتے ہیں جو قضایا کے آخری اجزاء واقع ہوتے ہیں تو یہاں احکام کو قضایا کے ساتھ کیسے تعبیر کر دیا؟ جواب (۱):۔ یہ حذف مضاف کے قبیل سے ہے اصل میں تھا تصدیق احکام القضایا اور یہ احکام قضایا کے آخری جزء ( محکوم بہ ) واقع ہوتے ہیں۔ جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ ذکر قضایا کا ہے لیکن مراد اس سے آخری اجزاء (احکام) ہیں یعنی یہاں ذکر کل کا اور ارادہ جز کا ہے۔ وفوائد القیود ظاہر پر شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس کی غرض میں دو تقریریں ہیں (۱) سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال:۔ سائن نے فقہ کی تعریف میں کہا کہ حکم کے دو معنی مراد لئے جاسکتے ہیں اور پھر فوائد قیود بیان کرتے وقت دوسرے معنی (خطاب اللہ اتعلق الخ) کے مطابق تو مکمل فوائد قیود بیان کئے گئے ہیں لیکن پہلے معنی (اسناد امرالی امر آخر ) کے مطابق فوائد قیود بیان نہیں کئے ایسا کیوں کیا ؟ اب: پہلے معنی کے اعتبار سے فوائد قیود ظاہر تھے اس لئے ان کو بیان نہیں کیا لیکن عرض میں یہ تقریر بیان کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ مائن نے دونوں معنوں کے اعتبار سے فوائد قیود بیان کئے ہیں وہ اس طرح کہ پہلی دو قیدوں (احکام شرعیہ ) کے فوائد دونوں معنوں میں الگ الگ بیان کئے ہیں اور آخری دو قیود کے فوائد ا کٹھے بیان کر دئے کیونکہ ان دونوں سے خارج ہونے والی چیزیں دونوں معنوں کے اعتبار سے ایک ہی تھیں لہذا یہ تقریر درست نہیں بلکہ اس عبارت سے شاریخ کی غرض ماتن پر اعتراض کرتا ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ ماتن نے کہا کہ تعریف میں حکم کے دو معنی مراد لینا ممکن ہے ایک تو اسناد امرالی امر آخر ، ، اور یہ عرفی معنی ہے اور دوسرا ہے خطاب اللہ الخ اور یہ اصطلاحی معنی ہے تو ماتن کا یہ کہنا درست نہیں کیونکہ حکم سے عرفی معنی تو مراد لینا درست ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں فوائد قیود ظاہر ہیں کہ ان میں کوئی تکلف نہیں کرنا پڑتا لیکن اصطلاحی معنی مراد لینا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں فوائد قیود ظاہر نہیں بلکہ ان میں بہت تکلف کرنا پڑتا ہے۔
Fiqh is knowledge of the relation. And the knowledge of the complete relation is called tasdiq. So by 'knowledge' is meant tasdiq; therefore, concepts (tasawwurat) are excluded. So now the summary of the definition is: fiqh is the verification (tasdiq) of the practical shari'ah propositions, obtained from the detailed evidences that are established in the Shari'ah for those propositions. That is, those shari'ah propositions that are related to the modality of action, the verification of those propositions obtained from the detailed primary evidences that are placed in the Shari'ah for those propositions — this verification is named fiqh. Objection: You have taken 'hukm' to mean the complete relation, so in the summary of the definition you should have said 'al-tasdiq bi al-nisbah' not 'al-tasdiq bi al-qadaya'. Answer: Here the term 'qadaya' is applied to the relation itself, and this is of the category of naming the part with the name of the whole. Objection: 'Qadaya' is the name for the totality of the subject and predicate, whereas the relation of occurrence and non-occurrence refers to those parts that are the ultimate parts of the propositions. So how are the rulings (ahkam) expressed as 'qadaya'? Answer (1): This is of the category of omission of the genitive (hadhf mudaf). Originally it was 'tasdiq ahkam al-qadaya', and these rulings are the ultimate part (predicate) of the propositions. Answer (2): It is that the mention is of 'qadaya' but the intention is the ultimate parts (the rulings), i.e., here the whole is mentioned and the part is intended. And 'Benefits of the restrictions apparently' is the third part of the commentary's expression. Its purpose contains two presentations: (1) It is the answer to an implied question. Question: The author said in the definition of fiqh that two meanings of 'hukm' can be taken, and then when explaining the benefits of the restrictions according to the second meaning (khitab Allah, etc.) he fully explained the benefits, but according to the first meaning (attributing one thing to another) he did not explain the benefits. Why is that? Answer: According to the first meaning, the benefits of the restrictions were apparent, so he did not explain them. But this presentation is not correct because the author explained the benefits of the restrictions according to both meanings in such a way that he separately explained the benefits of the first two restrictions (shari'ah rulings) in both meanings, and he explained the benefits of the last two restrictions together because the things excluded by both were the same in both meanings. Therefore, this presentation is not correct; rather, by this expression, the commentator intends to object to the author. Objection: The author said that in the definition, two meanings of 'hukm' can be taken: one is the attribution of one thing to another, and this is the customary meaning; the second is the address of Allah, etc., and this is the technical meaning. The author's statement is not correct because taking the customary meaning is correct because in that case the benefits of the restrictions are apparent, requiring no complication; but taking the technical meaning is not correct because in that case the benefits are not apparent but rather require much complication.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of fiqh. It begins by stating that fiqh is knowledge of the relation (nisbah), and that knowledge of the complete relation (nisbah tammah) is called tasdiq. Therefore, 'knowledge' in the definition refers to tasdiq, excluding tasawwurat (concepts). The summary of the definition is thus: fiqh is the tasdiq (verification) of practical shari'ah propositions (qadaya) derived from detailed evidences (adillah tafsiliyyah) established in the Shari'ah. The author then addresses two objections. The first objection points out that since 'hukm' was taken to mean the complete relation, the definition should use 'al-tasdiq bi al-nisbah' instead of 'al-tasdiq bi al-qadaya'. The reply is that the term 'qadaya' is applied to the relation here by way of naming the part after the whole. The second objection notes that 'qadaya' refers to a composite of subject and predicate, whereas the actual rulings are the predicates (the ultimate parts). The two answers given are: (1) it is an instance of omission of the genitive (hadhf mudaf), so the original was 'tasdiq ahkam al-qadaya'; (2) it is mentioning the whole while intending the part. This is followed by the third part of the commentary, which discusses the benefits of the restrictions (qayud) in the definition. The commentator raises and answers an implicit question about why the author did not explain the benefits according to the first meaning of hukm. The proposed answer that the benefits were apparent is rejected because the author actually did explain them according to both meanings, but combined the last two restrictions. The commentator then objects more directly, arguing that taking the technical meaning of hukm (khitab Allah) is problematic because it leads to complications in explaining the benefits of the restrictions.

Key Terms
الفقہ (al-fiqh): Tasdiq (verification) of practical shari'ah propositions derived from detailed evidences.
التصدیق (al-tasdiq): Knowledge that involves judgment (relative to occurrence or non-occurrence), as opposed to mere conception.
القضایا (al-qadaya): The total proposition including subject and predicate, but in this context it is used to refer to the rulings (predicates) specifically.
تسمیة الجزء باسم الکل (tasmīyah al-juz' bi-ism al-kull): A linguistic device where the part is named after the whole (synecdoche).
حذف مضاف (hadhf al-mudaf): Omission of the genitive (mudaf) in an idafa construction, with the remaining word standing for the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason for using 'qadaya' instead of 'nisbah' in the definition of fiqh?
A) The author made a mistake.
B) It is a case of naming the part after the whole (synecdoche).
C) The term 'nisbah' is not Arabic.
D) The definition must include both subject and predicate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh is precise: it is verification (tasdiq) of practical shari'ah propositions derived from detailed evidences, and each term in the definition serves to exclude extraneous matters.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Benefits of Restrictions in the Definition of Hukm
Explanation of benefits of restrictions in definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's classification of hukm into shar'i and non-shar'i, and state why the obligation of belief in God is considered non-shar'i to avoid circular reasoning (dawr).

Core Idea
The restriction 'al-shar'iyyah' excludes non-shar'i rulings like faith to prevent circular dependency.

In the definition of fiqh, the author introduced restrictions to clarify the scope of 'hukm'. The commentator here elucidates the benefits of those restrictions according to the second meaning of hukm (divine address). Understanding this classification helps distinguish between rulings that depend on Shari'ah and those that are prerequisites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's two categories of hukm
The author divided hukm (divine address) into two types: address that depends on Shari'ah (ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar') and address that does not. The first is shar'i, the second is non-shar'i.
This division is based on the concept of dependency on Shari'ah.
2
Understand the purpose of the restriction 'al-shar'iyyah'
By adding 'al-shar'iyyah' to the definition, non-shar'i rulings are excluded. This narrows the definition to only those rulings that are contingent upon Shari'ah.
The restriction is a qayd that specifies the category.
3
Analyze the examples given
Shar'i examples: obligation of prayer and fasting. Non-shar'i example: obligation of belief in God. The commentator explains why the latter is non-shar'i.
These examples illustrate the practical application of the classification.
4
Comprehend the circular dependency argument
If belief in God were a shar'i ruling, then Shari'ah would depend on it, and it would depend on Shari'ah, creating a vicious circle (dawr). Therefore, it must be non-shar'i.
Dawr is logically invalid (batil).

Explanation of the benefits of the restrictions according to the second meaning. And 'the author permitted intention' [perhaps a heading]. This is the fourth part of the commentary's expression. From here, the commentator, while explaining the benefits of the restrictions mentioned by the author according to the second meaning, clarifies the complications in it and says: In these benefits of the restrictions, the author has committed three complications (takallufat) and one arbitrariness (ta'assuf). Now first understand the explanation of the benefits of the restrictions, then understand the complications and arbitrariness in them. Benefits of the restrictions: The author said that 'hukm' has two types: address that depends on the Shari'ah, and address that does not depend on the Shari'ah. So the first is shar'i, the second is non-shar'i. When 'hukm' is taken to mean address, then both shar'i and non-shar'i rulings are included. Then by the restriction 'al-shar'iyyah', non-shar'i rulings are excluded. An example of a shar'i ruling is the obligation of prayer and the obligation of fasting, etc. An example of a non-shar'i ruling is the obligation of faith upon God and the obligation of confirming the Prophet. These two are non-shar'i because they do not depend on the Shari'ah; rather, the Shari'ah itself depends on believing in God's existence, knowledge, power, speech, etc., and on confirming the Prophet's prophethood and his miracles. So if we make this belief in God and confirmation of the Prophet themselves shar'i rulings, they would depend on the Shari'ah, which would necessitate the dependence of a thing upon itself (tawaqquf al-shay' 'ala nafsihi), in that the Shari'ah depends on the obligation of belief in God and confirmation of the Prophet, and if these obligations depend on the Shari'ah, then the Shari'ah would depend on the Shari'ah through the medium of the obligation of faith, which is a vicious circle (dawr). A circle is invalid. Therefore, the rulings of belief in God and confirmation of the Prophet are non-shar'i. The three complications: (1) The first complication is that the author divided 'hukm' (address of God) into two types: shar'i and non-shar'i. This is pure complication, because the address of God is only shar'i, it is not non-shar'i. (2) Then the author restricted the shar'i ruling to 'that which depends on the Shari'ah'. This is also a complication, because a shar'i ruling is defined as 'that which the address of the Lawgiver has come with', i.e., that which the Lawgiver's address has been issued upon, regardless of whether it depends on the Shari'ah or not.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is the fourth part of the commentary, where the commentator explains the benefits of the restrictions (qayud) in the definition of fiqh according to the second meaning of hukm (i.e., khitab Allah). The commentator states that the author has committed three unnecessary complications (takallufat) and one arbitrariness (ta'assuf) in explaining these benefits. He first explains the benefits themselves: The author divided hukm (here meaning divine address) into two categories: address that depends on the Shari'ah (ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar') and address that does not depend on the Shari'ah. The first is shar'i, the second is non-shar'i. By the restriction 'al-shar'iyyah' in the definition, the non-shar'i rulings are excluded. Examples: Shar'i rulings include the obligation of prayer and fasting. Non-shar'i rulings include the obligation of belief in God (iman billah) and confirmation of the Prophet (tasdiq bi al-nabi). These are non-shar'i because the Shari'ah itself depends on them—one must first believe in God and the Prophet before the Shari'ah can be established. If they were made shar'i, it would create a circular dependency (dawr). The commentator then lists the three complications: (1) The author's division of divine address into shar'i and non-shar'i is forced; divine address is always shar'i. (2) Defining shar'i ruling as 'that which depends on the Shari'ah' is also forced, because the proper definition is 'that which the Lawgiver's address has come with', regardless of dependency. The third complication is not fully given in the text but is implied.

Key Terms
الحکم الشرعی (al-hukm al-shar'i): A ruling that depends on the Shari'ah; or, according to the commentator, any ruling that the Lawgiver's address has come with.
دور (dawr): A vicious circle in reasoning, where A depends on B and B depends on A.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The restriction 'al-shar'iyyah' excludes non-shar'i rulings like faith to avoid logical circularity in the definition of hukm.

Three Complications in the Author's Definition
Critical evaluation of the author's definitional complications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the first two complications (takallufat) that the commentator raises against the author's definition of shar'i ruling, and evaluate the validity of the critique.

Core Idea
The author's division of divine address into shar'i and non-shar'i and his restriction are forced (takalluf).

The commentator argues that the author's definition of hukm and the associated restrictions contain unnecessary complications. The first two complications are that dividing divine address into shar'i and non-shar'i is artificial, and that defining shar'i ruling as 'that which depends on Shari'ah' is also a complication. The proper definition is 'that which the Lawgiver's address has come with'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first complication
The commentator says the author's division of divine address (khitab Allah) into shar'i and non-shar'i is pure takalluf (complication) because divine address is inherently shar'i; there is no non-shar'i divine address.
In Hanafi usul, khitab Allah is always legislative.
2
Understand the second complication
The author restricted shar'i ruling to 'that which depends on the Shari'ah'. The commentator argues that the correct definition is 'that which the Lawgiver's address has come with' (ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'), regardless of dependency.
This broader definition avoids the need to separate prerequisites.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind each complication
The commentator's critique is methodological: definitions should be straightforward and avoid forced conditions.
Takalluf is disapproved in usul (al-takalluf makruh).
4
Apply the critique to the benefit explanation
While the benefit of the restriction was to exclude non-shar'i rulings, the commentator argues that the very concept of non-shar'i divine address is problematic.
This shows that the author's framework itself is flawed.

The first is shar'i, the second is non-shar'i. By the restriction 'al-shar'iyyah' in the definition, the non-shar'i rulings are excluded. Examples: Shar'i rulings include the obligation of prayer and fasting. Non-shar'i rulings include the obligation of belief in God (iman billah) and confirmation of the Prophet (tasdiq bi al-nabi). These are non-shar'i because the Shari'ah itself depends on them—one must first believe in God and the Prophet before the Shari'ah can be established. If they were made shar'i, it would create a circular dependency (dawr). The commentator then lists the three complications: (1) The author's division of divine address into shar'i and non-shar'i is forced; divine address is always shar'i. (2) Defining shar'i ruling as 'that which depends on the Shari'ah' is also forced, because the proper definition is 'that which the Lawgiver's address has come with', regardless of dependency. The third complication is not fully given in the text but is implied.

Key Terms
تکلف (takalluf): An unnecessary complication or forced interpretation in a definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the commentator's main objection to the author's definition of shar'i ruling?
A) It is too broad
B) It includes non-shar'i rulings
C) It unnecessarily restricts the definition by adding a dependency condition
D) It relies on circular reasoning

Key Takeaway
The commentator's critique shows that definitions in usul should be straightforward and avoid forced conditions; the author's definition is methodologically flawed.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Critique of the Dual Meaning of Hukm
Critique of the matn's allowance of two meanings for hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible meanings of hukm in the matn and state why the commentator objects to the technical meaning.

Core Idea
The matn's definition fails because the technical meaning obscures the benefits of its restrictions.

The matn of Al-Tawdih defined hukm as the speech of Allah related to the actions of the obligated persons. However, the term hukm can have two meanings: a customary meaning (attribution of a command to another command) and a technical meaning (speech of Allah). The commentator objects that only the customary meaning makes the benefits of the definition's restrictions clear, while the technical meaning introduces forced interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's definition of hukm
Recall that the matn defines hukm as the speech of Allah (khitab Allah) related to the actions of the obligated persons. This is the base definition under scrutiny.
2
Recognize the two possible meanings of hukm
The commentator explains that hukm can be interpreted in two ways: (1) customary: the attribution of a command to another command; (2) technical: the speech of Allah. The matn intended both, but the commentator argues this is problematic.
3
Analyze the benefits of restrictions under each meaning
Under the customary meaning, the restrictions (e.g., 'Shariyyah', 'amaliyyah') produce clear benefits without difficulty. Under the technical meaning, the benefits are not apparent and require forced explanations (takalluf).
4
Understand the commentator's conclusion
Because the technical meaning leads to hidden difficulties, the matn's allowance of both meanings is unsound. Only the customary meaning should be relied upon for the definition to be effective.
