The Nature of Theoretical Shari'ah Rulings
Objection and response on whether theoretical rulings are shari'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi distinction between theoretical and practical shari'ah rulings and explain why the obligation of belief is not a shari'ah ruling according to the matn's position.

Core Idea
The Shari'ah depends on the essence of belief, not its obligation — avoiding circularity in defining shari'ah rulings.

In this passage, the commentator critiques the matn's exclusion of theoretical obligations like belief in God from shari'ah rulings. The core issue is whether a ruling that the Shari'ah depends upon can itself be called a shari'ah ruling. The Hanafi position distinguishes the essence of belief from its obligation, while Ash'aris insist on revelation as the source of all obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of shari'ah ruling and its two types
Find where the passage defines shari'ah ruling (ḥukm sharʿī) as that which depends on the Shari'ah. Note the two subtypes: theoretical (naẓarī) and practical (ʿamalī).
Theoretical rulers do not relate to the modality of action, e.g., 'ijma is a proof'.
2
Analyze the objection regarding the obligation of belief
The matn claimed the obligation to believe is not a shari'ah ruling because Shari'ah depends on it, not vice versa. The objector argues this leads to circularity only if Shari'ah depends on the obligation itself, but it actually depends on the essence of belief.
The objector distinguishes between nafs imān (essence of belief) and wujūb imān (obligation of belief).
3
Contrast the Hanafi and Ash'ari positions
The Hanafi matn holds that theoretical obligations like belief are prior to revelation and thus not shari'ah rulings. The Ash'ari position (mentioned in the passage) holds that all obligation comes through revelation (lā wujūba illā bi al-samʿ).
This is a key usul disagreement on the source of obligation.
4
Evaluate the matn's restriction to practical rulings
The passage notes that the matn's restriction (taqyīd) to practical is intended to exclude theoretical rulings from fiqh. However, if 'ruling' is taken in its technical sense (khitāb Allāh), it already excludes theoretical matters, making the restriction redundant.
This highlights the importance of istilah (technical terminology) in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the consequence for the definition of fiqh
Since fiqh is knowledge of practical shari'ah rulings, theoretical rulings are not part of fiqh. This shapes the scope of Hanafi fiqh as action-oriented.
The thamarah (practical fruit) is that fiqh does not cover purely doctrinal matters.

Source Text

بالنبی (۲) وجوب ایمان بالله و وجوب تصدیق بالنبی (۳) علم بوجوب ایمان باللہ وصفاتہ اور علم بوجوب تصدیق النبي ما اعتراض: ۔ ماتن نے وجوب ایمان اور وجوب تصدیق بالنبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کوحکم غیر شرعی کہا اس کی وجہ انہوں نے یہ بیان فرمائی کہ یہ شریعت پر موقوف نہیں ہیں کیونکہ اصل میں خود شریعت ان پر موقوف ہے اب اگر ان کو شریعت پر موقوف کر کے ان کو حکم شرعی کہیں تو اس سے دور لازم آئے گا تو ماتن کا اس کو ستلزم دور کہنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب ایمان وغیرہ کو حکم شرعی کہنے کی وجہ سے دور تو تب لازم آئے گا جب شریعت وجوب ایمان پر موقوف ہو حالانکہ شریعت (چاہے اس سے مراد خطاب اللہ لیا جائے یا شریعت النبی سے مراد لی جائے دونوں صورتوں میں ) وجوب ایمان پر موقوف نہیں ہے بلکہ شریعت تو نفس ایمان اور نفس تصدیق پر موقوف ہے اور نفس ایمان پر شریعت کے موقوف ہونے سے یہ ثابت ہوگا کہ شریعت نفس ایمان پر موقوف ہے اور وجوب ایمان شریعت پر موقوف ہے اور اس میں کوئی دور لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ شریعت کے موقوف ہونے کی جہت اور ہے اور موقوف علیہ ہونے کی جہت اور ہے حالانکہ دور اس وقت لازم آتا ہے جب جانبین سے توقف کی جہت ایک ہو تو جب یہاں دور لازم نہیں آرہا تو ماتن کا دور کو دلیل بنا کر یہ کہنا کہ وجوب ایمان شریعت پر موقوف نہیں درست نہیں ہے بلکہ وجوب ایمان پر نہیں در شریعت پر موقوف ہے جیسا کہ اشاعرہ کا کہنا ہے لا وجوب الا با سمع قَوْلُهُ ) ثُمَّ الشَّرْعِيُّ ( أَى الْمُتَوَقِّفُ عَلَى الشَّرْعِ إِمَّا نَظَرِيٌّ لَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِكَيْفِيَّةِ عَمَلٍ وَإِمَّا عَمَلِي يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا فَالتَّقْيِيدُ بِالْعَمَلِيَّةِ لِإِخْرَاجِ النَّظَرِيَّةِ كَكَونِ الْإِجْمَاعِ حُجَّةً ، وَهَذَا إِنَّمَا يَصِحُ عَلَى التَّقْدِيرِ الثَّانِى لَوْ كَانَ الْحُكْمُ الْمُصْطَلَحُ شَامِلا لِلنَّظَرِي ، وَفِيهِ كَلَامٌ سَيَجِيءُ . ترجمہ:۔ پھر شریعت پر موقوف ہونے والا حکم یا تو نظری ہوگا کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوگا یا عملی ہوگا کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگا پس عملیہ کی قید لگانا نظریہ کو نکالنے کے لئے ہے مثلاً اجتماع کا حجت ہونا اور یہ جزیں نیست درست ہوگا دوسری صورت پر اگر ہو حکم اصطلاحی شامل حکم نظری کو اور اس میں بحث ہے جو عنقریب آئے گی۔ تشریح ۔ غرض یہاں سے شاریخ ماتن کی عبارت کی وضاحت کرنے کے بعد اس پر اعتراض کر رہے ہیں۔ وضاحت: ماتن نے عملیہ کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ حکم شرعی کی دو قسمیں تھیں (۱) نظری جس کا تعلق کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ نہیں ہوتا (۲) عملی جس کا تعلق کیفیت عمل کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے عملیہ کی قید سے حکم شرعی نظری کو خارج کر دیا کیونکہ اس کے علم کا نام فقہ نہیں ہے۔ - و هدا انما صبح سے ماتن پر اعتراض ہے کہ یہ تقریر اس وقت درست ہے جب حکم سے عرفی معنی مراد لیا جائے لیکن جب حکم کا اصطلاحی معنی ( خطاب اللہ ) مراد لیا جائے تو پھر یہ تقریر اس صورت میں درست ہوسکتی ہے کہ حکم عملی اور نظری دونوں کو شامل ہو حالانکہ حکم (خطاب) صرف عملی کو شامل ہے نظری کو شامل نہیں ہے جیسا کہ آگے بھی آ رہا ہے لہذا عملیہ کی قید لگانا درست نہیں ہے۔
Regarding the Prophet (2) obligation of belief in Allah and obligation of affirming the Prophet (3) knowledge of obligation of belief in Allah and His attributes and knowledge of obligation of affirming the Prophet. Objection: The matn said that the obligation of belief and the obligation of affirming the Prophet, peace be upon him, are non-shari'ah rulings. The reason he gave is that they do not depend on the Shari'ah, because in reality the Shari'ah itself depends on them. Now if we make them depend on the Shari'ah and call them shari'ah rulings, then circularity would be required. The matn's saying that it requires circularity is not correct, because circularity from calling the obligation of belief etc. a shari'ah ruling would only be required when the Shari'ah depends on the obligation of belief, while the Shari'ah (whether by it is meant the address of Allah or the Shari'ah of the Prophet, in both cases) does not depend on the obligation of belief. Rather, the Shari'ah depends on the essence of belief and the essence of affirmation. And from the fact that the Shari'ah depends on the essence of belief, it is proven that the Shari'ah depends on the essence of belief, and the obligation of belief depends on the Shari'ah. And there is no circularity required, because the aspect of the Shari'ah depending is one, and the aspect of being depended upon is another. Since circularity is only required when the aspect of dependence is the same from both sides, so when no circularity is required here, the matn's statement that it requires circularity as a proof to say that the obligation of belief does not depend on the Shari'ah is not correct. Rather, the obligation of belief does not depend on the Shari'ah? No, it depends on the Shari'ah, as the Ash'aris say: 'No obligation except through revelation.' His statement: 'Then the shari'ah-related (ruling) i.e. that which depends on the Shari'ah; either theoretical, not related to the modality of an action, or practical, related to it. Thus restricting it to practical is to exclude theoretical rulings, such as that consensus is a proof. And this is only valid on the second consideration if the technical term 'ruling' included theoretical, and there is discussion about it that will come.' Translation: Then the ruling that depends on the Shari'ah is either theoretical, not related to the modality of an action, or practical, related to it. So the restriction to 'practical' is to exclude theoretical, e.g., that consensus is a proof. And this is only correct on the second interpretation if the technical ruling includes theoretical, and there is discussion about it that will come. Explanation: In short, from here the commentator is explaining the matn's expression and then objecting to it. Clarification: The matn placed the restriction 'practical' because there are two types of shari'ah rulings: (1) theoretical, which is not related to the modality of action, (2) practical, which is related to the modality of action. By the restriction to 'practical', he excluded the theoretical shari'ah ruling because knowledge of it is not called fiqh. And this (statement) from 'and this is only valid' is an objection to the matn, saying that this exposition is correct when 'ruling' is taken in its common meaning. But when the technical meaning of 'ruling' (the address of Allah) is taken, then this exposition can only be correct if the ruling includes both practical and theoretical. However, the ruling (address) only includes practical, not theoretical, as will come later. Therefore, the restriction to 'practical' is not correct.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is an objection to the matn (the original text) regarding the classification of rulings as shari'ah or non-shari'ah. The matn had stated that the obligation to believe in Allah and to affirm the Prophet are non-shari'ah rulings because they do not depend on the Shari'ah; in fact, the Shari'ah depends on them. The objector argues that this reasoning is flawed: circularity only arises if the Shari'ah depends on the obligation of belief, but actually the Shari'ah depends on the essence of belief itself, not on its obligation. Thus the obligation of belief can depend on the Shari'ah without circularity, as the Ash'aris hold. The passage then cites the matn's classification of shari'ah rulings into theoretical and practical, and the restriction to practical to exclude theoretical. The commentator explains that this restriction is correct only if 'ruling' is understood in its common sense. If taken in the technical sense (as the address of Allah), the restriction is problematic because the technical ruling excludes theoretical matters altogether. The passage thus refines the definition of shari'ah ruling and clarifies the Hanafi position on theoretical obligations.

Key Terms
حكم شرعي (ḥukm sharʿī): A ruling that depends on the Shari'ah, either theoretical (not related to action modality) or practical (related to action modality).
نظري (naẓarī): A type of shari'ah ruling that does not relate to the modality of an action, e.g., that consensus is a proof.
عملي (ʿamalī): A type of shari'ah ruling that relates to the modality of an action, e.g., prayer is obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason for restricting shari'ah rulings to 'practical'?
A) To exclude theoretical rulings because knowledge of them is not called fiqh.
B) Because all shari'ah rulings are practical.
C) Because theoretical rulings are not dependent on Shari'ah.
D) Because the matn was mistaken.

Key Takeaway
The definition of shari'ah ruling depends on its relation to the Shari'ah: something that the Shari'ah depends upon cannot itself be a shari'ah ruling in the technical sense.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Exclusion of the Muqallid’s Knowledge from Fiqh
Commentary defending the condition 'from detailed evidence' to exclude taqlid from fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the muqallid's knowledge is excluded from the Hanafi definition of fiqh, applying the condition that knowledge must be obtained directly from detailed evidence.

Core Idea
Fiqh requires direct derivation from detailed evidence; indirect knowledge through taqlid does not qualify.

The Hanafi definition of fiqh is precise: 'knowledge of practical legal rulings from their detailed evidence.' The phrase 'from their detailed evidence' is crucial. Without it, even a muqallid who knows the rulings would be considered a faqih. This lesson clarifies why the muqallid's knowledge falls short, as explained in the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its condition
Start with the full definition of fiqh: 'al-ilm bi al-ahkam al-shar'iyyah al-'amaliyyah min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah'. Focus on the condition 'min adillatiha'.
The condition is a restrictive clause that defines how the knowledge must be obtained.
2
Recognize the potential misreading
One might mistakenly think 'min adillatiha' qualifies 'al-ahkam' (the rulings), thereby including the muqallid since rulings are based on evidence.
This misreading would render the condition redundant because all rulings are from evidence.
3
Understand the correction
The commentary argues that 'min adillatiha' actually qualifies 'al-ilm' (knowledge). The evidence produces knowledge of the thing, not the thing itself. Moreover, the ruling (divine address) is eternal and cannot be 'obtained'.
This shifts the requirement: knowledge must be directly acquired from the evidence.
4
Apply the distinction to the muqallid
The muqallid's knowledge is based on the mujtahid's statement, not on his own examination (nazar) of the evidence. Therefore, it does not satisfy the condition of being 'from the evidence' directly.
The passage states: 'لم يحصل من النظر في الدليل' (it is not obtained from looking into the evidence).
5
Note the restriction to detailed evidence
The word 'tafṣīliyyah' excludes general knowledge like knowing obligation due to the presence of a cause (muqtada) or non-obligation due to a negator (nafi), without citing specific texts.
This further narrows fiqh to rulings derived from particular scriptural proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ مِنْ اَدِلْتِهَا ( أى العِلْمُ الْحَاصِلُ ) قَد يُتَوَهُمُ أَنْ قَوْلَهُ مِنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا مُتَعَلِّق بِالأحْكامِ وَحِينَئِذٍ لَا يَخْرُجُ عِلْمُ الْمُقَلّدِ ؛ لأنَّهُ عَلِمَ بِالْأَحْكَامِ الْحَاصِلَةِ عَنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عِلْمُ الْمُقَلّدِ حَاصِلا عَنِ الْأَدِلَّةِ فَدَفَعَ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بالعِلم لا بالأحكام إذِ الْحَاصِلُ مِنَ الدَّلِيلِ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالشَّيْء لَا الشَّيْء نَفْسُهُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ إذَا أُريدَ بِالْحُكْمِ الْخِطَابُ فَهُوَ قَدِيمٌ لَا يَحْصُلُ مِنْ شَيْءٍ ، وَمَعْنَى حُصُولِ العِلم مِنْ الدَّلِيل أَنَّهُ يَنظُرُ فِي الدَّلِيلِ فَيَعْلَمُ مِنْهُ الْحُكْمَ فَعِلْمُ الْمُقَلْدِ ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسْتَنِدًا إِلَى قَوْلِ الْمُجْتَهِدِ الْمُسْتَنِدِ إِلَى عِلْمِهِ الْمُسْتَنِدِ إِلَى دَلِيلِ الْحُكْمِ لَكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْصُلْ مِنَ النَّظَرِ فِي الدَّلِيلِ وَقَيَّدَ الْأَدِلَّةَ بِالتَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ ؛ لِأَنَّ الْعِلْمَ بِوُجُوبِ الشَّيْءِ بِوُجُودِ الْمُقْتَضِى أَوْ بِعَدَمِ وُجُوبِهِ لِوُجُودِ النَّافِي لَيْسَ مِنَ الْفِقْهِ .
His saying 'from its evidences' (i.e., the obtained knowledge). It might be imagined that his saying 'from its evidences' is connected to the rulings, and then the knowledge of the muqallid would not be excluded because he knows the rulings that have been obtained from their detailed evidences, even if the muqallid's knowledge is not obtained from the evidences. So he repelled that by [saying] that it is connected to the knowledge, not to the rulings, because that which is obtained from the evidence is the knowledge of the thing, not the thing itself; moreover, if by 'ruling' is meant the divine address, then it is eternal and is not obtained from anything. And the meaning of the obtaining of knowledge from the evidence is that he looks into the evidence and thereby knows the ruling. So the muqallid's knowledge, even if it is based on the statement of the mujtahid which is based on his knowledge which is based on the evidence of the ruling, still it is not obtained from looking into the evidence. And he restricted the evidences to detailed ones because knowledge of the obligation of a thing due to the existence of its requisite, or of its non-obligation due to the existence of the negator, is not from fiqh.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the definition of fiqh in the matn. The commentator addresses a potential misunderstanding: one might think the phrase 'min adillatiha' (from its evidences) modifies 'al-ahkam' (the rulings), which would include the muqallid's knowledge, since the muqallid knows rulings derived from detailed evidence. The commentator refutes this by clarifying that 'min adillatiha' actually modifies 'al-ilm' (the knowledge) that is obtained—an implied word. The knowledge obtained from evidence is the knowledge of the thing, not the thing itself. Moreover, if 'hukm' means the divine address (khitab Allah), it is eternal and cannot be 'obtained.' The process is: one examines the evidence and through it knows the ruling. The muqallid's knowledge, though ultimately traceable to evidence through the mujtahid's chain, does not come from his own examination of that evidence. Hence it is excluded. The restriction to detailed evidence excludes general knowledge like knowing that something is obligatory due to the presence of its cause or absent due to the presence of a negating factor, without reference to specific proof texts.

Key Terms
المقلد (al-muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid without having direct knowledge of the detailed evidence.
الأدلة التفصيلية (al-adillah al-tafṣīliyyah): Specific proof-texts from Quran and Sunnah from which rulings are derived directly.
الحكم الشرعي العملي (al-ḥukm al-sharʿī al-ʿamalī): A legal rule pertaining to actions of the mukallaf, as opposed to theoretical beliefs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of practical legal rulings from detailed evidence' exclude the muqallid's knowledge?
A) Because the muqallid does not know the rulings at all.
B) Because the muqallid's knowledge comes directly from the evidence itself.
C) Because the muqallid's knowledge comes from the mujtahid's statement and not from his own examination of the detailed evidence.
D) Because the muqallid's knowledge is limited only to theoretical rulings.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh requires direct personal derivation from detailed evidence; the muqallid's inherited knowledge, though correct, does not meet this standard.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The True Meaning of 'Obtaining Knowledge from Evidence' and the Exclusion of the Muqallid
Commentary clarifying two conditions in the definition of fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the muqallid's knowledge is not considered fiqh according to Hanafi usul, and distinguish between detailed evidence (tafsili) and total evidence (ijmali).

Core Idea
Fiqh requires direct reflection on detailed evidence; mere attribution through a mujtahid does not qualify.

In defining fiqh, Hanafi usul scholars insisted that knowledge must be obtained from evidence after personal reflection. This lesson unpacks a key objection: does the muqallid's knowledge, which traces back to evidence through the mujtahid, count as fiqh? The commentary answers with a sharp distinction that safeguards the integrity of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the objection: if 'al-hasil' is implied, the muqallid's knowledge is attributed to evidence through the mujtahid. According to the principle that the attributed-to of the attributed-to is the attributed-to, the muqallid's knowledge is ultimately from evidence. So why is it excluded?
The objection uses a transitivity argument.
2
Locate the Hanafi Response
The response reframes 'husool al-ilm min al-daleel' to require direct reflection (ghawr wa fikr) on the evidence. The mujtahid reflects; the muqallid does not. Hence, even if the source is the same, the mode of acquisition differs.
This is a qualitative distinction, not a chain-of-custody one.
3
Understand the Condition 'tafsiliyya'
The condition 'detailed evidence' excludes knowledge derived from total evidence – e.g., inferring non-existence from the presence of a preventer. Such inference is not based on a detailed examination of the evidence.
Total evidence (ijmali) gives a general ruling, not a specific case-based deduction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و معنی حصول العلم من الدلیل :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض: ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض ۔ اگر آپ الحاصل مقدر نکالیں پھر بھی اس قید سے مقلد کا علم خارج نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ پھر مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کاوہ علم جوادلہ سے حاصل ہو وہ فقہ ہے یعنی علم کی نسبت ادلہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے اور مقلد کا علم بھی ایسے ہی ہے کیونکہ مقلد کا علم منسوب ہوتا ہے مجتہد کے علم کی طرف اور اس کا علم حاصل ہوتا ہے ادلہ سے اور ضابطہ ہے کہ مئی کے منسوب الیہ کا منسوب الیہ بھی شئی کا منسوب الیہ ہوتا ہے لہذا جب مجتہد کا قول منسوب الیہ ہے۔ مقلد کے علم کے لئے اور مجتہد کے قول کے لئے منسوب الیہ اس کا علم ہے اور اس کے علم کے لئے منسوب الیہ ادلہ ہیں تو مقلد کے علم کا منسوب الیہ ادلہ ہوں گے تو مقلد کا علم بھی دو واسطوں سے ادلہ سے حاصل ہوالہذ ا مقلد کا علم من ادلتہا کی قید سے خارج نہ ہوا۔
جواب: علم کے دلیل سے حاصل ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کے بعد وہ علم حاصل ہوا ہو اور دلیل میں مجتہد تو غور و فکر کرتا ہے مقلد نہیں کرتا لہذا مقلد کا علم اگر چہ دو واسطوں سے دلیل سے ہی حاصل ہوا ہے لیکن مقلد نے دلیل میں غور و فکر نہیں کیا لہذا امن ادلتہا کی قید سے مقلد کا علم بھی خارج ہو گیا۔
و قید الا دلته با تفصیلیہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔
غرض: ماتن کی عبارت کی وضاحت کرنا ہے کہ تعریف میں اتفصیلیہ کی قید سے اس علم کو خارج کر دیا جو دلیل اجمالی سے حاصل ہو جیسے کسی شئی کے وجود پر اس کا مقتضی دلیل ہوتا ہے اور کسی شئی کے موجود نہ ہونے پر نانی کا پایا جانا دلیل ہوتا ہے تو اب اگر کسی شئی کے عدم وجود کا علم اس کے نانی سے حاصل ہو تو یہ علم فقہ نہیں ہو گا۔
And the meaning of obtaining knowledge from the evidence: This is the third part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: to answer an objection. Objection: If you assume 'al-hasil' as implied, then the knowledge of the muqallid is still not excluded by this condition, because then the meaning would be that the knowledge of practical legal rulings which is obtained from the evidence is fiqh, meaning knowledge is attributed to the evidence, and the muqallid's knowledge is also like that because the muqallid's knowledge is attributed to the mujtahid's knowledge, and that knowledge is obtained from the evidence, and the principle is that the 'attributed to' of the 'attributed to' is also the 'attributed to' of the thing. Therefore, when the mujtahid's statement is the 'attributed to' for the muqallid's knowledge, and for the mujtahid's statement the 'attributed to' is his knowledge, and for his knowledge the 'attributed to' is the evidence, then the muqallid's knowledge's 'attributed to' would be the evidence, so the muqallid's knowledge is also obtained from the evidence through two intermediaries; thus the muqallid's knowledge is not excluded by the condition of 'from its evidence'. Answer: The meaning of knowledge being obtained from the evidence is that the knowledge is obtained after reflection and pondering over the evidence. The mujtahid reflects on the evidence, but the muqallid does not. So even though the muqallid's knowledge is obtained from the evidence via two intermediaries, the muqallid did not reflect on the evidence, so his knowledge is excluded by the condition of 'from its evidence'. And the condition of 'its detailed evidence': This is the fourth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: to clarify the matn's expression, that in the definition, the condition of 'detailed' excludes that knowledge which is obtained from total evidence, such as the existence of a thing is evidenced by its requirement, and the non-existence of a thing is evidenced by the presence of a preventer. So if knowledge of the non-existence of something is obtained from its preventer, that knowledge is not fiqh.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of fiqh, specifically addressing the condition that fiqh is 'knowledge of practical legal rulings obtained from detailed evidence'. The commentary responds to an objection that if we take 'al-hasil' (the obtained) as implied, then the muqallid's knowledge would also be included because it is ultimately derived from evidence through the mujtahid. The answer distinguishes between immediate derivation after reflection (as done by the mujtahid) and derivative knowledge without reflection (as done by the muqallid). The muqallid does not reflect on the evidence himself, so his knowledge is excluded. The passage then explains the condition 'tafsiliyya' (detailed) which excludes knowledge obtained from total (ijmali) evidence, such as inferring non-existence from the presence of a preventer. The example illustrates that knowledge from a preventer is not considered detailed evidence.

Key Terms
حصول العلم من الدلیل (husool al-ilm min al-daleel): Knowledge obtained from evidence after reflection and contemplation, not merely by attribution or transmission.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid's ruling without knowledge of its evidence or without reflecting on it.
ادلہ تفصیلیہ (adilla tafsiliyya): Detailed evidence that specifies the ruling for a particular case, as opposed to total (ijmali) evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the main reason the muqallid's knowledge is excluded from the definition of fiqh?
A) The muqallid's knowledge is not from evidence at all.
B) The muqallid does not reflect directly on the evidence.
C) The muqallid follows a different madhhab.
D) The muqallid uses total evidence, not detailed.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is knowledge obtained by direct reflection on detailed evidence; the muqallid's derivative knowledge does not qualify.

Defining Hukm as Khitab Allah
Definition of hukm from al-Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ash'ari definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah' and identify its components using the legal definition dissector.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address — it encompasses all divine commands, prohibitions, and permissions.

This lesson introduces one of the most foundational terms in usul al-fiqh: al-hukm. The passage presents the definition transmitted from Imam al-Ash'ari, defining hukm as the very address of Allah. Understanding this definition is crucial because it sets the framework for how legal rulings are derived from divine revelation. As we break down this definition, you will learn to apply the legal definition dissector to any term in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition in the passage
Find the Arabic phrase 'wa al-hukmu qila khitabu Allahi ta'ala'. This is the core definition being introduced.
The phrase 'qila' indicates that this definition is attributed to a specific scholar (al-Ash'ari).
2
Identify the components of the definition
Break down 'khitab Allah ta'ala' into its constituent parts: 'khitab' (address), 'Allah' (the Speaker), and 'ta'ala' (exalted). Consider what each part includes.
The commentator notes that this definition encompasses all types of divine addresses.
3
Apply the legal definition dissector
Use the dissector tool to analyze 'hukm' as a legal term. Identify its sabab (cause: the divine address), shart (condition: the address must be from Allah), mani (preventer: absence of address or incapacity), and athar (effect: obligation, prohibition, etc.).
These components help clarify the scope and limitations of the term.
4
Contrast with the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school defines hukm as the speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah, not the address itself. Note how this subtle shift affects the ontological status of rulings. Be ready to identify this difference in the madhhab note.
This contrast is a key point of legitimate ikhtilaf in usul.

This definition is transmitted from al-Ash'ari. So his saying 'address of Allah ta'ala' encompasses all addresses.

Commentary
This passage is a brief section from a commentary on Al-Tawdih introducing the definition of 'hukm' (legal ruling) as a foundational term in usul al-fiqh. The author states that since fiqh is defined as knowledge of the sharia rulings, it is necessary to define both 'hukm' and 'shari'iyyah' (the quality of being sharia). The definition given is 'khitab Allah ta'ala' (the address of Allah), which is attributed to the Ash'ari school. The commentator notes that this definition includes all types of divine address (e.g., command, prohibition, permission). This is a standard definition in usul, though later scholars may refine it. The passage transitions from the previous discussion on the definition of fiqh to the definition of its components.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): The address of Allah ta'ala (خطاب الله تعالى) concerning the actions of the legally responsible individuals.
خطاب الله (khitab Allah): The divine address or communication from Allah, which includes commands, prohibitions, permissions, etc.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Definition of Hukm Shar'i and Its Two Types
Defining the term 'hukm' and explaining its divisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ash'ari definition of hukm shar'i, identify its components, explain the distinction between taklifi and wad'i rulings, and evaluate whether wad'i is a separate category.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address; it is not the resulting obligation but the divine command or permission itself.

In Usul al-Fiqh, the term 'hukm' is foundational. This lesson unpacks the definition transmitted from al-Ash'ari, clarifying that hukm is the divine address (khitab) that either demands (iqtida') or permits (takhyir) actions, and that it comes in two types: taklifi (obligatory/permissive) and wad'i (causal/conditional). Understanding this definition is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's components
Locate the Ash'ari definition: 'خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء أو التخيير'. Break it into five parts: (1) خطاب (address), (2) الله تعالى (of Allah), (3) المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين (relating to actions of the legally competent), (4) بالاقتضاء (by demand), (5) أو التخيير (or choice).
Demand includes obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and abomination; choice is permission.
2
Understand what is excluded
The definition excludes addresses that do not relate to actions of the mukallaf, such as stories (القصص), examples (الأمثال), and verses about Allah's attributes (like 'لا إله'). It also excludes verses like 'والله خلقكم وما تعملون' because they are not a demand or choice.
The phrase 'بالاقتضاء' is used to exclude such verses.
3
Analyze the two types of khitab
The passage divides khitab into: (i) taklifi – relating to actions by demand or choice, and (ii) wad'i – declaring something as cause (سبب) or condition (شرط) of another ruling. Example: sun's decline is a cause for prayer; purification is a condition.
Some scholars (like the author) insist wad'i is a separate type, not reducible to taklifi.
4
Examine the dispute on wad'i inclusion
Some later Ash'aris did not mention wad'i, arguing it is subsumed under demand because the meaning of 'cause' implies obligation. The author rebuts that the concept of wad'i (connection between two things) is distinct from demand, even if they coincide in some cases.
This debate shows the importance of precise conceptual boundaries in usul.
5
Distinguish between hukm as address and hukm as ruling
The passage notes that fuqaha often use 'hukm' for the resulting ruling (obligation, prohibition) metaphorically, whereas technically it is the address itself. This is like using 'creation' for the created.
Being aware of this terminological shift avoids confusion when reading fiqh texts.

Source Text

فَقُولُهُ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى يَسْمَلُ جَمِيعَ الخِطَابَاتِ . وَقَولُهُ ( المُتَعَلِّقُ بِأَفعَالِ المُكَلَّفِينَ يُخرِجُ مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ كَا الْقَصَصِ وَالْاَمْثَالِ وَالآيَاتِ أَىٰ الطَّلَبِ وَهُوَ إِمَّا طَلَبُ الفِعلِ جَازِمًا كَالإِيجَابِ أَو غَيْرَ جَازِمٍ كَالنُّدْبِ وَإِمَّا طَلَبُ التّركِ جَازِمًا كَالتَّحْرِيمِ أَو غَيْرَ جَازِمٍ كَالكَرَاهَةِ أَو التَّحْيِيرِ أَى الإِبَاحَةِ وَقَد زَادَ البَعضُ أو الوضع لِيَدخُلَ الحُكمُ بِالسَّبَبِيَّةِ وَالشَّرطِيَّةِ وَنَحوِهِمَا اعْلَم أَنَّ الخِطَابَ نَوعَانِ إِمَّا تَكلِيفِيٌّ وَهُوَ المُتَعَلِّقُ بِأَفعَالِ اصْطِلاحِيَّةٌ . ترجمہ:۔ جب تعریف کی گئی فقہ کی علم بالا حکام الشرعیہ کے ساتھ تو واجب ہوا حکم کی تعریف کرنا اور شرعیہ کی تعریف کرنا پس
And when fiqh was defined as knowledge of the sharia rulings, it became necessary to define 'hukm' and define 'sharia'. So he said: 'And al-hukm: it is said: the address of Allah the Exalted.' This definition is transmitted from al-Ash'ari. His statement 'address of Allah the Exalted' includes all addresses. And his statement (relating to the actions of the legally competent) excludes what is not like that, such as stories, examples, and verses relating to the attributes of Allah the Exalted, like His saying 'There is no god' [i.e., 'La ilaha'] then remains in the definition something like 'And Allah created you and what you make' even though it is not a ruling. So he excluded it by his statement 'by demand' which is request. And it is either a request for action, decisive like obligation, or non-decisive like recommendation; or a request for abandonment, decisive like prohibition, or non-decisive like abomination; or choice, i.e., permission. And some added 'or situational' to include rulings of causality, conditionality, and the like. Know that address is two types: either taklifi (obligatory) which relates to actions of the legally competent by demand or choice; or wad'i (situational) which is the address that this is a cause of that or a condition of it, like the decline of the sun is a cause for prayer and purification is a condition for it. So when one of the two types was mentioned, which is the taklifi, it became necessary to mention the other type, which is the wad'i. And some did not mention the wad'i because it is included in demand or choice, because the meaning of the decline of the sun being a cause for prayer is that when the decline occurs, prayer becomes obligatory at that time, and obligation is from the category of demand. But the correct is the first, because the concept understood from wad'i ruling is the connection of one thing to another, and the concept understood from taklifi ruling is not this, and the necessity of one for the other in a form does not indicate their unity in kind. (And some of them defined sharia ruling as this) i.e., some later followers of al-Ash'ari said: the sharia ruling is the address of Allah the Exalted; thus al-hukm according to this is the attribution of one thing to another. And the jurists use it for what is established by the address, like obligation and prohibition, metaphorically, by way of applying the name of the infinitive to the object, like 'creation' for the created, but when it became widespread in it, it became a transmitted terminological usage, and it is a terminological reality. Translation: When fiqh was defined as knowledge of sharia rulings, it became necessary to define hukm and to define sharia, then...
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage provides the Ash'ari definition of hukm sharia: it is Allah's address (khitab Allah) that pertains to the actions of the legally competent (mukallafin) by way of demand (iqtida') or choice (takhyir). The definition excludes other types of address like stories or verses about Allah's attributes. It also discusses whether the wad'i (situational) category should be included separately. Some argue wad'i rulings (like cause and condition) are subsumed under taklifi, but the author insists they are distinct types. The passage also explains that in Usul al-Fiqh, 'hukm' is the address itself, while jurists often use it metaphorically for the resulting ruling (obligation, prohibition). The lesson is foundational for understanding the nature of legal rulings in the Hanafi-Ash'ari tradition.

Key Terms
الحکم (al-hukm): Allah's address (khitab) relating to the actions of the legally competent, by demand or choice.
خطاب (khitab): The speech or address of Allah that contains a legal instruction.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand or request; a mode of address that requires an action or abandonment.
التخيير (al-takhyir): Choice or permission; the address that leaves the mukallaf free to act or not (mubah).
الحکم التکلیفی (al-hukm al-taklifi): A ruling that demands or permits an action, creating a direct legal obligation or choice.
الحکم الوضعی (al-hukm al-wad'i): A ruling that establishes a thing as a cause, condition, or preventer (mani') of another ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Address of Allah
B) Relating to actions of the legally competent
C) By demand or choice
D) Including stories and examples

Key Takeaway
Hukm shar'i is Allah's address that demands or permits an action of the legally competent, and it is divided into taklifi (demand or choice) and wad'i (cause, condition, preventer).

The Hanafi Definition of Hukm Shar'i
Explaining and expanding the definition of hukm shar'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i and distinguish between taklifi and wad'i rulings by identifying the qualifiers and their exclusions.

Core Idea
Hukm shar'i is Allah's address concerning actions, divided into direct demands (taklifi) and declarative connections (wad'i).

In this passage, the author unpacks the classical definition of hukm shar'i by examining each qualifier. You will learn what is excluded by 'related to actions of the legally responsible' and 'by requirement', and why Hanafis insist on a separate category of wad'i rulings. This distinction is foundational for understanding how rulings are derived and classified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its core definition
Extract the definition: 'The address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible by requirement or choice.' Note that this definition includes both imperative and permissive demands.
The phrase 'by requirement' (bi al-iqtida') is key—it demands or gives a choice.
2
Analyze the qualifier 'related to actions of the mukallaf'
This qualifier excludes stories, examples, and verses about Allah's attributes from being hukm. Such verses do not address actions with a demand.
Example: 'There is no god' (la ilaha) is not a hukm because it is a declaration, not a command or permission.
3
Analyze the qualifier 'by requirement' (bi al-iqtida')
This further excludes informative statements like 'And Allah created you and what you do'. The address must involve a demand (imperative or prohibitive) or choice.
This qualifier ensures that only normative addresses—not mere information—are considered hukm.
4
Distinguish between taklifi and wad'i rulings
Taklifi rulings are direct demands or choices (obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, permissibility). Wad'i rulings declare something as a cause, condition, or preventer for another ruling, e.g., the declination of the sun as a cause for prayer.
Hanafis maintain that wad'i is a distinct type, despite some scholars subsuming it under taklifi.

وَقَولُهُ ( المُتَعَلِّقُ بِأَفعَالِ المُكَلَّفِينَ يُخرِجُ مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ كَا الْقَصَصِ وَالْاَمْثَالِ وَالآيَاتِ الْمُتَعَلَّقَةِ بِصِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى كَقَوْلِهِ لَا إِلَهَ فَبَقِيَ فِي الحَدِّ نَحوُ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُم وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ مَعَ أَنَّهُ لَيسَ بِحُكُمْ فَأَخْرَجَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ بِالِاقْتِضَاءِ أَىٰ الطَّلَبِ وَهُوَ إِمَّا طَلَبُ الفِعلِ جَازِمًا كَالإِيجَابِ أَو غَيْرَ جَازِمٍ كَالنُّدْبِ وَإِمَّا طَلَبُ التّركِ جَازِمًا كَالتَّحْرِيمِ أَو غَيْرَ جَازِمٍ كَالكَرَاهَةِ أَو التَّحْيِيرِ أَى الإِبَاحَةِ وَقَد زَادَ البَعضُ أو الوضع لِيَدخُلَ الحُكمُ بِالسَّبَبِيَّةِ وَالشَّرطِيَّةِ وَنَحوِهِمَا اعْلَم أَنَّ الخِطَابَ نَوعَانِ إِمَّا تَكلِيفِيٌّ وَهُوَ المُتَعَلِّقُ بِأَفعَالِ المُكَلَّفِينَ بِالِاقْتِضَاءِ أَو التَّحْيِيرِ وَإِمَّا وَضَعِيٌّ وَهُوَ الخِطَابُ بِأَنَّ هَذَا سَبَبُ ذَلِكَ أَو شَرطُهُ كَالدُّلُوكِ سَبَبٌ لِلصَّلَاةِ وَالطَّهَارَةٌ شَرطْلَهَا فَلَمَّا ذَكَرَ أحَدَ النُّوعَينِ وَهُوَ التَّكْلِيفِيُّ وَجَبَ ذِكرُ النوع الآخَرِ وَهُوَ الوَضْعِيُّ وَالبَعضُ لَم يَذكُر الوَضِعِيَّ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ دَاخِلٌ فِي الْاقْتِصَاءِ أو التخيير ؛ لأنَّ المَعنَى مِن كون الدُّلُوكِ سَبَبًا لِلصَّلَاةِ أَنَّهُ إِذَا وُجِدَ الدُّلُوك وَجَبَتْ الصَّلاةُ حِينَيدِ وَالوُجُوبُ مِن بَاب الاقتصاءِ لَكِنَّ الحَقَّ هُوَ الأوَّلُ ؛ لأنَّ المفهوم مِن الحُكمِ الوَضِعِي تَعَلُّقُ شَيءٍ بِشَيْءٍ آخَرَ وَالمَفهُومُ مِن الحُكمِ التَّكلِيفِى لَيسَ هَذَا وَلُزُومُ أَحَدِهِمَا لِلآخَرِ فِي صُورَةٍ لَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى اتِّحَادِهِمَا نَوعًا (وَبَعضُهُم قَد عَرَّفَ الحُكمَ الشَّرعِيَّ بِهَذَا ) أى بَعضُ المُتَأَخْرِينَ مِن مُتَابِعِي الأشعَرِى قَالُوا الحُكمُ الشَّرعِيُّ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَالحُكمُ عَلَى هَذَا إِسْنَادُ أَمرٍ إلَى آخَرَ وَالفُقَهَاءُ يُطلِقُونَهُ عَلَى مَا ثَبَتَ بِالخِطَابِ كَالوُجُوبِ وَالحُرمَةِ مَجَازًا) بِطَرِيقِ إطلاقِ اسمِ المَصَدَرِ عَلَى المَفعُول كَالخَلقِ عَلَى المَخلُوقِ لَكِن لَمَّا شَاعَ فِيهِ صَارَ مَنقُولًا اصْطِلَاحِيًّا وَهُوَ حَقِيقَةٌ اصْطِلَاحِيَّةٌ .
And his statement (related to the actions of the legally responsible) excludes what is not like that, such as stories, examples, and verses related to the attributes of Allah Most High, like His saying 'There is no god' (la ilaha). So there remains in the definition something like 'And Allah created you and what you do' while it is not a ruling; so he excluded it by his statement 'by requirement' meaning request. And it is either a request for action decisively like obligation, or non-decisively like recommendation; or a request for leaving action decisively like prohibition, or non-decisively like dislike; or making equal i.e. permissibility. And some added the word 'or stipulation' to include the ruling by causality, conditionality, and the like. Know that the address is of two types: either taklifi, which is related to the actions of the legally responsible by requirement or making equal; or wad'i, which is the address that this is a cause for that or a condition for it, like the declination of the sun is a cause for prayer and purification is a condition for it. So when he mentioned one type, namely taklifi, it was necessary to mention the other type, namely wad'i. And some did not mention wad'i because it is included in requirement or making equal; because the meaning of the declination being a cause for prayer is that when declination occurs, prayer becomes obligatory at that time, and obligation is from the category of requirement. But the truth is the first, because the concept of wad'i ruling is the connection of one thing to another, and the concept of taklifi ruling is not this; and the necessity of one of them for the other in one form does not indicate their unity in type. And some of them have defined hukm shar'i with this, i.e. some later followers of al-Ash'ari said: hukm shar'i is the address of Allah Most High. So hukm according to this is the attribution of one thing to another. And the fuqaha apply it to what is established by the address, like obligation and prohibition, metaphorically, by way of applying the name of the infinitive to the object, like 'creation' applied to the created. But when it became widespread in that, it became a technical transferred term, and it is a technical reality.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the definition of hukm shar'i (legal ruling) within the Hanafi usul tradition. It begins by explaining the qualifier 'related to the actions of the legally responsible' in the definition, which excludes topics like stories and verses about Allah's attributes. It then clarifies the term 'by requirement' (bi al-iqtida'), meaning a demand, which encompasses five categories: obligatory (jāzim), recommended (mandūb), prohibited (ḥarām), disliked (makrūh), and permissible (mubāḥ). Some scholars added 'or stipulation' (aw al-waḍ‘) to include wad‘ī rulings (causes, conditions, preventers). The text distinguishes between taklīfī rulings (direct demands or choices) and waḍ‘ī rulings (declaring a thing as cause or condition). It presents the argument that waḍ‘ī rulings are subsumed under taklīfī because they entail obligation, but refutes this, asserting their conceptual distinctness. Finally, it notes that later Ash‘arī scholars define hukm shar‘ī as the address itself, while Hanafi jurists use it for the result (e.g., obligation) metaphorically, though it has become a technical reality.

Key Terms
الحكم التكليفي (al-hukm al-taklifi): The address that requires or gives a choice concerning an action of the legally responsible
الحكم الوضعي (al-hukm al-wad'i): The address that declares something as a cause, condition, or preventer for another ruling
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand or requirement, which includes both imperative and prohibitive demands

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition presented, what does the term 'by requirement' (bi al-iqtida') in the definition of hukm shar'i exclude?
A) Stories and examples from the Quran
B) The permissibility (ibaha) category
C) Wad'i rulings like causality
D) The address concerning attributes of Allah

Key Takeaway
Hukm shar'i is defined as Allah's address concerning actions by demand or choice, and it encompasses both taklifi (direct rulings) and wad'i (causal/conditional rulings), which are distinct categories in Hanafi usul.

Ash'ari Definition of Hukm and Its Components
Defines hukm with exclusion of non-demand speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ash'ari definition of hukm, identify the three components, and explain which types of divine speech are excluded by each component.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address with demand or option – stories and attributes are out.

This lesson examines the definition of hukm (legal ruling) as formulated by Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The Ash'ari definition is widely cited in usul al-fiqh and serves as a foundation for understanding how rulings are derived from divine speech. By analyzing each component of the definition, we will see what is included and excluded, and why the distinction between taklifi and wadi rulings matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components
The definition has three key parts: 'address of Allah', 'related to actions of the mukallaf', and 'with demand or option'. Understand what each part means.
2
Analyze what each component excludes
The first excludes non-divine speech; the second excludes verses about Allah's attributes and stories; the third excludes informative statements that do not command or permit.
Each component narrows the scope of hukm.
3
Consider the addition of wadi rulings
Some scholars add 'al-wad' (declaratory) to include causality and conditionality. Examine the argument for and against this addition.
This is a point of ikhtilaf among usulis.
4
Evaluate the preferred position
The commentator states that the correct view is to keep taklifi and wadi separate because their meanings differ. Assess the reasoning: entailment does not imply unity.
This shows the precision required in usul definitions.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرمایا اور حکم کے بارہ میں بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ وہ خطاب اللہ تعالى المتعلق با فعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخیر ہے ) یہ تعریف منقول ہے ابوالحسن اشعری سے پس اس کا قول خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ یہ شامل ہے تمام خطابات کو اور اس کا قول المتعلق با فعال المکلفین نکال دیتا ہے اس کو جو اس طرح نہ ہو جیسا کہ قصص ہیں اور مثالیں ہیں اور وہ آیات ہیں کہ جن کا تعلق اللہ کی صفات کے ساتھ ہے جیسا کہ قول خدا تعالی ہے لاالہ الا ہو، پس باقی رہ گیا حد حکم میں واللہ خلقكم و ماتعملون کی مثل ا خودیکہ یہ حکم نہیں ہے پس خارج کیا اس کی مثل کو اپنے اس قول ، بالاقتضاء اوالتخیر، کے ساتھ یعنی طلب کے ساتھ اور وہ (طلب) یا تو فعل کو طلب کرنا ہوگا۔ یقینا مثل ایجاب کے یا غیر یقینی طور پر جیسے نذب اور یا ترک فعل کو طلب کیا جائے یقینی قطعی طور پر جیسے تحریم یا غیر یقینی طور پر جیسے کراہت یا تخیر یعنی اباحت کے ساتھ اور تحقیق زیادہ کیا ہے بعض حضرات نے او الوضع کی قید کو تا کہ داخل ہو جائے سببیت اور شرطیت اور ان دونوں کی مثل کو تو جان لے کہ بیشک شریعت کا خطاب یا تو تکلیفی ہوتا ہے اور وہ ۔ جو متعلق ہو مکلفین کے افعال کے ساتھ اقتضاء یا تخیر کے ساتھ اور یا وضعی ہوتا ہے اور وہ خطاب ہے اس بات کا کہ یہ شئی اس شئی کا سبب ہے یا اس کی شرط ہے جیسا کہ دلوک نماز کا سبب ہے اور طہارت نماز کی شرط ہے پس جب ذکر کیا دونوں میں سے ایک کو اور وہ تکلیفی ہے تو واجب ہے یہ کہ ذکر کرتے دوسری نوع کو بھی اور وہ وضعی ہے اور بعض حضرات نے نہیں ذکر کیا وضعی کی قید کو کیونکہ وہ ( وضعی ) داخل ہے اقتضاء او التخیر میں کیونکہ معنی دلوک کے نماز کے لئے سبب ہونے کا یہ ہے کہ جب پایا جائے گا دلوک تو نماز واجب ہوگی اس وقت اور وجوب اقتضاء کے باب سے ہے لیکن حق بات وہ اول ہے کیونکہ حکم وضعی کا مفہوم تعلق شئی بھی آخر، ہے اور مفہوم حکم تکلیفی کا یہ نہیں ہے اور لازم آ جانا ان دونوں میں سے ایک قسم کا دوسری قسم کو کسی ایک صورت میں یہ نہیں دلالت کرتا ان دونوں کے متحد ہونے پر ۔
He said: Regarding hukm, some people have said that it is the address of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of the legally responsible persons with demand or option. This definition is transmitted from Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. So his saying 'address of Allah the Exalted' includes all addresses. And his saying 'related to the actions of the legally responsible persons' excludes that which is not like that, such as stories and examples, and those verses that relate to the attributes of Allah, like His saying 'there is no deity but Him'. So that which remains in the definition is like 'And Allah created you and what you do' – it is not a ruling, so he excluded its like by his saying 'with demand or option', i.e., with request. And that (request) either is a request for an action – definitely like obligation, or non-definitely like recommendation, or a request for leaving an action – definitely like prohibition, or non-definitely like dislike, or option i.e., permissibility. And some people added the condition of 'al-wad' (declaratory) to include causality and conditionality and their likes. So know that the address of Sharia is either taklifi (obligatory) which is related to the actions of the legally responsible with demand or option, or wadi (declaratory) which is the address that such thing is a cause for such thing or a condition for it, like the declining of the sun is a cause for prayer, and purity is a condition for prayer. So when one of the two types is mentioned, and it is the taklifi, it is necessary to mention the other type which is wadi. And some people did not mention the condition of wadi because it is included in demand and option, because the meaning of the declining being a cause for prayer is that when the declining occurs, prayer becomes obligatory at that time, and obligation is from the category of demand. But the correct statement is the first, because the meaning of wadi ruling is the relation of a thing to another, and the meaning of taklifi ruling is not that. And the entailment of one type to the other in one form does not indicate their unity.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage defines the Ash'ari definition of hukm (ruling) as the address of Allah concerning the actions of the legally responsible (mukallaf) with a demand (iqtida') or option (takhyir). The commentator breaks down each part: 'address of Allah' excludes non-divine speech; 'related to actions of the legally responsible' excludes verses about Allah's attributes or stories; 'with demand or option' excludes informative verses like 'Allah created you...' which are not commands or permissions. The demand can be for an action (obligatory or recommended) or for abandonment (prohibited or disliked), and option is permissibility. Some scholars add a condition of wadi (declaratory) rulings like causality and conditionality to include them in the definition. The author prefers to keep them separate because the meaning of wadi is different from taklifi. This shows the precision in defining the subject matter of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
الخطاب (al-khitab): The address from Allah to the mukallaf; includes all types of divine speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari definition, which of the following is an example of hukm?
A) 'Allah created you and what you do'
B) 'There is no deity but Him'
C) 'Establish prayer'
D) The story of Prophet Musa

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari definition precisely delimits hukm to divine addresses that command, forbid, or permit actions of the legally responsible, excluding informative and descriptive verses.

Hanafi Definition of Hukm: Ma Thabata Bil-Khitab
Presents the Hanafi definition and contrast with Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm as 'ma thabata bil-khitab' and explain how it differs from the Ash'ari definition, using the analysis of qayd (restrictions).

Core Idea
Hukm for the Hanafis is the legal effect established by the divine address, not the address itself.

In this lesson, we dive into the Hanafi definition of hukm (legal ruling). The fuqaha define hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), such as obligation and prohibition. This contrasts with the Ash'ari view that identifies hukm directly with the divine address. We will analyze the restrictions in the Ash'ari definition and see why the Hanafi definition is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key definitions
Locate the three definitions of hukm mentioned: the Ash'ari definition (khitab Allah), the absolute hukm definition (isnad amr ila amr), and the fuqaha definition (ma thabata bil-khitab).
The fuqaha definition is the Hanafi one.
2
Analyze the Ash'ari definition's restrictions
Examine how the Ash'ari definition uses qayd (restrictions) like 'related to actions of the legally responsible' and 'with demand or option' to narrow the scope. Understand what each restriction excludes.
Notice that stories and proverbs are excluded by the first restriction, and informative verses by the second.
3
Understand the Hanafi refutation
The Hanafis argue that the Ash'ari definition leads to redundancy if it is considered the definition of hukm shar'i, because the restriction 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh would be superfluous. Hence, the Ash'ari definition must be for absolute hukm, not hukm shar'i.
This is a logical argument based on consistency.
4
Grasp the Hanafi definition
The fuqaha define hukm as 'what is established by the address'. This means the ruling (e.g., obligation) is the effect, not the address itself. The word 'hukm' is applied metaphorically (majaz) but became a conventional term (naql).
The example: 'khalaqa' (creation) is applied to the created object.

اور ان کے بعض نے تعریف کی ہے حکم شرعی کی اس کے ساتھ یعنی اشعری کے متبعین میں سے بعض متاخرین نے کہا ہے کہ حکم شرعی نام ہے خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ الخ کا پس حکم اس قول کے مطابق اسناد امرالی امر آخر کا نام ہوگا (اور فقہاء اطلاق کرتے ہیں اس حکم کا اس چیز پر جو ثابت ہو خطاب کے ساتھ، جیسا کہ وجوب ہے اور حرمت ہے یہ اطلاق مجاز ا ہے ) یعنی اسم مصدر کا مفعول پر اطلاق کرنے کے قبیل سے ہے جیسا کہ خلق کا اطلاق مخلوق پر کیا جاتا ہے لیکن جب وہ (حکم ) مشہور ہو گیا اس ( ما شبت بالخطاب میں ) تو ہو گیا وہ حکم منقول اصطلاحی اور وہی حقیقت اصطلاحیہ ہے۔

فقال والحکم قیل:۔ یہاں سے علم کی تعریف بیان کی ہے اور ماتن نے دراصل علم کی تین تعریفیں ذکر کی ہیں دوا شاعرہ کے حوالہ سے اور ایک فقہاء کے حوالہ سے یہاں سے حکم کی تعریف کی ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم کی یہ تعریف کی ہے خطاب اللہ تعالى المتعلق با فعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخیر اور آگے جا کر بعضہم عرف الحکم سے دوسری تعریف کی ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ جو تعریف کی گئی ہے یہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے اس حکم کی تعریف نہیں ہے جو فقہ کی تعریف میں ماخوذ ہے یعنی حکم مطلق کی تعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ حکم مطلق کی تعریف یہ ہے اسناد امرالی امر آخر ایک امر کا دوسرے امر کی طرف اسناد کرنا لیکن پہلے والے بعض اشاعرہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر یہ تعریف (خطاب اللہ الخ ) حکم شرعی کی ہو تو فقہ کی تعریف میں الشرعیہ،، کی قید زائد ہوگی لہذا یہ تعریف حکم مطلق کی ہی ہے اس کے بعد و الفقہاء سے تیسری تعریف ذکر کی ہے کہ فقہاء نے حکم کی تعریف یوں فرمائی ہے ما ثبت بالخطاب، کہ جو چیز خطاب سے ثابت ہو وہ حکم ہے جیسے وجوب اور حرمت وغیرہ نفس خطاب کا نام حکم نہیں ہے اب مکمل تفصیل ہذا التعريف منقول الخ سے فوائد قیود کا ذکر ہے خطاب اللہ میں جو لفظ خطاب ہے یہ تمام خطابات کو شامل ہے جب خطاب کی نسبت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف ہوئی تو خطاب اللہ کے علاوہ تمام خطابات خارج ہو گئے پھر المتعلق با فعال المكلفين کی قید سے وہ خطابات خارج ہو گئے جن کا تعلق افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ نہیں ہے جیسے فقص اور ضرب المثل وغیرہ کہ یہ ابند تعالیٰ کے خطاب تو ہیں لیکن ان کا تعلق مکلفین کے افعال کے ساتھ نہیں ہے لیکن اس قید کے باوجود اس میں ایسے خطابات داخل تھے جو حکم نہیں ہیں جیسے اللہ خلفكم و ماتعملون، تو ایسے خطابات کو حکم سے خارج کرنے کے لئے بالاقتضاء اوالخجیر کی قید لگائی کیونکہ اقتضاء سے مراد طلب ہے اور تخیر سے مرادا باحت ہے اور اللہ خلقکم و ماتعملون جیسے خطابات میں نہ طلب ہے اور نہ ہی اباحت ہے بلکہ یہ اخبار کے قبیل سے ہیں تو یہ تعریف سے خارج ہو گئے ۔
و ہوا ما طلب الفعل: اقتضاء کی پانچ قسموں کو ذکر کیا ہے جن کی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ طلب دو حال سے خالی نہیں فعل کی طلب ہوگی یا ترک فعل کی فعل کی طلب ہو تو اس کے ترک سے منع کیا گیا ہو گا یا نہیں اول واجب اور ثانی مندوب ہے اور اگر ترک فعل کی طلب ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے کہ اس فعل سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا نہیں ثانی مکروہ تنزیہی ہے اور اول دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ اس کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے ہوگا یا دلیل ظنی سے اول ہے تو حرام ہے ثانی ہے تو مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔
And some of them defined hukm shari'i with it – i.e., some later followers of Ash'ari said that hukm shari'i is the name for the address of Allah the Exalted, etc. So according to this statement, hukm would be the name for the attribution of one thing to another. (And the fuqaha apply the word hukm to that which is established by the address, like obligation and prohibition. This application is metaphorical, i.e., from the category of applying the verbal noun to its object, just as 'creation' is applied to the created. But when it became well-known in the sense of 'what is established by the address', it became a transferred customary term, and that is the conventional reality.)
Explanation: 'And when he defined fiqh...' From here, the author (matn) explains the connection of the phrase with what preceded. Previously there was the definition of fiqh which included the restrictions of 'ahkam' and 'shar'iyya', so after the definition, it was necessary to clarify these restrictions. Hence the author now clarifies the restrictions of 'ahkam' and 'shar'iyya'.
Definitions of hukm
253
So he said: 'And hukm, it was said:' From here, the author has explained the definition of 'ilm (knowledge). Actually, the author mentioned three definitions of 'ilm: two with reference to some Ash'aris and one with reference to the fuqaha. From here, he defines hukm: Some Ash'aris defined hukm as 'the address of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of the legally responsible with demand or option'. And later, from 'some of them defined hukm', he gives a second definition: Some Ash'aris say that this definition is the definition of hukm shar'i, not the definition of the hukm that is taken in the definition of fiqh – i.e., it is not the definition of absolute hukm. Rather, the definition of absolute hukm is 'the attribution of one thing to another'. But the former some Ash'aris say that if this definition (address of Allah) is for hukm shar'i, then the restriction 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. Hence this definition is for absolute hukm. After that, from 'and the fuqaha', he mentions the third definition: The fuqaha defined hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab). That which is established by the address is hukm, like obligation and prohibition. The address itself is not called hukm. Now the complete detail: From 'this definition is transmitted' etc., the benefits of the restrictions are mentioned. The word 'khitab' in 'khitab Allah' includes all addresses. When the address is attributed to Allah, all addresses besides the address of Allah are excluded. Then the restriction 'related to the actions of the legally responsible' excludes those addresses that are not related to the actions of the legally responsible, like stories and proverbs – these are indeed addresses of Allah, but they are not related to the actions of the legally responsible. But despite this restriction, there remain addresses that are not rulings, such as 'Allah created you and what you do'. So to exclude such addresses, the restriction 'with demand or option' was added, because 'demand' means request and 'option' means permissibility. In addresses like 'Allah created you and what you do', there is neither demand nor permissibility; rather, they belong to the category of information. So they are excluded from the definition.
And 'what is a request for an action': He mentioned the five types of iqtida'. The reason for this enumeration is that request is either for an action or for leaving an action. If it is for an action, then either its abandonment is prohibited or not. The first is obligatory, the second is recommended. If it is for leaving an action, then either the action itself is prohibited or not. The second is mildly disliked, and the first is either established by a definitive proof (haram) or by a probable proof (prohibitively disliked).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on definitions of hukm, now focusing on the Hanafi (fuqaha) definition and the debate among Ash'aris. The author explains that later Ash'aris distinguish between 'hukm shar'i' and 'absolute hukm', with the latter being the attribution of one thing to another. The fuqaha (Hanafis) define hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), such as obligation and prohibition, not the address itself. This usage is metaphorical originally but became conventional. The commentator then revisits the Ash'ari definition, analyzing each restriction and showing how it narrows the meaning. Finally, he enumerates the five types of iqtida' (demand): obligatory, recommended, prohibited, prohibitively disliked, and mildly disliked. This breakdown is crucial for understanding the categories of hukm taklifi.

Key Terms
ما ثبت بالخطاب (ma thabata bil-khitab): What is established by the address – the Hanafi definition of hukm, meaning the legal effect (e.g., obligation) rather than the address itself.
خطاب اللہ (khitab Allah): The divine address; the words of Allah (Quran and Sunnah as revelation).
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand or request; a key component in the Ash'ari definition to exclude informative verses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is considered hukm?
A) The verse 'Establish prayer' itself
B) The obligation of prayer established by that verse
C) The address 'There is no deity but Him'
D) The story of Prophet Musa in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm as 'ma thabata bil-khitab' is foundational for understanding the nature of legal rulings in the Hanafi school.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Five Types of Demand (Iqtida') in Hanafi Usul
Classifies the five types of demand (iqtida') in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and distinguish the five categories of iqtida' (demand/request) in Hanafi usul, and classify any given ruling into one of these categories based on the nature of request and the strength of evidence.

Core Idea
The five types of demand (iqtida') form the basis of taklifi rulings: obligatory, recommended, prohibited, prohibitively disliked, and mildly disliked.

In this lesson, we examine the five divisions of iqtida' mentioned by the author. Iqtida' refers to the demand aspect within the divine address. The author breaks down demand into five types: obligatory (wajib), recommended (mandub), prohibited (haram), prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), and mildly disliked (makruh tanzihi). Understanding these categories is essential for applying rulings to actions and for distinguishing between levels of obligation and prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the primary division
Note that demand (iqtida') is first divided into two kinds: demand for an action (talab al-fi'l) and demand for leaving an action (talab al-tark). This binary forms the root of the classification.
2
Subdivide demand for action
For demand for an action, there are two possibilities: either the abandonment of the action is prohibited, or it is not. If abandonment is prohibited, it is obligatory (wajib). If not, it is recommended (mandub).
This shows that the strength of the demand depends on the prohibition of its opposite.
3
Subdivide demand for leaving an action
For demand for leaving an action, there are two subcategories: either the action itself is prohibited or it is not. If prohibited, the prohibition is further split based on evidence strength: definitive evidence (qat'i) gives haram; probable evidence (zanni) gives makruh tahrimi. If the action is not prohibited, the ruling is makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked).
This is a unique Hanafi contribution: not all prohibitions are haram; some are makruh tahrimi.
4
Memorize the five categories
Synthesize the previous steps into a clear list: (1) Wajib, (2) Mandub, (3) Haram, (4) Makruh Tahrimi, (5) Makruh Tanzihi. Understand the conditions for each.
The text explicitly mentions these five.

Definitions of hukm
253
So he said: 'And hukm, it was said:' From here, the author has explained the definition of 'ilm (knowledge). Actually, the author mentioned three definitions of 'ilm: two with reference to some Ash'aris and one with reference to the fuqaha. From here, he defines hukm: Some Ash'aris defined hukm as 'the address of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of the legally responsible with demand or option'. And later, from 'some of them defined hukm', he gives a second definition: Some Ash'aris say that this definition is the definition of hukm shar'i, not the definition of the hukm that is taken in the definition of fiqh – i.e., it is not the definition of absolute hukm. Rather, the definition of absolute hukm is 'the attribution of one thing to another'. But the former some Ash'aris say that if this definition (address of Allah) is for hukm shar'i, then the restriction 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. Hence this definition is for absolute hukm. After that, from 'and the fuqaha', he mentions the third definition: The fuqaha defined hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab). That which is established by the address is hukm, like obligation and prohibition. The address itself is not called hukm. Now the complete detail: From 'this definition is transmitted' etc., the benefits of the restrictions are mentioned. The word 'khitab' in 'khitab Allah' includes all addresses. When the address is attributed to Allah, all addresses besides the address of Allah are excluded. Then the restriction 'related to the actions of the legally responsible' excludes those addresses that are not related to the actions of the legally responsible, like stories and proverbs – these are indeed addresses of Allah, but they are not related to the actions of the legally responsible. But despite this restriction, there remain addresses that are not rulings, such as 'Allah created you and what you do'. So to exclude such addresses, the restriction 'with demand or option' was added, because 'demand' means request and 'option' means permissibility. In addresses like 'Allah created you and what you do', there is neither demand nor permissibility; rather, they belong to the category of information. So they are excluded from the definition.
And 'what is a request for an action': He mentioned the five types of iqtida'. The reason for this enumeration is that request is either for an action or for leaving an action. If it is for an action, then either its abandonment is prohibited or not. The first is obligatory, the second is recommended. If it is for leaving an action, then either the action itself is prohibited or not. The second is mildly disliked, and the first is either established by a definitive proof (haram) or by a probable proof (prohibitively disliked).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on definitions of hukm, now focusing on the Hanafi (fuqaha) definition and the debate among Ash'aris. The author explains that later Ash'aris distinguish between 'hukm shar'i' and 'absolute hukm', with the latter being the attribution of one thing to another. The fuqaha (Hanafis) define hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), such as obligation and prohibition, not the address itself. This usage is metaphorical originally but became conventional. The commentator then revisits the Ash'ari definition, analyzing each restriction and showing how it narrows the meaning. Finally, he enumerates the five types of iqtida' (demand): obligatory, recommended, prohibited, prohibitively disliked, and mildly disliked. This breakdown is crucial for understanding the categories of hukm taklifi.

Key Terms
اقتضاء (iqtida'): Demand or request within a divine address; the basis for taklifi rulings.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory; an action whose performance is demanded and whose abandonment is prohibited.
مندوب (mandub): Recommended; an action whose performance is demanded but whose abandonment is not prohibited.
حرام (haram): Prohibited; an action whose abandonment is demanded and whose performance is prohibited by definitive evidence.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): Prohibitively disliked; an action whose abandonment is demanded and whose performance is prohibited by probable evidence.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): Mildly disliked; an action whose abandonment is demanded but whose performance is not prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A demand for leaving an action, where the action itself is prohibited by a probable proof, yields which ruling?
A) Haram
B) Makruh Tahrimi
C) Makruh Tanzihi
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi five-type classification of iqtida' provides a precise framework for categorizing legal rulings based on the nature of the demand and the strength of evidence.

The Ash'ari Definition of Hukm: Divine Address and Its Conditions
Defining hukm and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the Ash'ari definition of hukm and explain how each condition excludes certain addresses from being rulings.

Core Idea
Hukm is divine address linked to actions by demand or choice—excluding mere information.

This lesson unpacks the formal definition of hukm (ruling) as presented by some Ash'ari theologians. Understanding this definition is crucial because it establishes the fundamental criteria for what constitutes a legal ruling in contrast to mere informative statements. We will dissect each part of the definition and see how it filters out addresses that do not impose any legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining elements
The definition has three key parts: 'address of God,' 'connected to actions of the mukallaf,' and 'by demand or choice.' You must recognise each part and its role.
Memorise the Arabic: خطاب الله المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء أو التخير
2
Determine what 'address of God' excludes
This part excludes all addresses that are not from God, such as human commands or historical narratives. Only divine speech can constitute a hukm.
3
Analyse the effect of 'connected to actions'
This excludes divine addresses that do not relate to human actions, e.g., verses about creation or stories of past nations. These are not rulings because they do not direct behaviour.
Example: "God created you and what you do" is informative, not a ruling.
4
Understand the function of 'by demand or choice'
This final condition excludes even action-related addresses that lack demand or permission. Only addresses that command, prohibit, or permit constitute rulings. Informative statements are therefore excluded.
Demand (iqtida') can be for the act or its abandonment; choice (takhyir) results in mubah.

Source Text

و ہوا ما طلب الفعل: اقتضاء کی پانچ قسموں کو ذکر کیا ہے جن کی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ طلب دو حال سے خالی نہیں فعل کی طلب ہوگی یا ترک فعل کی فعل کی طلب ہو تو اس کے ترک سے منع کیا گیا ہو گا یا نہیں اول واجب اور ثانی مندوب ہے اور اگر ترک فعل کی طلب ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے کہ اس فعل سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا نہیں ثانی مکروہ تنزیہی ہے اور اول دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ اس کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے ہوگا یا دلیل ظنی سے اول ہے تو حرام ہے ثانی ہے تو مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔
He said: 'And the ruling is said to be...' From here, the definition of knowledge is explained. The author (may God have mercy on him) mentioned three definitions of knowledge from two Ash'aris and one from the jurists. Here he defines ruling: some Ash'aris defined ruling as 'The address of God Almighty connected to the actions of the morally responsible, by demand or choice.' And later, with 'some defined ruling as shari'i', a second definition: some Ash'aris say this definition is of shari'i ruling, not the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh, i.e., not absolute ruling; rather, absolute ruling is the attribution of one matter to another. But the former Ash'aris say if this definition were for shari'i ruling, then the qualification 'shari'i' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. Hence this definition is for absolute ruling. Then he mentions a third definition from the jurists: they defined ruling as 'what is established by address'—that the thing established by address is ruling, like obligation and prohibition; the address itself is not called ruling. Now the complete detail of the benefits of the conditions from 'this definition transmitted' etc. The word 'address' in 'address of God' includes all addresses. When address is attributed to God, all addresses other than God's are excluded. Then the condition 'connected to the actions of the morally responsible' excludes those addresses not connected to actions, like narratives and parables—these are God's addresses but not connected to actions. But even with this condition, some addresses that are not rulings are included, like 'God created you and what you do'—so to exclude such addresses, the condition 'by demand or choice' is added, because demand means request and choice means permission. In addresses like 'God created you and what you do', there is neither request nor permission; rather, they are of the type of information, so they are excluded from the definition.
And it is what requests the act: He mentioned the five types of iqtida'. The reason for the encompassing is that request is either for the act or for abandoning the act. If it is for the act, either its abandonment is prohibited or not: first is obligatory, second is recommended. If it is for abandoning the act, either the act is prohibited or not: second is makruh tanzihi, and the first (prohibition) is either proven by definitive evidence—then it is haram—or by presumptive evidence—then it is makruh tahrimi.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the definition of hukm (ruling) in Usul al-Fiqh. The author first presents the definition held by some Ash'ari theologians: 'The address of God Almighty connected to the actions of the morally responsible, by demand or choice.' He then notes a disagreement among the Ash'aris: some consider this the definition of absolute hukm (applicable to both taklifi and wad'i), while others restrict it to shari'i hukm and define absolute hukm differently (as attribution of one matter to another). The text explains that if the definition were only for shari'i hukm, the qualification 'shari'i' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. The commentary then details the conditions of this definition: 'address of God' excludes all other addresses; 'connected to actions' excludes narratives and parables; 'by demand or choice' excludes informative statements. Finally, the text breaks down iqtida' (demand) into five categories: wajib (obligatory) when the act is demanded and its abandonment is prohibited; mandub (recommended) when the act is demanded but abandonment is not prohibited; haram (prohibited) when abandonment is demanded and the act is prohibited by definitive evidence; makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) when prohibition is by presumptive evidence; and makruh tanzihi (disliked) when abandonment is demanded without a prohibition of the act. This division is fundamental to understanding the five ahkam taklifiyya in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand or request; includes both demand to do and demand to leave.
التخير (al-takhyir): Choice or permission; results in mubah (permissible) when there is no demand.
الحكم (al-hukm): The legal classification (e.g., wajib, haram) that results from divine address.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari definition in this passage, which condition excludes the verse 'God created you and what you do' from being a hukm?
A) The verse is not a divine address.
B) The verse is not connected to actions of the mukallaf.
C) The verse lacks demand or choice.
D) The verse is not attributed to God.

Key Takeaway
A hukm in the Ash'ari sense is a divine address that directly commands, prohibits, or permits human actions; mere information is not a ruling.

The Five Categories of Iqtida': Demand and Its Types
Classifying iqtida' into five rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any demand (iqtida') into one of the five categories (wajib, mandub, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) based on whether the demand is for the act or its abandonment, and the strength of evidence.

Core Idea
Demand to do or leave yields five rulings: wajib, mandub, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage, which breaks down the concept of iqtida' (demand) into five distinct categories. These categories are the building blocks of the ahkam taklifiyya (obligatory rulings) in Hanafi fiqh. By understanding the logic behind this division, you will be able to systematically determine the legal status of any command or prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Determine if the demand is for the act or its abandonment
Iqtida' is either a demand to perform an act or a demand to abstain from it. This is the first branching point.
2
If demand is for the act: check if abandonment is prohibited
If the demand is to do something, and the text also prohibits abandoning it, then the action is wajib (obligatory). If there is no such prohibition, it is mandub (recommended).
Example: 'Establish prayer' is wajib because abandonment is prohibited; 'perform optional night prayer' is mandub.
3
If demand is for abandonment: check if the act is prohibited
If the demand is to leave something, and the text prohibits doing it, then the act is prohibited. Otherwise, it is merely makruh tanzihi.
Example: 'Do not commit zina' prohibits the act.
4
If the act is prohibited, examine the evidence strength
A prohibition proven by definitive evidence (qat'i) results in haram. A prohibition proven by presumptive evidence (zanni) results in makruh tahrimi.
Definitive evidence: Quran mutawatir; presumptive: ahad hadith.
5
If demand for abandonment but act not prohibited: it is makruh tanzihi
This is when there is a request to leave an act, but the act itself is not prohibited. This is a disliked but not sinful act.
Example: eating raw garlic before mosque is makruh tanzihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
