Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the definition of hukm (ruling) in Usul al-Fiqh. The author first presents the definition held by some Ash'ari theologians: 'The address of God Almighty connected to the actions of the morally responsible, by demand or choice.' He then notes a disagreement among the Ash'aris: some consider this the definition of absolute hukm (applicable to both taklifi and wad'i), while others restrict it to shari'i hukm and define absolute hukm differently (as attribution of one matter to another). Key Terms
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand or request; the passage divides it into five categories.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation: demand for the act with prohibition of its abandonment.
الندب (al-nadb): Recommendation: demand for the act without prohibition of abandonment.
التحريم (al-tahrim): Prohibition: demand for abandonment of the act with definitive evidence.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyya): Prohibitive dislike: demand for abandonment of the act with presumptive evidence.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyya): Dislike: demand for abandonment without actual prohibition of the act.

Key Takeaway
The five ahkam taklifiyya (wajib, mandub, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) are derived from the logical analysis of iqtida' (demand) and the strength of the evidence for prohibitions.

Including Declaratory Rulings in the Definition of Hukm
Debate on adding 'or declaratory' to the definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul requires explicitly including wad'i rulings in the definition of hukm and evaluate the opposing Ash'ari argument of implicit inclusion.

Core Idea
Wad'i rulings have a distinct legal essence (talluq al-shay'i bil-shay'i) and cannot be subsumed under taklifi iqtida' without express mention.

One of the foundational debates in usul al-fiqh concerns the precise definition of hukm shari'. This passage examines whether the phrase 'or declaratory' (أو الوضع) must be added to the standard definition to cover wad'i rulings (sabab, shart, mani'). The discussion reveals a critical difference in how scholars conceptualize legal address (khitab): some see wad'i as implicitly demanding a ruling, while the Hanafi position insists on a separate category. Understanding this nuance sharpens your ability to distinguish between types of shari' rulings and their epistemological bases.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish taklifi from wad'i
First, recall that taklifi rulings directly demand or permit actions (wujub, haram, etc.), while wad'i rulings declare something to be a cause, condition, or impediment for another ruling. This classification is central to the debate.
2
Identify the point of dispute
Some Ash'aris argue that the definition of absolute hukm (especially the phrase 'iqtida' aw takhyir') covers taklifi but not wad'i, since wad'i lacks explicit demand or choice. Hence they add 'aw al-wad'i'. Others argue that wad'i is already implicitly included.
The two sides are: (1) explicit inclusion required, (2) implicit inclusion sufficient.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
The second group claims that wad'i rulings involve implicit iqtida'. For example, stating that 'the decline of the sun is a cause of Zuhr' implicitly demands that Zuhr becomes obligatory. Thus the definition without 'aw al-wad'i' still covers wad'i.
The proof is: if x is a cause for y, then y is demanded; therefore iqtida' is present.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The preferred view (al-haqq huwa al-awwal) holds that implicit iqtida' is not enough. The meaning of wad'i is 'the relation of a thing to a thing' (talluq al-shay'i bil-shay'i), which is conceptually distinct from taklifi's demand for an act. A separate condition is needed to ensure wad'i rulings are not excluded.
5
Apply the outcome to the definition
If we accept the preferred view, the definition of absolute hukm becomes: 'Khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin bi iqtida' aw takhyir aw al-wad'.' This ensures sabab, shart, and mani' are recognized as shari' rulings.
This definition is the one adopted in Hanafi usul works.

امرالی امر آخر والفقہاء يطلقونہ :۔ یہاں سے تیسری تعریف ذکر کر رہے ہیں جو فقہا ، نے کی ہے کہ حکم نام ہے اس شئی کا جو خطاب سے
And some added 'or declaratory'. From here it is explained that among the Ash'aris who say 'the address of God etc.' is the definition of absolute ruling, there is a slight disagreement. First a premise: ruling (address) is of two types: taklifi and wad'i. Taklifi is that which relates to the actions of the morally responsible. Wad'i is the name for the address that something is a cause, condition, or impediment for something else, like the address that the decline of the sun is a cause for the obligation of Zuhr prayer, and that sunrise is an impediment for Fajr prayer, and that wudu is a condition for prayer. Now the dispute: some Ash'aris say that in the definition given for absolute ruling, adding the condition 'or declaratory' is necessary, because without it only taklifi address enters the definition (since it has demand or choice) while wad'i address does not (it has neither demand nor choice). And some did not mention (it): but other scholars say this condition is not needed, because wad'i address is also included under the condition of iqtida'. For example, the address that the decline of the sun is a cause for the obligation of Zuhr means that as soon as the sun declines, Zuhr becomes obligatory, so effectively obligation is demanded, and obligation falls under iqtida'. Thus, just as taklifi address enters the definition, so does wad'i. In summary, although wad'i address does not explicitly contain iqtida', it does implicitly. But the truth is the first: here the author mentions the preferred view, that the first opinion is stronger, i.e., adding the condition 'or declaratory' is better, because although sometimes taklifi and wad'i rulings come together, they differ in meaning: the meaning of a wad'i ruling is 'the relation of a thing to a thing', and this is not the meaning of a taklifi ruling. Since their meanings differ, a separate condition is needed to include wad'i rulings. 'Some defined the shari'i ruling': from here the author mentions the second Ash'ari view, whose detail has passed, and its summary is that 'the address of God Almighty connected... etc.' is the definition of shari'i ruling, while the definition of absolute ruling is 'attribution of one matter to another'. And the jurists apply it: from here he mentions the third definition given by the jurists: that ruling is the name for that thing which comes from the address...
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul dispute among Ash'ari theologians regarding the definition of hukm (ruling). The text first distinguishes between two types of rulings: taklifi (concerned with demands regarding actions) and wad'i (declaratory, concerning causes, conditions, and impediments). Some Ash'aris argue that the definition of absolute hukm must include the phrase 'or declaratory' (او الوضع) to explicitly cover wad'i rulings, since wad'i addresses do not contain an explicit demand (iqtida') or choice (takhyir). Others counter that wad'i rulings are implicitly covered under iqtida' because they entail a demand for a ruling: for example, stating that the sun's decline is a cause for Zuhr's obligation implicitly demands that obligation follow from the cause. Therefore, no separate condition is needed. The author (the matn) then declares the first view as preferable (الحق هو الأول) because the meanings of taklifi and wad'i are genuinely distinct—wad'i signifies the relationship between a thing and another thing (تعلق الشيء بالشيء), while taklifi does not. Hence, a separate condition is necessary to fully encompass wad'i rulings. Finally, the passage mentions the third definition from the jurists (فقہاء) that hukm is 'what is established by the address' (ما ثبت بالخطاب), but this is only introduced before the OCR cuts off.

Key Terms
الحكم الوضعي (al-hukm al-wad'i): Declaratory ruling: an address that something is a cause, condition, or impediment for another ruling.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand; in this context, explicit demand (as in taklifi) versus implicit demand (as argued for wad'i).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, why must the condition 'or declaratory' (او الوضع) be added to the definition of hukm?
A) Because wad'i rulings do not involve any demand (iqtida') even implicitly.
B) Because taklifi and wad'i rulings have different meanings and thus need separate mention.
C) Because the majority of scholars reject wad'i rulings as part of hukm.
D) Because the jurists' definition already includes wad'i without that condition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul position requires explicit inclusion of 'aw al-wad'i' in the definition of hukm to preserve the distinct conceptual nature of causes, conditions, and impediments.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
The Dispute over 'aw al-wad'' in the Definition of Hukm
Analyzing the dispute over 'aw al-wad'' in the definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between taklifi and wad'i address and state why some Ash'aris require 'aw al-wad'' in the definition of absolute hukm, while others do not, and give the Hanafi preferred view.

Core Idea
Wad'i hukm is conceptually distinct from taklifi, so 'aw al-wad'' is needed in the definition.

The definition of hukm (legal ruling) is foundational in usul al-fiqh. This passage from At-Tarwih presents an intra-Ash'ari dispute: should the definition include 'aw al-wad'' to explicitly cover wad'i address (causes, conditions, preventers)? Understanding this clarifies the precise scope of the term 'hukm' and its categories.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of khitab
Identify that khitab (address) is divided into taklifi (imposing obligation, prohibition, or choice) and wad'i (establishing a thing as cause, condition, or preventer).
Taklifi directly demands action/abstention; wad'i connects one thing to another.
2
Identify the two Ash'ari positions
Some Ash'aris argue the definition of absolute hukm must include 'aw al-wad'' to include wad'i; others argue it is unnecessary.
3
Understand the opponent's proof
The opposing view claims wad'i address implicitly contains iqtida' (requirement) because declaring a cause for an obligation implies the obligation itself.
They say wad'i is thus covered under the general definition without extra wording.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi author argues that though sometimes coinciding, taklifi and wad'i have different conceptual meanings (wad'i = connection of one thing to another; taklifi = demand/choice). Therefore a separate qualifier is needed.
Conceptual difference (taghayur al-mafhum) necessitates explicit inclusion.
5
State the tarjih
The author prefers the first opinion, i.e., adding 'aw al-wad'' is better for precision.
This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in this text.

التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّدْويج
ثابت ہو جیسے وجوب حرمت وغیرہ۔
مجاز ا: سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔
255
اعتراض: حکم مصدر ہے اور مصدر سے مراد معنی مصدری ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حاصل مصدر اور آپنے جو تعریف کی ہے ماثبت بالخطاب ،، یہ حاصل مصدر ہے لہذا یہ درست نہیں ہے۔
جواب:۔ مصدر سے مراد تو معنی مصدری ہی ہوتا ہے لیکن یہاں اس سے مجاز حاصل مصدرمرا دلیا گیا ہے اس ' ح کہ مصدر کا اطلاق مفعول پر کیا گیا ہے جیسے خلق مصدر کا اطلاق مخلوق (مفعول) پر ہوتا ہے تو یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہے تو مطلب یہ ہوا کہ حکم سے مراد ما خوطب یہ ہے اور یہ درست ہے۔
لکن لما شاع فیہ:۔ سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔
اعتراض:۔ اشاعرہ نے جو تعریفیں کی ہیں وہ حقیقی ہیں اور فقہاء نے جو تعریف کی ہے یہ مجازی ہے تو فقہاء نے تعریف حقیقی کو چھوڑ کر تعریف مجازی کو کیوں اختیار کیا ؟
جواب:۔ ہم نے جو تعریف کی ہے یہ تھی تو مجازی لیکن پھر حکم کا استعمال اس تعریف (ماخوطب یہ ) میں عام ہو گیا جس کی وجہ سے یہ منقول اصطلاحی بن گیا اور منقول اصطلاحی حقیقت اصطلاحی ہوتی ہے لہذا ہماری تعریف حقیقی ہوئی نہ کہ مجازی۔
تلویح
قَوْلُهُ ) وَلَمَّا عُرِفَ الْفِقْهُ اَقُوْلُ الْمَذْكُورُ فِى كُتُبِ الشَّافِعِيَّةِ أَنَّ خِطَابَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْمُتَعَلَّقَ بِأَفْعَالِ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ تَعْرِيفٌ لِلْحُكْمِ الشَّرْعِيِّ الْمُتَعَارَفِ بَيْنَ الأُصُولِينَ لَا لِلْحُكْمِ الْمَأْخُوذِ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْفِقْهِ وَالْمُصَنِّقُ ذَهَبَ إِلَى أَنَّهُ تَعُرِيفٌ لَهُ وَأَنَّ الشَّرْعِيَّ قَيْدٌ زَائِدٌ عَلَى خِطَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَأَنَّ كَوْنَهُ تَعْرِيفًا لِلْحُكْمِ الشَّرْعِيِّ إِنَّمَا هُوَ رَأَى بَعْضِ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ وَ كُلُّ ذَلِكَ لِعَدَمِ تَصَفْحِهِ كُتُبَهُمْ فَتَقُولُ عَرَّفَ بَعْضُ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ الْحُكْمَ الشَّرْعِيَّ بِخِطَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْمُتَعَلِّقِ بِأَفْعَالِ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ وَالْخِطَابُ فِي اللُّغَةِ تَوْجِيهُ الْكَلَامِ نَحْوَ الْغَيْرِ لِلْإِفْهَامِ ، ثُمَّ نُقِلَ إِلَى مَا يَقَعُ
At-Tarwih li-Hall at-Tawdih wa at-Talwih. The definition of hukm should include the qualification 'aw al-wad'. And some added 'aw al-wad': From here it is being explained that among the Ash'aris, those who say "Khitab Allah ... etc." as the definition of absolute hukm, there is a slight difference among them. Before that, as an introduction, a premise needs to be understood. Premise: Hukm (address) is of two types: taklifi and wad'i. Taklifi is that which pertains to the actions of the obligated. Wad'i is the name for the address that something is a cause, condition, or preventer for another thing, like the address that the declination of the sun is a cause for the obligation of Zuhr prayer, and the address that the rising of the sun is a preventer for Fajr prayer, and the address that ablution is a condition for prayer. Now the difference is that some Ash'aris say that in the definition of absolute hukm, it is necessary to add the qualification 'aw al-wad', because if this qualification is not added, then the definition would include taklifi address (since it contains a requirement or choice) but not wad'i address (since it contains neither requirement nor choice). And some did not mention it: But other scholars say that this qualification is not necessary because wad'i address is also included under the condition of requirement, in that, for example, the address that the declination of the sun is a cause for the obligation of prayer means that as soon as the sun declines, Zuhr prayer becomes obligatory, so it also involves a requirement of obligation, and obligation is included in requirement. Therefore, just as taklifi address is included in the definition of hukm, so is wad'i address. In summary, although wad'i address does not explicitly contain a requirement, it does implicitly. But the truth is the first: From here the author mentions the preference that the first opinion is preponderant, i.e., adding the qualification 'aw al-wad' is better because, although sometimes taklifi and wad'i hukm coincide, conceptually there is a difference: the meaning of wad'i hukm is the connection of one thing to another, and taklifi hukm does not have this meaning. So when their meanings differ, a separate qualification is needed to include wad'i hukm. Some of them defined shar'i hukm: From here the author mentions the opinion of other Ash'aris, the detail of which has passed, and its summary is that "Khitab Allah ta'ala al-muta'alliq... etc." is the definition of shar'i hukm, and the definition of absolute hukm is the attribution of a command to another command. And the fuqaha use it: From here a third definition is mentioned, which the fuqaha gave, that hukm is the name for the thing that is established by the address, like obligation, prohibition, etc. Majaz: A response to an objection is mentioned. Objection: Hukm is a verbal noun, and by verbal noun is meant the infinitive meaning, not the resultant noun, and you have defined it as 'what is established by the address', which is a resultant noun, so it is not correct. Response: By verbal noun is indeed meant the infinitive meaning, but here a metonymy has been used to mean the resultant noun, because the verbal noun is applied to the object, like 'khalq' (creation) is applied to the created thing. So here too, it is similar, so the meaning is that hukm means 'what is addressed', and that is correct. But since it became widespread: A response to another objection. Objection: The definitions given by the Ash'aris are real, and the definition given by the fuqaha is metaphorical, so why did the fuqaha abandon the real definition and adopt a metaphorical one? Response: Our definition was initially metaphorical, but the usage of hukm with this definition (what is addressed) became common, hence it became a transmitted conventional term, and a transmitted conventional term is a real conventional term. Therefore, our definition is real, not metaphorical. Talwih: His statement: And when fiqh was defined... I say: The aforementioned in the books of the Shafi'is is that the address of Allah ta'ala related to the actions of the obligated is a definition of shar'i hukm commonly used among usul scholars, not for the hukm taken in the definition of fiqh. And the author opined that it is a definition for it and that 'shar'i' is an additional qualification to the address of Allah ta'ala, and that its being a definition of shar'i hukm is only the view of some Ash'aris, and all that is due to his not having examined their books. So you say: Some Ash'aris defined shar'i hukm as the address of Allah ta'ala related to the actions of the obligated. And address in language is the direction of speech towards another for understanding, then it was transferred to what occurs...
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from At-Tarwih deals with the definition of hukm (legal ruling) in usul al-fiqh, specifically whether the phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or the dispositive address) must be added. The author begins by explaining that khitab (address) is of two types: taklifi (imposing obligations or giving choices) and wad'i (establishing causes, conditions, or preventers). The dispute among the Ash'aris is whether the definition of hukm (absolute) should include only taklifi address or also wad'i. Some argue that without the qualification 'aw al-wad'', wad'i address is excluded because it lacks an explicit requirement or option. Others argue that wad'i address implicitly involves a requirement (e.g., declaring the sun's declination a cause for obligation implies the requirement of the obligation), so it is already included. The author rules that the first opinion is correct: a separate qualification is needed because the two types of hukm have different conceptual meanings: wad'i hukm relates a thing to another thing, while taklifi does not. The passage then presents the fuqaha's definition of hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), which is a resultant noun (ism maful). This leads to two objections: first, that hukm as a verbal noun should not be defined as a resultant noun; second, that the fuqaha's definition is metaphorical while the Ash'ari definitions are real. Both objections are answered. The first is resolved by noting that the verbal noun is used metonymically for the object (as in khalq for makhluq). The second is resolved by arguing that the fuqaha's definition, through widespread use, became a transmitted conventional term, which is a true conventional reality. Finally, a portion of the Talwih commentary is quoted, clarifying that the Ash'ari definition (address of Allah related to actions) is specifically for shar'i hukm as used by usul scholars, and the author of the Tawdih is critiqued for misunderstanding their books.

Key Terms
الخطاب التكليفي (al-khitab al-taklifi): Address that requires performance or abstinence, or gives a choice, pertaining to actions of the obligated.
الخطاب الوضعي (al-khitab al-wad'i): Address that establishes a thing as a cause, condition, or preventer for another ruling.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Requirement or demand inherent in the address.
التخيير (al-takhyir): Option or choice, as in mubah (permissible) rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do some Ash'aris argue that 'aw al-wad'' is unnecessary in the definition of hukm?
A) Because wad'i address is not considered hukm at all.
B) Because wad'i address implicitly contains a requirement (iqtida').
C) Because the fuqaha's definition already includes it.
D) Because the Ash'ari definition is only for taklifi hukm.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm must explicitly include both taklifi and wad'i addresses, as they are conceptually distinct.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
The Fuqaha's Definition of Hukm and Its Defense
Defending the fuqaha's definition of hukm against objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fuqaha's definition of hukm ('what is established by the address') and defend it against the objections that it uses a resultant noun and that it is metaphorical, using the concepts of majaz and haqiqah istilahiyyah.

Core Idea
The fuqaha's definition of hukm is a true conventional reality, not a metaphor.

After presenting the Ash'ari definitions, the passage turns to the fuqaha's definition: hukm is 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), such as obligation or prohibition. Critics raise two objections: first, that hukm is a verbal noun and should not be defined as a resultant noun; second, that this definition is metaphorical. The author defends the fuqaha's definition, showing it is both linguistically sound and a genuine conventional reality.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the fuqaha's definition
Identify that the fuqaha define hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab) — examples: obligation, prohibition.
This is a resultant noun (ism maful) sense.
2
Understand the first objection
Critics say hukm is a verbal noun (masdar) so it should mean the act of judging, not the thing judged. The definition uses a resultant noun.
Grammatically, masdar denotes the action, not the object.
3
Apply the Hanafi response (majaz)
The response uses metonymy (majaz): the verbal noun is applied to the object, as in 'khalq' (creation) used for 'makhluq' (created thing). So 'hukm' can mean 'what is judged'.
This is a common linguistic usage.
4
Understand the second objection
Critics claim that the fuqaha's definition is metaphorical (majazi) while Ash'ari definitions are real (haqiqi).
Metaphorical definitions are considered less precise.
5
Apply the response (haqiqah istilahiyyah)
The author argues that through widespread usage (shuyu'), the term 'hukm' in this sense became a transmitted conventional term (manqul istilahi), which is a true conventional reality (haqiqah istilahiyyah).
Common usage bestows reality on the term.

اعتراض: حکم مصدر ہے اور مصدر سے مراد معنی مصدری ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حاصل مصدر اور آپنے جو تعریف کی ہے ماثبت بالخطاب ،، یہ حاصل مصدر ہے لہذا یہ درست نہیں ہے۔

At-Tarwih li-Hall at-Tawdih wa at-Talwih. The definition of hukm should include the qualification 'aw al-wad'. And some added 'aw al-wad': From here it is being explained that among the Ash'aris, those who say "Khitab Allah ... etc." as the definition of absolute hukm, there is a slight difference among them. Before that, as an introduction, a premise needs to be understood. Premise: Hukm (address) is of two types: taklifi and wad'i. Taklifi is that which pertains to the actions of the obligated. Response: By verbal noun is indeed meant the infinitive meaning, but here a metonymy has been used to mean the resultant noun, because the verbal noun is applied to the object, like 'khalq' (creation) is applied to the created thing. Commentary
This passage from At-Tarwih deals with the definition of hukm (legal ruling) in usul al-fiqh, specifically whether the phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or the dispositive address) must be added. The author begins by explaining that khitab (address) is of two types: taklifi (imposing obligations or giving choices) and wad'i (establishing causes, conditions, or preventers). The dispute among the Ash'aris is whether the definition of hukm (absolute) should include only taklifi address or also wad'i. Some argue that without the qualification 'aw al-wad'', wad'i address is excluded because it lacks an explicit requirement or option. Others argue that wad'i address implicitly involves a requirement (e.g., declaring the sun's declination a cause for obligation implies the requirement of the obligation), so it is already included. The author rules that the first opinion is correct: a separate qualification is needed because the two types of hukm have different conceptual meanings: wad'i hukm relates a thing to another thing, while taklifi does not. The passage then presents the fuqaha's definition of hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), which is a resultant noun (ism maful). This leads to two objections: first, that hukm as a verbal noun should not be defined as a resultant noun; second, that the fuqaha's definition is metaphorical while the Ash'ari definitions are real. Both objections are answered. The first is resolved by noting that the verbal noun is used metonymically for the object (as in khalq for makhluq). The second is resolved by arguing that the fuqaha's definition, through widespread use, became a transmitted conventional term, which is a true conventional reality. Finally, a portion of the Talwih commentary is quoted, clarifying that the Ash'ari definition (address of Allah related to actions) is specifically for shar'i hukm as used by usul scholars, and the author of the Tawdih is critiqued for misunderstanding their books.

Key Terms
حقيقة اصطلاحية (haqiqah istilahiyyah): A term that is made real by conventional usage after being transmitted from its original literal meaning.
مجاز (majaz): Metonymy; using a word in a non-literal sense due to a relation (e.g., cause for effect).
مصدر (masdar): Verbal noun, the root meaning of the action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the passage defend using a resultant noun (ism maful) in defining hukm?
A) It argues that hukm is not a verbal noun.
B) It provides an example from Arabic where a verbal noun is used metonymically for the object.
C) It says the fuqaha made an exception for usul terms.
D) It claims the definition is only for beginners.

Key Takeaway
The fuqaha's definition of hukm is a real conventional term, not a metaphor, and is linguistically valid through metonymy.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
The Hanafi Definition of Hukm Shar'i
Debating the definition of hukm shar'i and addressing objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i, explain how widespread usage transforms a metaphorical definition into a real terminological one, and apply the restriction 'by requirement or authorization' to exclude non-ruling narratives.

Core Idea
Hukm shar'i is Allah's address to actions; its definition is real through widespread usage, not merely metaphorical.

The definition of a legal ruling (hukm shar'i) is foundational in usul al-fiqh. This lesson unpacks a critical refinement of that definition from the Hanafi perspective, showing how objections about metaphorical language and exclusivity are resolved. You will see how the Hanafi school defends its definition as a terminological reality and why a restriction (qayd) is needed to exclude Qur'anic stories from the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its initial definition
The term is al-hukm al-shar'i. The initial definition proposed is 'the address of Allah Most High connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons'. Understand the core components: khitab, Allah, ta'alluq, af' al-mukallafin.
This definition is the starting point; it will be refined.
2
Address the objection about metaphorical usage
Objection: 'Hukm' is a verbal noun (masdar), but the definition uses it in the sense of 'what is addressed' (ma khutiba), which is a derived verbal noun. The Hanafi response: through widespread usage (shuyu'), this metaphorical application becomes a transferred terminological reality (haqiqah 'urfiyyah/shari'iyyah).
Key concept: shuyu' transforms a majaz into a haqiqah 'urfiyyah.
3
Compare Hanafi and Ash'ari definitions
Some Ash'aris define hukm shar'i as the eternal inner speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah. The Hanafi definition focuses on the address as directed and connected to actions. The practical difference: the Ash'ari definition without restriction includes all divine addresses, including stories, while the Hanafi definition can exclude them.
Both agree that khitab is kalam nafsi, but differ on whether it is called address in pre-eternity.
4
Analyze the exclusivity objection
Objection: The definition is not exclusive (ghayr mani') because it includes Qur'anic stories about actions of the mukallafin, which are not rulings. The solution: add the restriction 'by requirement (iqtida') or authorization (takhyir)', or use the broader haythiyya restriction (i.e., connected to an action as being a ruling).
Requirement: obligation, recommendation, prohibition, disapproval. Authorization: permission. Stories lack this connection.
5
Synthesize the final Hanafi definition
The refined Hanafi definition: 'The address of Allah Most High connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons, by way of requirement or authorization.' Alternatively, some hold that the haythiyya restriction suffices. Evaluate which is more precise and why.
The haythiyya argument: the address is connected to the action insofar as it is an action of the mukallaf, not as a mere report.

It becomes established like obligation, prohibition, etc. Metaphor: an answer to an objection is mentioned. Objection: Hukm is a verbal noun, and the verbal noun denotes the meaning of the verbal noun not the derived verbal noun, and your definition 'what is established by address' is the derived verbal noun, so it is not correct. Answer: The verbal noun indeed denotes the meaning of the verbal noun, but here it is used metaphorically for the derived verbal noun, by applying the verbal noun to the object, like 'creation' applies to the created, so the meaning is that hukm refers to what is addressed, and this is correct. 'However, due to its prevalence': an answer to another objection. Objection: The definitions given by the Ash'aris are real, and the definition given by the jurists is metaphorical; why did the jurists adopt the metaphorical definition? Answer: Our definition was metaphorical, but then the use of hukm for this definition became widespread, making it a transferred terminological usage, and transferred terminological usage is a terminological reality; thus our definition is real, not metaphorical. (His statement: 'And when fiqh was known...') I say: What is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is is that the address of Allah Most High connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons is a definition of the legal ruling (hukm shar'i) commonly known among usul scholars, not for the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. The author holds that it is a definition for it, and that 'legal' is an additional restriction on 'the address of Allah Most High', and that its being a definition of the legal ruling is only the view of some Ash'aris. All of this is due to his not perusing their books. So, one may say: Some Ash'aris defined the legal ruling as the address of Allah Most High connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons. 'Address' linguistically is directing speech towards another for comprehension, then it was transferred to that by which verbal exchange occurs. Here it is the eternal inner speech (kalam nafsi). Whoever holds that speech is not called 'address' in pre-eternity interprets 'address' as speech directed for comprehension or speech intended to make comprehending someone who is ready to understand it. The meaning of its connection to the actions of the legally responsible persons is its connection to an action among their actions; otherwise there would be no ruling at all, since there is no address that connects to all actions. So, the special rulings for the Prophet, peace be upon him, such as the permission of more than four wives, enter into the definition, and the address of Allah related to states of His essence, attributes, and glorifications, and other things that are not actions of the legally responsible, are excluded. It may not be said: Adding the address to Allah Most High indicates that there is no ruling except His address, while obedience to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and to those in authority and the master is obligatory, so their address is also a ruling. Because we say: Their obedience is only obligatory due to Allah Most High making it obligatory; thus there is no ruling except His ruling. Then, objection was raised against this definition that it is not exclusive (ghayr mani'), because it includes the stories that explain the states and actions of the legally responsible and the reports connected to their deeds, like His statement (And Allah created you and what you do), even though they are not rulings. So, a restriction was added to the definition that specifies it and excludes what entered from non-instances of the defined term; this is their statement 'by requirement or authorization'. For the connection of the address to actions in stories and reports about deeds is not a connection of requirement or authorization. The meaning of authorization is permission of the action and omission for the legally responsible, and the meaning of requirement is demanding the action from him with prevention from omission—this is obligation, or without it—this is recommendation; or demanding omission with prevention from action—this is prohibition, or without it—this is disapproval. And it may be answered that there is no need to add 'by requirement or authorization', because the restriction of 'being a ruling' (haythiyya) is intended, meaning: the address of Allah connected to the action of the legally responsible in terms of it being an action of the legally responsible. The address's connection to actions in the counter-examples is not from the aspect of them being actions...
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion on the definition of hukm shar'i (legal ruling) from the Hanafi perspective, as presented in Al-Talwih by Taftazani. It addresses two main objections: first, that the definition uses the word 'hukm' in a metaphorical sense; second, why the Hanafis prefer a definition that appears metaphorical over the Ash'ari real definition. The commentary answers that through widespread usage, the metaphorical becomes a real terminological definition. The text then presents the Ash'ari definition (kalam nafsi) and explains its components. It clarifies that the definition includes special rulings for the Prophet and excludes divine attributes. An objection is raised that the definition is not exclusive because it includes Qur'anic stories. The response is that such stories have a different type of connection to actions (not requirement or authorization). The passage then explains the types of rulings derived from requirement (obligation, recommendation, prohibition, disapproval) and authorization (permissibility). Finally, an alternative answer is offered: that the restriction of 'being a ruling' (haythiyya) suffices without adding 'by requirement or authorization'. This entire discussion is a refinement of the definition to ensure it is both comprehensive and exclusive.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-hukm al-shar'i): The address of Allah Most High connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons, by way of requirement (iqtida') or authorization (takhyir).
الخطاب (al-khitab): Here it refers to the eternal inner speech of Allah (kalam nafsi) or the directed speech for comprehension.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Requirement: demanding the action with prevention from omission (obligation) or without (recommendation); or demanding omission with prevention from action (prohibition) or without (disapproval).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i is considered real rather than metaphorical?
A) Because it is based on a verse from the Quran.
B) Because it was originally metaphorical but became a terminological reality through widespread usage.
C) Because the Ash'aris agreed with it.
D) Because it is the literal meaning of the word.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i is the address of Allah connected to actions of the mukallaf by requirement or authorization; it is a real terminological definition due to widespread usage, and the restriction excludes narratives from being mistaken as rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Defining Hukm Shari: The Refinement by Iqtida' and Takhyir
Definition and refinement of hukm shari with objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm shari, explain why the condition 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' is necessary, and apply the definition to classify Quranic verses as rulings or narratives.

Core Idea
Hukm shari is divine address that demands or permits—narrative verses are not rulings.

The term 'hukm shari' is foundational to usul al-fiqh. This passage refines the classic definition by adding the condition of demand (iqtida') or choice (takhyir) to exclude simple reports. Understanding this refinement sharpens our ability to distinguish what constitutes a legal ruling from mere informative speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial definition
The passage begins by stating the simple definition: 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin'. Recognize this as the starting point before refinement.
This definition is attributed to some Ash'ari scholars.
2
Pinpoint the objection
The objection (naqd) is that this definition is not exclusive (mani') because it includes narrative and informative verses about actions of the mukallaf, like 'Wa Allahu khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun' (37:96), which are not rulings.
Such verses are reports, not demands or permissions.
3
Analyze the added condition
To exclude narratives, the condition 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' is added. Understand the two terms: iqtida' covers commands (obligation, recommendation) and prohibitions (tahrim, karaha); takhyir covers permissibility (ibaha).
The condition limits the definition to speech that either demands or permits an action.
4
Examine the alternative response
The text also mentions that some argue the condition is implicit, because the address is already connected to actions from the perspective of being actions of the mukallaf. Evaluate this counterargument.
This shows internal Hanafi nuance; the refined definition is still preferred.
5
Apply the definition
Practice classifying Quranic verses: identify whether each verse is a demand or permission (hukm) or a report (not hukm).
E.g., 'Aqimu al-salah' is demand; 'Wa Allahu khalaqakum' is report.

بِهِ التَخَاطُبُ ، وَهُوَ ههنا الكَلامُ النَّفْسِيُّ الأزلِيُّ وَمَنْ ذَهَبَ إِلَى أَنَّ الْكَلَامَ لَا يُسَمَّى فِي الْأَزَلِ خِطَابًا فَسَّرَ الْخِطَابَ بالكَلامِ الْمُوَجَّه للإفهام أو الكلام الْمَقْصُودِ مِنْهُ إِفَهَامُ مَنْ هُوَ مُتَهَيِّءٌ لِفَهُمِهِ ، وَمَعْنَى تَعَلُّقِهِ بِأَفْعَالِ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ تَعَلَّقُهُ بِفِعْلٍ مِنْ أَفْعَالِهِمْ وَإِلَّا لَمْ يُوجَدُ حُكُمْ أَصَلا ، إِذْ لَا خِطَابَ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِجَمِيعِ الْأَفْعَالِ فَدَخَلَ فِي الحَدْ خَوَاصُ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ كَإِبَاحَةِ مَا فَوْقَ الْأَرْبَعِ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ وَخَرَجَ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِأَحْوَالِ ذَاتِهِ وَصِفَاتِهِ وَتَنْزِيهَاتِهِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا لَيْسَ بِفِعْلِ المُكَلَّفِ لَا يُقَالُ إضَافَةُ الْخِطَابِ إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى تَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنْ لَا حُكْمَ إِلَّا خِطَابُهُ تَعَالَى وَقَدْ وَجَبَ طَاعَةُ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأُولِي الْأَمْرِ وَالسَّيِّدِ فَخِطَابُهُمُ أَيْضًا حُكُمْ ، لأنَّا نَقُولُ إِنَّمَا وَجَبَتْ طَاعَتُهُمُ بإيجاب اللَّهِ تَعَالَى إِيَّاهَا فَلا حُكْمَ إِلَّا حُكْمُهُ تَعَالَى ، ثُمَّ اعْتُرِضَ عَلَى هَذَا التَّعْرِيفِ بِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَانِعِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْقَصَصُ الْمُبَيِّنَةُ لِأَحْوَالِ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَالْأَخْبَارُ الْمُتَعَلَّقَةُ بِأَعْمَالِهِمْ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ) مَعَ أَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ أَحْكَامًا فَزِيدَ عَلَى التَّعْرِيفِ قَيْدٌ يُخَصِّصُهُ وَيُخْرِجُ مَا دَخَلَ فِيهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَفْرَادِ الْمَحْدُودِ ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُمْ بِالِاقْتِضَاء أَو التَّحْيِيرِ ، فَإِنَّ تَعَلَّقَ الْخِطَابِ بِالْأَفْعَالِ فِي الْقَصَصِ وَالْإِخْبَارِ عَنْ الْأَعْمَالِ لَيْسَ تَعَلَّقَ الاقْتِضَاء أَو التَّخْيِيرِ ، إِذْ مَعْنَى التَّحْيِيرِ إِبَاحَةُ الْفِعْلِ وَالتَّرْكِ لِلْمُكَلَّفِ ، وَمَعْنَى الاقْتِضَاءِ طَلَبُ الْفِعْلِ مِنْهُ مَعَ الْمَنْعِ عَنْ التَّرْكِ ، وَهُوَ الْإِيجَابُ أَوْ بِدُونِهِ ، وَهُوَ النَّدْبُ أَوْ طَلَبُ التَّرْكِ مَعَ الْمَنْعِ عَنْ الْفِعْلِ ، وَهُوَ التَّحْرِيمُ أَوْ بِدُونِهِ ، وَهُوَ الْكَرَاهَهُ وَقَدْ يُجَابُ بِأَنَّهُ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى زِيَادَةِ قَوْلِهِمْ بِالِاقْتِضَاء أَو التَّخْيِيرِ ؛ لَّانَّ قيد الحينِيَّةِ مُرَادٌ وَالْمَعْنَى خِطَابُ اللهِ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِفِعْلِ الْمُكَلِّفِ مِنْ حَيْثُ هُوَ فِعل المُكلّف وَلَيْسَ تَعَلُّقُ الْخِطَاب بِالأفْعَالِ فِي صُوَرِ النَّقْضِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا أَفْعَالُ الْمُكَلِّفِينَ ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ ترجمہ:۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ تحقیق خطاب اللہ تعالٰی المتعلق با فعال المکلفین اس حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے جو اصولیوں کے ہاں مشہور ہے نہ کہ اس حکم کی جو فقہ کی تعریف میں ماخوذ ہے اور مصنف اس بات کی طرف چلے گئے کہ یہ اسی ( حکم ماخوذ فی الفقہ ) کی تعریف ہے اور تحقیق الشرعی کی قید خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ پر زائد ہے اور یہ کہ اس کا حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہونا جز این نیست یہ بعض اشاعرہ کی رائے ہے اور یہ سب کچھ ان (مصنف) کے شوافع کی کتب کی چھان بین نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے پس ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم شرعی کی تعریف کی ہے خطاب اللہ المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کے ساتھ اور خطاب لغت میں کلام کو غیر کی طرف سمجھانے کے لئے متوجہ کرتا ہے پھر اس کو نقل کیا گیا اس کی طرف جس سے خطاب واقع ہو اور وہ یہاں کلام نفسی از لی ہے اور جو شخص اس طرف گیا کہ کلام کو ازل میں خطاب کا نام نہیں دیا جا سکتا تو اس نے خطاب کی تعریف کی الکلام الموجھہ لا فہام . وہ کلام جو سمجھانے کے لئے تیار کی گئی) کے ساتھ یا الکلام المقصود منہ افہام من ہو تی الہم ( ایسی کلام جس سے مقصود اس کو سمجھانا ہو جو سمجھنے کے لئے تیار ہو) کے ساتھ اور اس خطاب کے افعال المکلفین کے ساتھ تعلق کا معنی ان کے افعال میں سے کسی فعل کے ساتھ معلق ہونا ہے ورنہ کوئی حکم موجود نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ کوئی خطاب تمام افعال کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوسکتا پس تعریف میں نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کے خواص داخل ہو گئے مثلا چار عورتوں سے زائد کا مباح ہونا اور خارج ہو گیا اللہ تعالیٰ کا وہ خطاب جو اسکی ذات صفات و تنزیہات سے متعلق ہے اور اس کے علاوہ جو فعل مکلف سے متعلق نہیں ہے ( یہ اعتراض کرتے ہوئے ) نہیں کہا جاسکتا کہ خطاب کی اضافت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے خطاب کے علاوہ کوئی حکم ہی نہیں حالانکہ نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام اور اولی الامر اور آقا کی اطاعت بھی واجب ہے پس ان کا خطاب بھی حکم ہے اس لئے کہ ہم (جواب میں) کہتے ہیں جز این نیست کی ان کی اطاعت واجب ہوئی ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے واجب کرنے کے ساتھ پس اللہ تعالٰی کے حکم کے علاوہ کوئی حکم نہیں ہے پھر اعتراض کیا گیا اس تعریف پر کہ یہ مانع از دخول غیر ) نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں وہ نقص داخل ہو جاتے ہیں بیان کئے گئے ہیں جن میں مکلفین کے احوال اور افعال اور وہ اخبار جوان (مکلفین ) کے اعمال کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں جیسے اس بلند و برتر کا ارشاد والله خلقکم و ما تعملون باوجود یکہ یہ احکام نہیں ہیں پس زیادہ کی گئی اس تعریف پر ایسی قید جو اسکو خاص کر دے اور نکال دے ان کو جو داخل ہو گئے تعریف میں محدود کے افراد کے غیر سے اور وہ ان کا قول بالاقتضاء او التحیر ہے پس تحقیق خطاب کا تعلق افعال کے ساتھ قصص میں اور اخبار عن الاعمال میں الاقتضاء او اتخییر والا تعلق نہیں ہے اس لئے کر تخییر کا معنی فعل اور ترک کا مکلف کے لئے مباح ہوتا ہے اور اقتضاء کا معنی طلب فعل ہے بمع منع عن
The address (khitab) is here the internal eternal speech. And whoever holds that speech is not called address in eternity interpreted the address as speech directed for understanding, or speech intended by which to convey understanding to one who is prepared to understand it. And the meaning of its connection to the actions of the legally responsible is its connection to an action from their actions; otherwise no ruling would exist at all, since no address relates to all actions. So the special characteristics of the Prophet (peace be upon him) enter the definition, like the permissibility of more than four wives, and the address of Allah relating to His essence, attributes, and transcendence and other than that which is not an action of the legally responsible is excluded. It cannot be said that the attribution of the address to Allah indicates that there is no ruling except His address, even though obedience to the Prophet, those in authority, and the master is obligatory, so their address is also a ruling? We say: their obedience is obligatory by Allah's making it obligatory, so there is no ruling except His. Then an objection was raised against this definition: that it is not exclusive (mani'), because it includes narrative passages that explain states of the legally responsible and their actions, and reports related to their deeds, like His saying 'And Allah created you and what you do', even though these are not rulings. So a condition was added to the definition that specifies it and excludes what entered from non-individuals of the defined: that is their statement 'by demand (iqtida') or choice (takhyir)'. For the connection of the address to actions in narratives and reports about deeds is not a connection of demand or choice. The meaning of choice is permissibility of action and omission for the legally responsible. And the meaning of demand is seeking the action from him with prevention from omission: that is obligation (ijab), or without it: that is recommendation (nadb); or seeking omission with prevention from action: that is prohibition (tahrim), or without it: that is dislike (karaha). And it could be answered that there is no need for the addition of their statement 'by demand or choice', because the condition of being an address from the perspective of being an action of the legally responsible is intended, and the meaning is: the address of Allah relating to the action of the legally responsible from the perspective that it is an action of the legally responsible. And the connection of the address to actions in the counterexamples is not from that perspective, and that is apparent. [Urdu commentary: I say that indeed the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible is the definition of hukm shari that is well-known among usul scholars, not the definition of hukm taken in fiqh. And the author (sahib al-Tawdih) went to the view that it is the definition of the same (hukm taken in fiqh), and that the condition 'al-shar'i' is additional to 'khitab Allah', and that it being the definition of hukm shari is not but that this is the view of some Ash'aris. And all this is due to his not examining the books of the Shafi'is. So we say: some Ash'aris defined hukm shari as khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin. And khitab linguistically means speech directed to another for understanding; then it was transferred to the one to whom address occurs, and here it is internal eternal speech. And the one who held that speech cannot be called address in eternity defined address as al-kalam al-muwajjah li-ifham (speech directed for understanding) or al-kalam al-maqsud minhu ifham man huwa mutahayyi' li-fahmihi (speech intended to convey understanding to one prepared to understand it). And the meaning of the address's connection to actions is that it is attached to some action of theirs; otherwise no ruling would exist, since no address relates to all actions. So the special characteristics of the Prophet enter the definition, like the permissibility of more than four, and the address of Allah related to His essence and attributes is excluded. It cannot be said that attribution of address to Allah indicates that there is no ruling except His address, while obedience to the Prophet and those in authority is obligatory, so their address also is a ruling? Because we say: their obedience is obligatory by Allah's making it obligatory, so there is no ruling except His. Then an objection was raised against this definition: that it is not exclusive because it includes narratives explaining states of the legally responsible and reports about their deeds, like the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do', even though these are not rulings. So a condition was added to the definition that specifies it and excludes what entered from non-individuals of the defined: that is their statement 'by demand or choice'. So indeed the connection of the address to actions in stories and reports about deeds is not a connection of demand or choice, because the meaning of choice is permissibility of action and omission for the legally responsible, and the meaning of demand is seeking the action with prevention from omission...]
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion of 'hukm shari' (Islamic legal ruling) from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary. The text begins by explaining the term 'khitab' (address) in the definition, distinguishing between linguistic and technical meanings. It clarifies that the address of Allah (swt) is eternal speech (kalam nafsi), and that some scholars restrict 'khitab' to speech directed for understanding. The author then addresses potential objections: first, that the definition might exclude rulings derived from prophetic or authoritative commands; the response is that such obedience is only obligatory because Allah commanded it, so rulings ultimately revert to His address. Second, a major objection is raised: the simple definition 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin' is not exclusive (mani') because it would include narrative and informative verses (e.g., 'And Allah created you and what you do') which are not rulings. To exclude these, the text introduces the refinement of 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' (by demand or choice). 'Iqtida'' covers commands (obligation, recommendation) and prohibitions (tahrim, karaha), while 'takhyir' covers permissibility (ibaha). The text also presents an alternative response: that the address itself already implies connection from the perspective of being an action of the legally responsible, rendering the additional condition unnecessary. The Urdu commentary further clarifies that this definition is the one accepted by usul scholars, not the fiqh definition, and critiques the author (sadr al-shari'ah) for conflating the two due to insufficient study of Shafi'i books. Overall, the passage establishes the Hanafi position that hukm shari is essentially divine address that either demands or permits an action by the mukallaf.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-hukm al-shar'i): خطاب الله المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء أو التخيير (divine address related to actions of the mukallaf by demand or choice)
الخطاب (al-khitab): الكلام النفسي الأزلي أو الكلام الموجَّه للإفهام (the internal eternal speech or speech directed for understanding)
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): طلب الفعل مع المنع عن الترك (الإيجاب) أو بدونه (الندب) أو طلب الترك مع المنع عن الفعل (التحريم) أو بدونه (الكراهة) (demand for action with prevention from omission - obligation, or without it - recommendation; demand for omission with prevention from action - prohibition, or without it - dislike)
التخيير (al-takhyir): إباحة الفعل والترك (permissibility of action and omission)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul scholars in this passage, what is the correct definition of hukm shari?
A) Khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin
B) Khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir
C) Al-amr li-ijab
D) Ma la yakhlu al-mukallaf min al-ahkam

Key Takeaway
Hukm shari is defined as divine address that either demands (iqtida') or permits (takhyir) an action, excluding narrative reports.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
The Definition of Ḥukm Sharʿī and Its Application to Fiqh
Commentary on the definition of hukm shar'i with objections and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the definition of ḥukm sharʿī from the ruling used in the definition of fiqh, and evaluate the Hanafi vs. Shāfiʿī positions on this issue.

Core Idea
The well-known definition of ḥukm sharʿī is not identical to the ruling used in fiqh's definition; conflating them creates redundancy.

This passage delves into a critical dispute in uṣūl al-fiqh: Is the definition 'Allah's address related to the acts of the obligated persons' the definition of ḥukm sharʿī, or is it the definition of the absolute ruling (ḥukm) used in the definition of fiqh? The author clarifies the Hanafi position, addresses objections from Shāfiʿī/Ashʿarī scholars, and refines the definition by adding the qualifier 'by way of demand or choice' to exclude non-ruling reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Competing Definitions
Locate in the text the two definitions at stake: one for ḥukm sharʿī (shared by uṣūliyyūn) and one for the 'ruling' taken in fiqh's definition (the matn author's view).
The commentary explicitly states: 'this is the definition of the shar'i ruling… not the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh.'
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi position is that 'khitāb Allāh al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' defines ḥukm sharʿī, not the ḥukm in fiqh. This avoids redundancy of the word 'sharʿī' in fiqh's definition.
3
Understand the Shāfiʿī/Ashʿarī Objection
Some Shāfiʿīs claim the definition is for the absolute ruling (ḥukm muṭlaq) used in fiqh, citing works like al-Minhāj. They argue that the matn author incorrectly applied it.
The objection is presented by the shāriḥ (commentator) against the matn author.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response points to internal disagreement among Shāfiʿīs: some define ḥukm sharʿī with the same phrase, while others do not. The Minhāj commentary itself shows this, vindicating the matn author.
The text states: 'it became known that according to these Shafi'is, this definition is for the shar'i ruling… according to others it is not.'
5
Examine the Essential Restriction (iqtiḍāʾ/takhyīr)
Without the qualifier 'by way of demand or choice', the definition would include reports (e.g., 'Allah created you') that are not rulings. The addition excludes such reports and completes the definition.
This restriction is added to prevent naqḍ (counterexamples) and to specify the relation of the address to acts.

التَّرُوَيْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويح
الْمُكَلِّفِينَ ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ
ترجمہ:۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ تحقیق خطاب اللہ تعالٰی المتعلق با فعال المکلفین اس حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے جو اصولیوں کے ہاں مشہور ہے نہ کہ اس حکم کی جو فقہ کی تعریف میں ماخوذ ہے اور مصنف اس بات کی طرف چلے گئے کہ یہ اسی ( حکم ماخوذ فی الفقہ ) کی تعریف ہے اور تحقیق الشرعی کی قید خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ پر زائد ہے اور یہ کہ اس کا حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہونا جز این نیست یہ بعض اشاعرہ کی رائے ہے اور یہ سب کچھ ان (مصنف) کے شوافع کی کتب کی چھان بین نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے پس ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم شرعی کی تعریف کی ہے خطاب اللہ المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کے ساتھ اور خطاب لغت میں کلام کو غیر کی طرف سمجھانے کے لئے متوجہ کرتا ہے پھر اس کو نقل کیا گیا اس کی طرف جس سے خطاب واقع ہو اور وہ یہاں کلام نفسی از لی ہے اور جو شخص اس طرف گیا کہ کلام کو ازل میں خطاب کا نام نہیں دیا جا سکتا تو اس نے خطاب کی تعریف کی الکلام الموجھہ لا فہام . وہ کلام جو سمجھانے کے لئے تیار کی گئی) کے ساتھ یا الکلام المقصود منہ افہام من ہو تی الہم ( ایسی کلام جس سے مقصود اس کو سمجھانا ہو جو سمجھنے کے لئے تیار ہو) کے ساتھ اور اس خطاب کے افعال المکلفین کے ساتھ تعلق کا معنی ان کے افعال میں سے کسی فعل کے ساتھ معلق ہونا ہے ورنہ کوئی حکم موجود نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ کوئی خطاب تمام افعال کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوسکتا پس تعریف میں نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کے خواص داخل ہو گئے مثلا چار عورتوں سے زائد کا مباح ہونا اور خارج ہو گیا اللہ تعالیٰ کا وہ خطاب جو اسکی ذات صفات و تنزیہات سے متعلق ہے اور اس کے علاوہ جو فعل مکلف سے متعلق نہیں ہے ( یہ اعتراض کرتے ہوئے ) نہیں کہا جاسکتا کہ خطاب کی اضافت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے خطاب کے علاوہ کوئی حکم ہی نہیں حالانکہ نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام اور اولی الامر اور آقا کی اطاعت بھی واجب ہے پس ان کا خطاب بھی حکم ہے اس لئے کہ ہم (جواب میں) کہتے ہیں جز این نیست کی ان کی اطاعت واجب ہوئی ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے واجب کرنے کے ساتھ پس اللہ تعالٰی کے حکم کے علاوہ کوئی حکم نہیں ہے پھر اعتراض کیا گیا اس تعریف پر کہ یہ مانع از دخول غیر ) نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں وہ نقص داخل ہو جاتے ہیں بیان کئے گئے ہیں جن میں مکلفین کے احوال اور افعال اور وہ اخبار جوان (مکلفین ) کے اعمال کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں جیسے اس بلند و برتر کا ارشاد والله خلقکم و ما تعملون باوجود یکہ یہ احکام نہیں ہیں پس زیادہ کی گئی اس تعریف پر ایسی قید جو اسکو خاص کر دے اور نکال دے ان کو جو داخل ہو گئے تعریف میں محدود کے افراد کے غیر سے اور وہ ان کا قول بالاقتضاء او التحیر ہے پس تحقیق خطاب کا تعلق افعال کے ساتھ قصص میں اور اخبار عن الاعمال میں الاقتضاء او اتخییر والا تعلق نہیں ہے اس لئے کر تخییر کا معنی فعل اور ترک کا مکلف کے لئے مباح ہوتا ہے اور اقتضاء کا معنی طلب فعل ہے بمع منع عن الترک کے اور وہ ایجاب ہے یا بغیر اس منع عن الترک کے اور یہ ندب ہے اور یا طلب ترک ہے ساتھ منع عن الفعل کے اور یہ کراہت ہے اور کبھی جواب دیا جاتا ہے کہ ان کے قول بالاقتضاء والتخمیر کی زیادتی کی ضرورت نہیں اس لئے حیثیت کی قید مراد ہے اور معنی یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی کا خطاب جو فعل مکلف کے ساتھ متعلق ہو فعل مکلف ہونے کی حیثیت سے اور نقض کی صورتوں خطاب ساتھ کہ میں خطاب اللہ تعالٰی کا تعلق افعال کے ساتھ اس حیثیت سے نہیں ہے کہ وہ افعال مکلفین ہیں اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے۔ قوله ولما عرف:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ماتن پر اعتراض کرنا ہے۔
اعتراض: ماتن نے فقہ کی تعریف جو شوافع کے حوالہ سے نقل کی ہے اس میں حکم سے مراد ( خطاب اللہ تعالی ... الخ نہیں ہے کیونکہ شوافع کی کتابوں میں موجود ہے کہ خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ ، حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے اس حکم کی نہیں جو فقہ کی تعریف میں ماخوذ ہے لہذا مائن کا اس تعریف کو حکم مطلق (ماخوذ فی التعريف الفقہ ) کے لئے بنانا درست نہیں ہے اور پھر ماتن نے یہ کہا کہ بعض اشاعرہ کے ہاں یہ تعریف حکم شرعی کی ہے اور بعض اشاعرہ نے کہا کہ اگر اس کو حکم شرعی کی تعریف بنا ئیں تو فقہ کی تعریف میں الشرعیہ کی قیدزائد ہوگی لہدایہ تعریف حکم مطلق کی ہے تو ماتن کا یہ کہنا بھی درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ کتب شوافع میں یہ موجود ہے کہ یہ تعریف تمام اشاعرہ کے ہاں حکم شرعی کی ہے لیکن شاید ماتن نے ان کی کتب میں چھان بین نہیں کی جس کی وجہ سے انہوں نے یہ کہہ دیا ۔
جواب:۔ ماتن کی جانب سے جواب یہ ہے کہ شاید شاریخ نے شوافع کی کتب کا مطالعہ نہیں کیا کیونکہ شوافع کی ایک کتاب المنہاج ،، میں فقہ کی یہ تعریف کی گئی ہے جو ہم نے کی ہے پھر اس پر اعتراض ہوا کہ اس تعریف میں الشرعیہ کی قید زائد ہے کیونکہ اس تعریف میں حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ ہے تو الشرعیہ کی قید لفظ حکم میں ہی ماخوذ ہوئی کیونکہ یہ تعریف حکم شرعی کی ہے اب اس پر اعتراض سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان شوافع کے ہاں یہ تعریف (خطاب اللہ حکم شرعی کی ہے لیکن پھر منہاج کے شارح نے اس کا جواب دیا کہ خطاب اللہ الخ حکم شرعی کی تعریف نہیں ہے تو پتہ چلا کہ بعض شوافع کے ہاں یہ تعریف حکم شرعی کی ہے اور بعض کے ہاں حکم شرعی کی نہیں بلکہ حکم مطلق کی ہے لہذا ماتن کی بات بالکل درست ہے اور شاریخ کی بات درست نہیں ہے۔
فتقول عرف بعض الاشاعرہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاری ماتن کی عبارت کی وضاحت فرمانا ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم شرعی کا معنی بیان کیا ہے خطاب اللہ الخ کہ حکم نام ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے اس خطاب کا جو مکلفین کے افعال سے متعلق ہو۔
I say: Verily, the address of Allah the Exalted related to the acts of the obligated persons is the definition of the shar'i ruling (hukm shar'i) that is well-known among the usulis, not the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. And the author proceeded to say that this is the definition of that same (ruling taken in fiqh), and that the qualification 'shar'i' is additional to the address of Allah, and that this being the definition of the shar'i ruling is not certain—this is the opinion of some Ash'aris. And all this is because he did not examine the books of the Shafi'is. So we say: Some Ash'aris defined the shar'i ruling as the address of Allah related to the acts of the obligated persons. And 'address' (khitab) in language directs speech towards another for understanding. Then it was transferred to the one to whom the address is made, and here it is the speech of the self (kalam nafsi). And whoever held that speech in eternity cannot be called address defined 'address' as 'speech directed for understanding' or 'speech intended for the understanding of the one who is prepared'. And the meaning of the relation of this address to the acts of the obligated persons is that it is attached to some of their acts; otherwise no ruling would exist, because no address can be related to all acts. Thus, the definition includes the special qualities of the Prophet, peace be upon him, such as the permissibility of more than four wives, and excludes Allah's address regarding His essence, attributes, and exaltations, and other things not related to the act of the obligated person. It cannot be said (as an objection) that the attribution of the address to Allah indicates that there is no ruling other than Allah's address, although obedience to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the rulers and masters is also obligatory, so their address is also a ruling. Because we say: It is not certain that their obedience became obligatory by Allah's making it obligatory, so there is no ruling except Allah's ruling. Then another objection was made to this definition: that it does not prevent the entry of foreign elements, because it includes those defects mentioned that are related to the states and acts of the obligated persons and the reports related to their deeds, like the Most High's saying: 'And Allah created you and what you do,' although these are not rulings. So a restriction was added to the definition to specify it and remove what entered, and that is their statement: 'by way of demand (iqtiḍāʾ) or choice (takhyīr).' So verily, the relation of the address to acts in stories and reports about deeds is not a relation of demand or choice. Because the meaning of takhyīr is that the act and its abandonment are permissible for the obligated person, and the meaning of iqtiḍāʾ is the demand to do the act with prevention from abandonment—that is obligation (ījāb), or without prevention from abandonment—that is recommendation (nadb), or the demand to abandon with prevention from the act—that is prohibition (karāhah). And sometimes it is answered that there is no need for the addition of their statement 'by way of demand or choice' because the restriction of aspect (ḥaythiyyah) is intended, and the meaning is: The address of Allah that is related to the act of the obligated person in terms of it being an act of the obligated person. And the cases of objection (naqḍ) are clear that the relation of Allah's address to acts is not in this aspect that they are acts of the obligated persons. This is apparent. His statement: 'And when he defined...': This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The purpose is that the commentator (shāriḥ) raises an objection against the matn author. Objection: The matn author, in the definition of fiqh he quoted from the Shafi'is, the intended meaning of 'ruling' is not 'the address of Allah...' because it is present in the books of the Shafi'is that 'the address of Allah the Exalted' is the definition of the shar'i ruling, not the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. Therefore, the matn author's making this definition for the absolute ruling (makhūdh fī taʿrīf al-fiqh) is not correct. And then the matn author said that this definition is for the shar'i ruling according to some Ash'aris, and some Ash'aris said that if it is made the definition of the shar'i ruling, then the qualification 'shar'i' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant; hence it is the definition of the absolute ruling. So the matn author's statement is also not correct, because it is present in the books of the Shafi'is that this definition is for the shar'i ruling according to all Ash'aris. But perhaps the matn author did not examine their books, which is why he said this. Response: The response on behalf of the matn author is that perhaps the commentator (shāriḥ) did not study the books of the Shafi'is, because in the Shafi'i book 'al-Minhāj', this definition of fiqh is given as we have given. Then an objection was raised that in this definition the qualification 'shar'i' is redundant, because in this definition the intended meaning of 'ruling' is 'the address of Allah the Exalted', so the qualification 'shar'i' is already taken in the word 'ruling', since this definition is for the shar'i ruling. Now from this objection it became known that according to these Shafi'is, this definition (address of Allah) is for the shar'i ruling. But then the commentator of al-Minhāj answered that 'the address of Allah...' is not the definition of the shar'i ruling. So it became clear that according to some Shafi'is this definition is for the shar'i ruling, and according to others it is not for the shar'i ruling but for the absolute ruling. Therefore, the statement of the matn author is absolutely correct, and the statement of the commentator (shāriḥ) is not correct. 'So he said: Some Ash'aris defined...': This is the second part of the commentary's phrase. The purpose is that the commentator (shāri) explains the phrase of the matn author that some Ash'aris explained the meaning of the shar'i ruling as 'the address of Allah...' that the ruling is the name of Allah's address that is related to the acts of the obligated persons.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharḥ) on a matn discussing the definition of ḥukm sharʿī (sharʿī ruling) and its relationship to the definition of fiqh. The author begins by asserting that the well-known definition among uṣūliyyūn—'the address of Allah related to the acts of the mukallafīn'—is in fact the definition of ḥukm sharʿī, not the definition of the 'ruling' used in fiqh. The matn author allegedly made an error by taking it as the definition for fiqh's ruling, leading to redundancy of the qualification 'sharʿī' in the definition of fiqh. The text then presents the Ashʿarī view that 'khitāb Allāh al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' is the definition of ḥukm sharʿī, and explores linguistic and terminological nuances of 'khitāb'. It addresses objections: (1) that the definition would include exclusive rulings for the Prophet ﷺ, which is correct; (2) that it would exclude non-Qur'anic obligations (like obedience to prophets and rulers), which is answered by noting that all obligation is ultimately from Allah; (3) that the definition is not exclusive enough (manʿ al-dukhūl) because it includes reports and stories that are not rulings, leading to the addition of the qualifier 'by way of demand (iqtiḍāʾ) or choice (takhyīr)'. The commentary then examines an objection raised by the shāriḥ (commentator) against the matn author, claiming inconsistency with Shāfiʿī works. The response is detailed: the matn author's view is defended by citing differences within the Shāfiʿī school itself—some take the definition as ḥukm sharʿī, others as ḥukm muṭlaq, as clarified in the Minhāj and its commentaries. The passage concludes by restating that the definition applies to ḥukm sharʿī according to some Ashʿarīs. Throughout, the author follows a dialectical style typical of uṣūl works: stating a position, raising objections, and providing counter-responses.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-ḥukm al-sharʿī): Allah's address related to the acts of the obligated persons, either by way of demand or choice.
الخطاب (al-khiṭāb): Speech directed towards another for understanding; here it refers to the eternal speech of Allah (kalam nafsi) that is related to acts.
الاقتضاء أو التخيير (al-iqtiḍāʾ aw al-takhyīr): Two modalities of relation between the address and the act: iqtiḍāʾ (demand) includes obligation and recommendation; takhyīr (choice) indicates permissibility. Both exclude mere reports.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the purpose of adding the restriction 'bi-al-iqtiḍāʾ aw al-takhyīr' to the definition of ḥukm sharʿī?
A) To include prophetic privileges (khaṣāʾiṣ) in the definition
B) To exclude reports and stories that are not rulings
C) To make the definition apply only to obligatory acts
D) To ensure the definition includes both command and prohibition

Key Takeaway
The definition of ḥukm sharʿī as 'Allah's address related to the acts of the obligated persons' is a uṣūlī definition, not to be conflated with the 'ruling' in the definition of fiqh, and it requires the additional qualifier of demand or choice to exclude non-ruling reports.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
The Definition of Hukm Shar'i: Qualification and Consistency
Objection and response about definition of hukm shari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the differing formulations of the definition of hukm shar'i among Ash'aris do not indicate a substantive disagreement, and identify the role of the qualifier 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir'.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm shar'i is one; the qualifier only clarifies its scope.

In usul al-fiqh, precision in definitions is paramount. This passage addresses an objection about an apparent inconsistency in the commentator's statements regarding the definition of hukm shar'i. The response reveals that the core definition is agreed upon by all Ash'aris; the only variation is whether the qualifier 'by requirement or choice' is included. Understanding this helps you navigate apparent contradictions in scholastic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the objection carefully. What does the objector claim about the commentator's statements? The objector sees a contradiction: first the commentator says 'all Ash'aris' hold this definition, then later 'some Ash'aris'.
The objection is based on a perceived inconsistency in wording.
2
Understand the response
Now read the commentator's response. Does he admit a contradiction or explain it away? He explains that the difference is not in the core definition but in whether the qualifier 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' is included.
The response resolves the contradiction by distinguishing between the definition and its qualification.
3
Distinguish the two versions
The two groups of Ash'aris both use the same foundational definition of hukm shar'i. The difference is only that one group appends 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' (by way of demand or choice), while the other does not. This qualifier specifies that hukm shar'i is limited to acts that are either demanded (wujub/nadb) or given a choice (ibaha).
This distinction affects whether mubah (permissible) is considered part of hukm shar'i.
4
Appreciate the usul significance
In usul al-fiqh, the scope of hukm shar'i determines which acts fall under legal rulings. If the qualifier is included, then acts that are purely permissible (mubah) may be considered outside the definition, whereas without it, they are included. This impacts the classification of actions and the derivation of rulings.
This is not a substantive disagreement but a refinement of terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض:۔ ابھی تو شاریخ نے یہ کہا تھا کہ حکم شرعی کی یہ تعریف تمام اشاعرہ کے ہاں ہے اور اب کہہ رہے ہیں کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم شرعی کی یہ تعریف کی ہے۔
جواب:۔ شارخ نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم شرعی کی یہ تعریف کی ہے اس کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ دوسرے بعض نے کوئی اور تعریف کی ہے بلکہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ بعض حضرات نے حکم شرعی کی یہ تعریف بالاقتضاء او الخیر کی قید کے بغیر کی ہے (جیسا کہ ابھی شاریخ نے فرمایا) اور بعض نے حکم شرعی کی یہ تعریف قید مذکور کے ساتھ کی ہے۔
Objection: Just now the commentator said that this definition of hukm shar'i is held by all Ash'aris, and now he says that some Ash'aris defined it. Response: What the commentator meant by saying that some Ash'aris gave this definition is not that others gave a different definition, but rather that some gave it without the restriction of 'by way of demand or choice' (as the commentator stated earlier), while others gave it with that restriction.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and response concerning the definition of hukm shar'i. The commentator had initially stated that the definition (likely the one involving khitab related to acts of mukallafin) is agreed upon by all Ash'aris. The objection points out an apparent contradiction: later he says 'some Ash'aris' gave this definition. The response clarifies that there is no contradiction; the difference is only whether the definition includes the qualifier 'by way of demand or choice' (bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir). Some include it, some do not, but the core definition is the same. This shows the care needed in understanding definitions in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (hukm shar'i): The address (khitab) of Allah related to the acts of the mukallafin
بالاقتضاء او التخيير (bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir): The qualifier indicating whether the address demands an act (wujub/nadb) or gives a choice (ibaha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between the two groups of Ash'aris mentioned in the text regarding the definition of hukm shari?
A) One group defines it differently from the other entirely.
B) One group includes the qualifier 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' while the other does not.
C) One group defines it as related to acts, the other as related to beliefs.
D) The commentator contradicts himself.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm shar'i is consistent; the qualifier only refines its scope regarding demand and choice.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Defining al-Hukm and Responding to Mu'tazili Objections
Defining hukm and defending against Mu'tazili critiques

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi/Ash'ari definition of hukm, apply the qualifiers (iqtida/takhyir or haythiyya) to distinguish rulings from mere narratives, and evaluate the three Mu'tazili objections along with the Hanafi/Ash'ari responses.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address concerning acts of the mukallaf, as demand or permission; mere narratives are not rulings.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational passage from Al-Tarweeḥ that defines the term 'hukm' (legal ruling). The author not only presents the definition but also defends it against two major lines of objection: first, that it would include mere stories of past nations, and second, that the definition is criticized by the Mu'tazila on three theological and methodological grounds. By understanding these responses, you will grasp the precision of the Hanafi/Ash'ari concept of hukm as an eternal divine attribute related to temporal acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition of hukm
The passage defines hukm as Allah's address (khatab Allah) concerning the acts of the mukallafun. Note the key qualifiers: either 'bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir' (with demand or option) or 'min haythu huwa fi'l al-mukallaf' (from the aspect of making the person a mukallaf). These qualifiers are essential to exclude mere narratives.
The definition is not simply 'Allah's address about acts' but must include the element of ḥukm (demand/permission) or the aspect of taklif.
2
Apply the qualifiers to exclude narratives
The first objection says that stories of past nations relate to acts of mukallafun, so they would be included. The first response: add the qualifier 'bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir' – these stories are not in the form of demand (command/prohibition) or permission, so they are excluded. The second response uses 'haythiyya': the address is considered only from the aspect of making the hearer a mukallaf; stories are merely informative, not intended to impose obligation, so they are excluded. If they do make us mukallaf (e.g., 'fA'tabirU'), then they are included, so no problem.
Both responses achieve the same result: mere narratives are not rulings. The choice between them reflects different methodologies (some add an explicit qualifier, others rely on a refined perspective).
3
Map the five hukm categories from iqtida
The passage outlines that iqtida (demand) generates five types: (1) wajib – act demanded, omission prohibited; (2) mandub – act demanded, omission not prohibited; (3) haram – omission demanded, act prohibited by qat'i proof; (4) makruh tahrimi – omission demanded, act prohibited by zanni proof; (5) makruh tanzihi – omission demanded, act not prohibited. Takhyir (option) gives mubah.
This is the classical Hanafi taxonomy of taklifi rulings. Note that iqtida covers both command and prohibition; takhyir covers permission.
4
Analyze the Mu'tazili objections
The Mu'tazila raise three objections: (1) Hukm is temporal (hadith) while the address is eternal (qadim), creating a contradiction. (2) The word 'aw' (or) in the definition implies doubt, which contradicts the purpose of definition. (3) The definition does not cover wad'iyyah rulings (cause, condition, preventer).
These objections challenge the coherence, form, and comprehensiveness of the definition.
5
Apply the Ash'ari responses
To (1): Ash'aris respond that what is temporal is not the hukm itself but its relation (ta'alluq) to the act; the act's occurrence is a sign (amara) for the eternal hukm, not a cause. To (2): 'aw' here is for division (taqsim), not doubt, so it does not undermine definition. To (3): The definition is specifically for taklifi rulings; wad'iyyah rulings are a separate category and do not need to be included. Some scholars say 'aw' can include them by interpretation.
The Ash'ari responses preserve the eternity of the divine address and the precision of the definition.
