The Two Meanings of al-Shar'iyyah in the Definition of Fiqh
Analyzing the definition of hukm and the meaning of shar'iyyah in fiqh definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two meanings of al-shar'iyyah in the definition of fiqh and apply the correct one based on whether hukm is defined absolutely or as hukm shar'i.

Core Idea
The qualification 'al-shar'iyyah' either excludes pre-revelation rulings or avoids redundancy, depending on the definition of hukm.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks a key ambiguity in the definition of fiqh: what does 'al-shar'iyyah' mean? The answer depends on how we interpret the preceding definition of hukm. By carefully distinguishing between absolute hukm and hukm shar'i, we avoid redundancy in the definition and correctly exclude matters of the heart like faith. This nuance is essential for understanding the boundaries of fiqh as a discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible meanings of al-shar'iyyah
Note that al-shar'iyyah can mean either 'what depends on revelation' (ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar') or 'what is conveyed by the address of revelation' (ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'). Which one is intended depends on the definition of hukm.
2
Determine the definition of hukm in context
The passage considers two cases: (1) if 'khitab Allah...' is taken as the definition of absolute hukm (i.e., the hukm that appears in the definition of fiqh), and (2) if it is taken as the definition of hukm shar'i specifically. Your choice here affects the meaning of al-shar'iyyah.
3
Apply the first scenario (absolute hukm)
If hukm = khitab Allah, then if al-shar'iyyah meant 'conveyed by revelation', it would be synonymous with hukm itself, making the qualification redundant. Therefore, al-shar'iyyah must mean 'what depends on revelation' to exclude rulings like wujub al-iman that do not depend on revelation for their existence.
This scenario makes al-shar'iyyah an exclusionary (ihtirazi) qualification.
4
Apply the second scenario (hukm shar'i)
If hukm is defined as hukm shar'i, then al-shar'iyyah must mean 'conveyed by revelation'. To avoid circularity in the definition of fiqh, 'hukm' in the fiqh definition must then be reinterpreted as 'isnad amr ila amr akhar' (attribution of one thing to another).
Here, al-shar'iyyah is not exclusionary but necessary to match the defined term.
5
Evaluate the objection and response
An objection states that if al-shar'iyyah means 'conveyed by revelation', matters of the heart like wujub al-iman would still be included. The response points to the second qualification 'al-'amaliyyah' (practical), which restricts fiqh to rulings pertaining to external actions (jawaarih), thus excluding matters of the heart. The definition remains valid.
This shows that multiple qualifications can work together to achieve the intended scope.

قال المصنف اذا کان : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارخ نے ماتن کی عبارت کی وضاحت کی ہے جس سے پہلے یہ سمجھیں کہ الشرعیہ کے دو معنی آتے ہیں (۱) ما توقف علی الشرع (۲) ماورد به خطاب الشرع اور یہ بھی سمجھیں که خطاب الله التعلق الخ بعض کے نزدیک حکم مطلق کی تعریف ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے۔ وضاحت:۔ اگر خطاب الله ... حکم مطلق کی تعریف ہو یعنی اس حکم کی تعریف ہو جو فقہ کی تعریف میں ماخوذ ہے تو پھر فقہ کی تعریف میں جو الشرعیہ کی قید ہے اس سے مراد ما توقف على الشرع ہوگا نہ کہ ماورد به خطاب الشرع کیونکہ اگر ماورد ... الخ مراد لین تو اس قید کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہو گا بلکہ الشرعیہ اور الا حکام سے مراد ایک ہی چیز ہوگی کیونکہ حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ ہوگا اور الشرعیہ سے مراد ماورد الخ ہوگا اور یہ دونوں ایک ہی چیز ہیں تو اسوقت الشرعیہ کی قید کا زائد ہونا لازم آئے گا اس لئے اس سے مراد ما نتوقف علی الشرع ہو گا اور یہ قید احترازی بن جائے گی ان خطابات کے لئے جو شرعیت پر موقوف نہیں ہیں جیسے و جوب ایمان وغیرہ کہ یہ خطاب اللہ میں داخل ہیں لیکن شرعیت پر موقوف نہیں اور اگر خطاب اللہ المتعلق ... الخ حکم شرعی کی تعریف نہو یعنی الحکم الشرعی محدود ہو اور خطاب اللہ الخ حد ہو تو پھر لفظ الشرعی ( جو محدود میں ہے ) سے مراد ماورد بہ خطاب الشارع ہوگا نہ کہ ما توقف علی الشرع کیونکہ اگر اس وقت اس سے مراد ما توقف علی الشرع ہو تو محدود کا خاص ہونا اور حد کا عام ہونا لازم آئے گا وہ اس طرح کہ ما توقف (محدود) میں صرف وہ خطابات داخل ہوں گے جو شرعیت پر موقوف ہیں اور خطاب اللہ (حد) میں وہ خطابات بھی داخل ہونگے جو شرعیت پر موقوف نہیں اور وہ بھی جو شرعیت پر موقوف ہیں تو حد عام ہو جائے گی اور محمد ود خاص ہوگا اور حد کا محدود سے عام ہونا درست نہیں ہے۔

الشرع کا معنیٰ ایک ہے جس کی وجہ سے شرعیہ کی قید حکم میں ہی ماخوذ ہے تو اس تکرار سے بچنے کے لئے ہم کہیں گے خطاب
اللہ الخ کے حکم شرعی ہونے کی صورت میں فقہ کی تعریف میں حکم سے مراد اسناد امرالی امر آخر ہوگا۔

قولہ الفقہاء:۔ یہاں سے ماتن پر ہونے والے ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے۔ اعتراض: فقہاء نے حکم کی تعریف ما ثبت بالخطاب کے ساتھ کی ہے اور یہ معنی مجازی ہے کیونکہ اس میں مصدر (حکم) کا اطلاق اسم مفعول ( محکوم ) پر کیا گیا ہے اور کسی بھی چیز کی تعریف حقیقی کی جاتی ہے مجازی نہیں لہذا یہ تعریف درست نہیں۔ جواب:۔ یہ تعریف حقیقی ہی ہے کیونکہ حکم فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں ما ثبت بالخطاب کی طرف منقول ہو گیا ہے اور منقول کے ساتھ تعریف حقیقی ہی ہوتی ہے ہاں زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ لازم آئے گا کہ مجاز لغوی ہے اور اس کا کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایسا ہوتا رہتا ہے جیسے صلوہ کی تعریف ارکان مخصوصہ کے ساتھ کی جاتی ہے حالانکہ یہ لغتہ مجاز ہے۔

يَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أَى عَلَى تَعرِيفِ الحُكمِ وَهُوَ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى إِلَخ إِنَّ الحُكم المُصطَلَحَ بَينَ الفُقَهَاءِ مَا ثَبَتَ بِالخِطَابِ لَا هُوَ أَى لَا الخِطَابُ فَلا يَكُونُ مَا ذُكِرَ تَعرِيفًا لِلحُكمِ المُصْطَلَحٍ بَيْنَ الفُقَهَاءِ وَهُوَ المَقْصُودُ بِالتَّعْرِيفِ هُنَا وَأَيضًا
The author said: 'when such...' This is the second part of the commentary's expression. From here the commentator clarifies the matn's expression. Before that, understand that al-shar'iyyah has two meanings: (1) what depends on revelation (ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar'), (2) what is conveyed by the address of revelation (ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'). Also understand that 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq...' according to some is the definition of absolute hukm, and according to some is the definition of hukm shar'i. Explanation: If 'khitab Allah...' is the definition of absolute hukm—i.e., the definition of that hukm which is taken in the definition of fiqh—then in the definition of fiqh, the qualification 'al-shar'iyyah' refers to 'ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar', not 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'. Because if the latter were meant, that qualification would have no benefit; rather al-shar'iyyah and al-ahkam would refer to the same thing. Because hukm would mean khitab Allah, and al-shar'iyyah would mean ma warada bihi khitab al-shar', and these two are the same, so the qualification would be redundant. Therefore, by it is meant 'ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar', and this qualification becomes exclusionary for those addresses that do not depend on revelation, like the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman) etc., which are included in khitab Allah but do not depend on revelation. And if 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq...' is the definition of hukm shar'i—i.e., al-hukm al-shar'i is the defined term and khitab Allah is the definition—then the word 'al-shar'i' (which is in the defined term) means 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'' not 'ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar'. Because if at that time it meant the latter, then the defined term would be specific and the definition general, necessary: that 'ma tawaqqafa' (defined) includes only those addresses that depend on revelation, while 'khitab Allah' (definition) includes both those that depend and those that do not, so the definition would be more general than the defined term, and that is not valid.

Clarification of the matn:
His statement: 'fa al-hukm 'ala hadha...': This is the first part of the commentary's expression. The commentator clarifies the matn's expression. Explanation: If 'khitab Allah...' is the definition of hukm shar'i, then in the definition of fiqh, 'hukm' means the attribution of one thing to another (isnad amr ila amr akhar), not khitab Allah. Because it has already passed that if 'khitab Allah...' is the definition of hukm shar'i, then in the definition of fiqh the qualification 'al-shar'iyyah' means 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar''. Now if in the definition of fiqh we take 'hukm' to mean khitab Allah and 'al-shar'iyyah' to mean 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'', then the qualification 'al-shar'iyyah' would be redundant because 'khitab Allah' and 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'' have the same meaning, so the qualification is already included in 'hukm'. To avoid this redundancy, we say that in the case of 'khitab Allah...' being hukm shar'i, in the definition of fiqh 'hukm' means the attribution of one thing to another.

'Fa in qila': This is the second part of the commentary's expression. The commentator assumes an objection and responds. Objection: If 'hukm' means attribution of one thing to another, and 'al-shar'iyyah' means 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'', then those actions on which an address has been revealed but which do not depend on revelation—like the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman) etc.—would not be excluded by this qualification, and they would enter into the definition of fiqh, although knowledge of them is not fiqh. So the definition would not be correct. Response: Your saying that such addresses not depending on revelation are not excluded by the qualification 'al-shar'iyyah' is correct. But it is not correct to say that they are not excluded at all from the definition of fiqh, because after 'al-shar'iyyah' there is the qualification 'al-'amaliyyah', which refers to rulings that pertain to the limbs (jawaarih). By this qualification, those addresses that pertain to the heart—like the obligation of faith—are excluded. So when they are excluded by the qualification 'al-'amaliyyah', the definition is completely correct, because the purpose is to exclude such addresses from the definition of fiqh, no matter which qualification excludes them. And this purpose is achieved. Therefore the definition is correct.

His statement: 'al-fuqaha'' : From here the purpose is to answer an objection against the matn. Objection: The fuqaha have defined hukm as 'ma thabata bil-khitab' (what is established by the address), and this is a metaphorical meaning because in it the infinitive (hukm) is applied to the passive participle (mahkum). And any definition of a thing is with its real meaning, not metaphorical. So this definition is not correct. Response: This definition is indeed real (haqiqi) because hukm in the terminology of the fuqaha has been transferred (manqul) to mean 'ma thabata bil-khitab', and with a transferred meaning, the definition is real. At most, it follows that it is a lexical metaphor (majaz lughawi), and that is not objectionable because such occurs frequently, like the definition of salah with specific pillars, although lexically it is metaphorical.

[End of page] It is objected against it—i.e., against the definition of hukm as 'khiab Allah ta'ala...'—that the conventional hukm among the fuqaha is 'what is established by the address', not the address itself. So what has been mentioned is not a definition of the conventional hukm among the fuqaha, which is intended by the definition here. Also...

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Al-Tawdih, focusing on the definition of hukm shar'i and its role in the definition of fiqh. The author begins by noting that the term 'al-shar'iyyah' (the legal) has two possible meanings: (1) that which depends on revelation for its existence, and (2) that which is stated by the address of the Lawgiver. He then explains that the correct interpretation depends on whether the phrase 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq...' is taken as the definition of absolute hukm (the hukm that appears in the definition of fiqh) or hukm shar'i specifically.

If it defines absolute hukm, then 'al-shar'iyyah' must mean 'what depends on revelation' (ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar') to avoid redundancy with 'hukm' itself. This exclusionary qualification ensures that rulings like the obligation of faith (which come from Allah's address but do not depend on revelation for their existence) are excluded from the definition of fiqh.

If it defines hukm shar'i, then 'al-shar'iyyah' means 'what is conveyed by the Lawgiver's address' (ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'). In this case, to prevent circularity, 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh must be understood not as the address itself but as the attribution of one thing to another (isnad amr ila amr akhar), because otherwise the qualification 'al-shar'iyyah' would repeat what is already in 'hukm'.

The commentator then addresses an objection: If 'al-shar'iyyah' means 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar', then actions like the obligation of faith (which are addressed but do not depend on revelation) would still be included. The response points out that the definition of fiqh includes an additional qualification: 'al-'amaliyyah' (practical), which restricts it to rulings pertaining to external actions (jawaarih), thus excluding matters of the heart. So the definition works.

Finally, the passage discusses an objection about the fuqaha's definition of hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab). Critics say this is a metaphorical usage, and definitions should be real. The response explains that in legal terminology, 'hukm' has been transferred (manqul) from its original lexical meaning to this technical meaning, so a definition based on it is real, not metaphorical. Similar transfers occur for terms like 'salah' (prayer) which is defined by specific pillars, though originally meaning 'supplication'.

The passage ends with an incomplete Arabic line objecting that if hukm has been defined as 'khiab Allah', it does not match the fuqaha's conventional definition, which is 'what is established by the address', not the address itself.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-hukm al-shar'i): The ruling that is either defined by khitab Allah or is the khitab itself, with two interpretations discussed
الشَرْعِيَّة (al-shar'iyyah): A qualification in the definition of fiqh meaning either what depends on revelation or what is stated by revelation
ما ثبت بالخطاب (ma thabata bil-khitab): The conventional definition of hukm among fuqaha: what is established by the address (the ruling itself, not the address)

Checkpoint
In the definition of fiqh, if 'khitab Allah...' is taken as the definition of absolute hukm, what must 'shar'iyyah' mean to avoid redundancy?
A) ما ورد به خطاب الشرع (ma warada bihi khitab al-shar)
B) ما توقف على الشرع (ma tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar)
C) نفس خطاب الله (nafs khitab Allah)
D) الحكم العقلي (al-hukm al-'aqli)

Key Takeaway
The correct interpretation of 'al-shar'iyyah' in fiqh's definition hinges on whether hukm is absolute or specifically shar'i, and the qualification 'al-'amaliyyah' ensures only practical rulings are included.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Refining the Definitions of Hukm and Fiqh in Hanafi Usul
Critical refinement of the definitions of hukm and fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the technical Hanafi definition of hukm (ma thabat bil-khitab) from the address itself, and explain how the restrictions 'amaliyyah' and 'related to actions of mukallaf' exclude heart actions, minors' rulings, and qiyas from fiqh.

Core Idea
Hanafi hukm is the result of the address, not the address; fiqh is limited to practical limb-actions.

In earlier lessons, you may have encountered the definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah' and fiqh as 'knowledge of practical rulings.' However, these definitions face several objections that require careful refinement. This passage from a sharh on al-Tawzih wa al-Talwih dissects these objections and fine-tunes the definitions to ensure precision. We will walk through each objection and the Hanafi response, clarifying the technical terminology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial definitions under attack
The passage begins by noting that in the definition of fiqh, 'hukm' is interpreted as 'isnad al-amr ila al-amr al-akhir' (attribution of command to the final command). It then assumes an objection: that this would include heart actions like wujub al-iman. Recognize the starting point of the debate.
This initial definition is from the sharh being commented on.
2
Trace the objection concerning heart actions
The objector argues that if 'hukm' and 'shar'iyyah' are taken broadly, rulings like obligation of faith (which are not 'amali) would enter fiqh, which is incorrect. The Hanafi response invokes the subsequent restriction 'amaliyyah' to exclude heart-related rulings.
'Amaliyyah' means practical, related to limbs, not beliefs.
3
Analyze the objection about the definition of technical hukm
A second objection states that the fuqaha' define hukm as 'ma thabat bil-khitab' (what is established by the address), which is metaphorical. The response explains that 'hukm' has been transferred (naql) to this technical meaning, making it haqiqi in the discipline.
Compare with 'salat' defined as specific pillars (majaz lugawi but haqiqi shar'i).
4
Examine the exclusion of minors' actions and qiyas
The definition of hukm as 'khitab related to actions of mukallaf' seems to exclude rulings concerning minors (e.g., validity of their sale, Islam, prayer). The response clarifies that for Islam and prayer, the ruling directly applies to the minor; for other transactions, the ruling attaches to the minor's property/liability, with the guardian's act being a separate ruling. Also, rulings established by qiyas are excluded because qiyas manifests (muzhir) the ruling from an underlying khitab, not establishes it anew.
Qiyas does not create a new khitab; it reveals the ruling.
5
Resolve the apparent repetition in definitions
If fiqh is 'knowledge of practical legal rulings' and hukm is 'khitab related to actions of mukallaf', the definition of fiqh becomes 'knowledge of khitabat related to actions of mukallaf, practical and legal', which seems repetitive. The resolution: 'actions' in the hukm definition includes both limb and heart actions, while 'practical' in fiqh restricts to limbs. Hence no redundancy.
This subtle distinction preserves the uniqueness of each definition.

اللہ الخ کے حکم شرعی ہونے کی صورت میں فقہ کی تعریف میں حکم سے مراد اسناد امرالی امر آخر ہوگا۔
فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے فرض شاریخ اعتراض کو نقل کر کے جواب دیتا ہے۔ اعتراض: اگر حکم سے مراد اسناد امرالی امر آخر ہو اور ادھر الشرعیہ سے مراد بھی ماورد به خطاب الشرع ہو تو وہ افعال جن پر خطاب تو وارد ہوا ہے لیکن وہ شرعیت پر موقوف نہیں مثلاً وجوب ایمان وغیرہ یہ اس قید سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے اور یہ فقہ کی تعریف میں داخل ہو جائیں گے حالانکہ ان کا علم فقہ نہیں ہے تو تعریف تو درست نہیں رہے گی ۔
جواب:۔ آپ کا یہ کہنا تو درست ہے کہ ایسے خطابات جو شرعیت پر موقوف نہیں وہ الشرعیہ کی قید سے خارج نہیں ہوتے لیکن یہ کہنا ٹھیک نہیں کہ یہ بالکل فقہ کی تعریف سے ہی خارج نہیں کیونکہ الشرعیہ کے بعد العملیہ کی قید ہے جس سے مراد وہ احکام ہیں جن کا تعلق جوارح کے ساتھ ہو تو اس قید سے وہ خطابات خارج ہو جائیں گے جن کا تعلق دل سے ہوتا ہے جیسے وجوب ایمان وغیرہ تو جب یہ عملیہ کی قید سے خارج ہو گئے تو تعریف بالکل درست ہے کیونکہ مقصود تو ان خطابات کو فقہ کی تعریف سے خارج کرنا ہے چاہے جس قید سے بھی ہوں اور یہ مقصود پورا ہو گیا ہے لہذا تعریف درست ہے۔
قولہ الفقہاء:۔ یہاں سے ماتن پر ہونے والے ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے۔ اعتراض: فقہاء نے حکم کی تعریف ما ثبت بالخطاب کے ساتھ کی ہے اور یہ معنی مجازی ہے کیونکہ اس میں مصدر (حکم) کا اطلاق اسم مفعول ( محکوم ) پر کیا گیا ہے اور کسی بھی چیز کی تعریف حقیقی کی جاتی ہے مجازی نہیں لہذا یہ تعریف درست نہیں۔ جواب:۔ یہ تعریف حقیقی ہی ہے کیونکہ حکم فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں ما ثبت بالخطاب کی طرف منقول ہو گیا ہے اور منقول کے ساتھ تعریف حقیقی ہی ہوتی ہے ہاں زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ لازم آئے گا کہ مجاز لغوی ہے اور اس کا کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایسا ہوتا رہتا ہے جیسے صلوہ کی تعریف ارکان مخصوصہ کے ساتھ کی جاتی ہے حالانکہ یہ لغتہ مجاز ہے۔
يَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أَى عَلَى تَعرِيفِ الحُكمِ وَهُوَ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى إِلَخ إِنَّ الحُكم المُصطَلَحَ بَينَ الفُقَهَاءِ مَا ثَبَتَ بِالخِطَابِ لَا هُوَ أَى لَا الخِطَابُ فَلا يَكُونُ مَا ذُكِرَ تَعرِيفًا لِلحُكمِ المُصْطَلَحٍ بَيْنَ الفُقَهَاءِ وَهُوَ المَقْصُودُ بِالتَّعْرِيفِ هُنَا وَأَيضًا يَخْرُجُ مِنْهُ مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِفِعَل الصَّبِيِّ كَجَوَازِ بَيعِهِ وَصِحَّةِ إِسْلَامِهِ وَصَلَاتِهِ وَكَونِهَا مَندُوبَةٌ وَنَحوِ ذَلِكَ فَإِنَّهُ لَيسَ بِمُتَعَلِّقِ بِأَفَعَالِ المُكَلَّفِينَ مَعَ أَنَّهُ حُكُمْ فَإِن قِيلَ هُوَ حكمْ بِاعْتِبَارِ تَعَلَّقِهِ بِفِعِلٍ وَلِيِّهِ قُلْنَا هَذَا فِي الإِسْلَامِ وَالصَّلَاةِ لَا يَصِحُ . وَأَمَّا فِى غَيْرِ الإِسْلَامِ وَالصَّلَاةِ فَإِنَّ تَعَلَّقَ الحَقِّ بِمَالِهِ أَو بِذِمَّتِهِ حُكُمْ شَرِعِيٌّ ثُمَّ أَدَاءُ الوَلِيِّ حُكْمٌ آخَرُ مُتَرَتِّبٌ عَلَى الأَوَّلِ لَا عَينُهُ وَسَيَجِيءُ فِي بَابِ الحُكمِ الأحكام المُتَعَلَّقَةِ بِأَفَعَالِهِ فَيَنبَغِى أن يُقَالَ بِأَفعَالِ العِبَادِ وَيَخْرُجُ مِنهُ مَا ثَبَتَ بِالقِيَاسِ إذ لا خِطَابَ هُنَا إلَّا أن يُقَالَ اعلَم أَنَّ المَصَادِرَ قَد تَقَعُ ظَرفًا نَحوُ اتیک طلوع الفجرِ أَى وَقتَ طُلوعِهِ فَقَولُهُ إِلَّا أَن يُقَالَ مِنْ هَذَا القَبِيلِ فَإِنَّهُ استِشَنَاءٌ مُفَرَّغْ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ وَيَخْرُجُ مِنهُ مَا ثَبَتَ بِالقِيَاسِ أَي فِي جَمِيعِ الْأَوقَاتِ إِلَّا وَقتَ قَولِهِ فِي جَوَابِ الإشكالِ يُدرَكَ بِالقِيَاسِ أَنَّ الخِطَابَ وَرَدَ بهَذا لا أَنَّهُ ثُبَتَ بِالقِيَاسِ فَإِنَّ القِيَاسَ مُظهِرٌ لِلحُكمِ لَا مُثبِتْ فَاندَفَعَ الإِسْكَالُ وَأَيضًا يَخْرُجُ نَحوُ آمِنُوا وَفَاعتَبِرُوا أَى مِن الحَدٌ مَعَ أَنَّهَا حُكُمْ فَالْمُرَادُ بِالْإِيمَانِ هَهُنَا التَّصْدِيقُ فَوُجُوبُ التصدِيقِ حُكمُ مَعَ أَنَّهُ لَيسَ مِن الأفعال إذ المُرَادُ بِالأفعالِ المَذْكُورَةِ أَفعَالُ الجَوَارِح وَوُجُوبُ الاعْتِبَارِ أَى القِيَاسُ حُكَمْ مَعَ أَنَّهُ لَيسَ مِن أَفَعَالِ ای الجَوَارِحِ. وَيَقَعُ التكرَارُ بَينَ العَمَلِيَّةِ وَبَينَ المُتعلّق بأفعال المُكَلِّقِينَ ؛ لأنَّهُ قَالَ فِى حَدٌ الفِقهِ العِلمُ بِالأحكامِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ العَمَلِيَّةِ وَفِي الحُكمِ خِطَابُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى المُتَعَلِّقُ بأفعَالِ المُكَلَّفِينَ فَيَكُونُ حَدُّ الفِقهِ العِلمُ بِخِطَابَاتِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى المُتَعَلّقَةِ بأفعال المُكَلَّفِينَ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ العَمَلِيَّةِ فَيَقَعُ التَّكْرَارُ إلَّا أن يُقَالَ نَعَنِي بِالْافَعَالِ مَا يَعُمُّ فِعَلَ الجَوَارِح وَفِعل القَلبِ وَبِالعَمَلِيَّةِ مَا يَختَصُّ بالجَوَارِح فَاندَفَعَ بِهَذِهِ العِنَايَةِ
In the case of the legal ruling of Allah etc., in the definition of fiqh, by 'hukm' is meant the attribution of the command to the final command. If it is said: This is the second part of the commentary's statement; the commentator assumes an objection and responds. Objection: If by 'hukm' is meant the attribution of the command to the final command, and by 'shar'iyyah' is also meant what is brought by the address of the Lawgiver, then those actions upon which an address has come but which are not dependent on being legal (e.g., the obligation of faith, etc.) will not be excluded by this restriction and will enter into the definition of fiqh, whereas knowledge of them is not fiqh, so the definition would not be correct. Response: Your statement that such addresses that are not dependent on being legal are not excluded by the restriction of 'shar'iyyah' is correct, but it is not correct that they are entirely not excluded from the definition of fiqh, because after 'shar'iyyah' there is the restriction of 'amaliyyah' (practical), by which is meant those rulings that relate to the limbs; thus, by that restriction, those addresses that relate to the heart (e.g., obligation of faith, etc.) are excluded. So when they are excluded by the restriction of 'amaliyyah', the definition is completely correct, because the aim is to exclude those addresses from the definition of fiqh, no matter by which restriction, and this aim has been achieved; therefore the definition is correct. His statement: 'al-fuqaha''. From here, the aim is to answer an objection against the matn. Objection: The fuqaha' have defined hukm as 'what is established by the address', and this is a metaphorical meaning because in it the infinitive (hukm) is applied to the passive participle (mahkum), and anything is defined by its real meaning, not metaphorical; therefore this definition is not correct. Response: This definition is indeed real because 'hukm' in the terminology of the fuqaha' has been transferred to 'what is established by the address', and definition by a transferred meaning is real; at most, it would entail that it is linguistic metaphor, and there is no harm in that, because such things occur, like defining 'salat' as specific pillars, even though it is a linguistic metaphor. It is objected against it—i.e., against the definition of hukm as 'the address of Allah, etc.'—that the technical hukm among the fuqaha' is what is established by the address, not the address itself; thus what was mentioned is not a definition of the technical hukm among the fuqaha', which is the intended object of definition here. Also, from it is excluded what relates to the action of a minor, such as the permissibility of his sale, the validity of his Islam and his prayer, and its being supererogatory, and the like; for it is not related to the actions of the legally responsible, despite being a ruling. If it is said: It is a ruling by virtue of its relation to the action of his guardian, we say: This is not valid in the case of Islam and prayer. As for other than Islam and prayer, the attachment of the right to his property or to his liability is a legal ruling; then the guardian's performance is another ruling consequent upon the first, not the same. And it will come in the chapter on rulings pertaining to actions. So it should be said: 'with the actions of the servants.' And from it is excluded what is established by analogy, for there is no address here, except if it is said: Know that verbal nouns can occur as circumstances, like 'I come to you at sunrise' i.e., at the time of its rising; so his statement 'except that it is said' is of this type, for it is an exceptive from his statement 'and from it is excluded what is established by analogy' i.e., in all times except the time of his saying in answer to the difficulty: 'It is known by analogy that the address came with this, not that it was established by analogy'; for analogy manifests the ruling, it does not establish it. Thus the difficulty is repelled. Also, like 'Believe' and 'So take heed' — i.e., the limit — despite their being rulings. For the meaning of 'iman' here is affirmation; so the obligation of affirmation is a ruling, even though it is not from the actions, since by 'actions' here is meant actions of the limbs; and the obligation of taking heed—i.e., analogy—is a ruling, even though it is not from the actions of the limbs. And there is repetition between 'amaliyyah' and 'related to the actions of the legally responsible'; because he said in the definition of fiqh: 'knowledge of the practical legal rulings' and in the definition of hukm: 'the address of Allah Almighty related to the actions of the legally responsible'; thus the definition of fiqh becomes 'knowledge of the addresses of Allah Almighty related to the actions of the legally responsible, practical and legal.' So repetition occurs, except that it can be said: By 'actions' we mean what includes both actions of the limbs and actions of the heart, and by 'practical' what is specific to the limbs. Thus it is repelled by this consideration.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the definitions of hukm and fiqh, addressing multiple objections. The author first clarifies that in the definition of fiqh, by 'hukm' is meant 'attribution of command to the final command' (isnad al-amr ila al-amr al-akhir). An objection is raised: if hukm is defined as such and 'shar'iyyah' refers to what is conveyed by the Lawgiver's address, then acts like the obligation of faith (wujub iman) would be included, yet knowledge of them is not fiqh. The response points out that the subsequent restriction 'amaliyyah' (practical) excludes rulings related to the heart, limiting fiqh to actions of the limbs. The passage then addresses another objection: the fuqaha' define hukm as 'ma thabat bil-khitab' (what is established by the address), which seems metaphorical because the word 'hukm' (infinitive) is applied to 'mahkum' (passive participle). The response argues that 'hukm' has been transferred (naql) to this technical meaning, making it a real (haqiqi) definition, just as 'salat' is defined as specific pillars despite being metaphorical in language. The Arabic text from the matn then presents further objections: the definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah' does not match the technical term among fuqaha', which is 'ma thabat bil-khitab'. Additionally, the definition seems to include rulings on minors' actions (e.g., validity of sale, Islam, prayer) even though minors are not mukallaf. The response distinguishes: for Islam and prayer, the ruling cannot be assigned to the guardian; for other cases, the right attaches to the minor's property or liability, and the guardian's action is a separate ruling. Then the passage excludes rulings established by qiyas (analogy) because there is no explicit address for them. However, it notes that qiyas can manifest the ruling (muzhir) but not establish it (muthbit). Finally, it addresses a potential repetition in the definitions of fiqh and hukm: fiqh is 'knowledge of practical legal rulings' and hukm is 'address related to actions of mukallaf', leading to overlap. The resolution is that 'actions' in the definition of hukm includes both limb and heart actions, while 'practical' in fiqh restricts to limb actions, thus avoiding redundancy.

Key Terms
حُكْم (hukm): In this passage, hukm refers to the technical term among fuqaha': 'what is established by the address' (mā thabata bi-l-khiṭāb). It is distinguished from the address itself.
خِطَاب (khitab): The address of the Lawgiver (Allah) that contains legal directives.
عَمَلِيَّة (amaliyyah): Practical rulings that concern actions of the limbs, as opposed to beliefs or heart actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary restriction that excludes rulings related to heart actions (like the obligation of faith) from the definition of fiqh?
A) The restriction 'shar'iyyah'
B) The restriction 'amaliyyah'
C) The requirement that the action be of a mukallaf
D) The requirement that the ruling be established by qiyas

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi technical hukm is 'what is established by the address' (ma thabat bil-khitab), and fiqh is exclusively knowledge of practical (amali) rulings of the limbs, excluding heart actions, minor-direct rulings, and qiyas-originated rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Three Objections to the Ash'ari Definition of Hukm
Critique of Ash'ari hukm definition with three objections and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three objections raised against the Ash'ari definition of hukm and explain the Hanafi response to each.

Core Idea
Hukm is contingent effect, not eternal speech; definition must include non-obligated persons and qiyas.

This passage critically examines the Ash'ari definition of hukm (legal ruling) as 'the speech of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons.' The Hanafi tradition holds that hukm is the effect of that speech – obligation, prohibition, etc. – which is contingent and an attribute of the mukallaf. The passage presents three objections that expose gaps in the Ash'ari definition: terminological mismatch, exclusion of children, and exclusion of rulings from qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari definition and the first objection
The Ash'aris define hukm as divine speech; Hanafis define it as the contingent effect (obligation, prohibition, etc.). The first objection is that this definition contradicts juristic terminology and attempts to define the contingent by the eternal.
This is a terminological dispute about the nature of hukm.
2
Examine the comprehensiveness issue (second objection)
The Ash'ari definition restricts rulings to actions of obligated persons (mukallafin), excluding children. Some respond by saying children's rulings revert to guardians. The author refutes this by giving counterexamples (child's prayer, sale) and showing that the rulings are independent.
The author suggests replacing 'al-mukallafin' with 'al-ibad' to include non-obligated persons.
3
Analyze the qiyas objection (third objection)
Rulings established by qiyas are not directly from divine speech, yet are considered hukm. The Hanafi response is that qiyas does not create a new ruling but manifests the divine ruling already present in the analogy.
This clarifies that qiyas is a means of discovering the ruling, not a source independent of revelation.

ہماری تعریف جامع ہے کیونکہ بچے کے افعال کے متعلق جو خطابات ہیں وہ بچے کے واسطے سے اس کے ولی کے متعلق ہوتے ہیں مثلاً اگر بچے کے مال میں سے زکوۃ ادا کرنا واجب ہے تو اس کی ادائیگی ولی پر واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ بچے پر اور ولی مکلف ہے لہذا بچے کے افعال بھی مکلف کے افعال ہوئے لہذ ا ہماری تعریف جامع ہوئی۔ رو:۔ ماتن نے اس جواب کو رد اس طرح کیا کہ اول تو ہم مانتے ہی نہیں کہ بچے کے تمام افعال اس کے واسطہ سے ولی کی طرف راجع ہیں کیونکہ کئی اقسام ایسے ہیں جو بچے کے فعل سے متعلق ہیں لیکن ولی کی طرف نہیں لوٹتے جیسا کہ بچے کی نماز کا مستحب ہونا اس کی بیع و شراء کا صحیح ہونا ان احکام کا ولی کے ساتھ کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے اور جو احکام ولی کی طرف راجع ہوتے ہیں وہ بعینہ وہ احکام نہیں ہوتے جو بچے سے متعلق ہوتے ہیں بلکہ وہ بچہ کے فعل کے علاوہ ایک مستقل حکم ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ کا وجوب بچے کے مال میں ہوتا ہے یہ ایک مستقل حکم ہے اب ولی کی طرف جو حکم ہوتا ہے وہ زکوۃ کا وجوب نہیں ہے بلکہ زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہے اور یہ علیحدہ مستقل حکم ہے لہذا آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ بچے کے افعال ولی کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں درست نہیں ہے۔ فینبغی ان یقال:۔ یہاں سے ماتن نے اپنی رائے کو نقل کیا ہے کہ اگر تعریف میں المکلفین کی بجائے العباد کی قید لگائی جاتی اور یوں کہا جاتا کہ خطاب اللہ تعالی المتعلق با فعال العباد تو یہ درست ہوتا کیونکہ عباد میں مکلف بھی داخل ہیں غیر مکلف بھی مثلا بچے وغیرہ بھی داخل ہو جاتے اور اس سے عدم جامعیت والا اعتراض رفع ہو جاتا۔ يخرج منہ ما ثبت بالقیاس:۔ یہاں سے تیسرا اعتراض نقل فرمایا ہے۔ اعتراض (۳):۔ اشاعرہ نے حکم کی تعریف جو کی ہے یہ جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے وہ حکم نکل جاتا ہے جو قیاس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ خطاب اللہ سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا حالانکہ وہ بھی حکم ہی ہوتا ہے الا ان یقال یدرک بالقياس ... یہاں سے جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب:۔ آپ کا اعتراض تو تب درست ہے کہ جب قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت ہوتا ہو حالانکہ قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ قیاس سے تو یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مقیس میں بھی خطاب اللہ وارد ہوا ہے یعنی قیاس سے خطاب اللہ کے مقیس میں وارد ہونے کا اظہار ہوتا ہے نئے سرے سے کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ قیاس مظہر حکم ہے نہ کہ مثبت حکم لہذا آپ کا اعتراض درست نہیں۔
Commentary: He said, 'peace be upon him'. Those Ash'aris who defined hukm as the speech of Allah the Exalted have five objections directed against them; from here these objections are being transmitted, and along with them, responses to some are also given. Objection (1): The definition of hukm given by the Ash'aris does not conform to the terminology of the jurists, because the jurists defined hukm as 'what is related to the speech' [i.e., the consequence of the address] meaning obligation, prohibition, etc., and these are attributes of the obligated person and are contingent, whereas the Ash'aris defined it as 'the speech of Allah the Exalted' and this is an attribute of Allah and is eternal. In summary, according to the jurists, hukm is contingent, and the Ash'aris define it as eternal, so this is a definition through opposites. Therefore the Ash'aris should have defined hukm in a way that conforms to the terminology of the jurists. Objection (2): The definition of hukm given by the Ash'aris is not comprehensive, because some rulings are excluded from it, such as the addresses related to the actions of a child, e.g., the permissibility of a child's sale and purchase, the validity of his embracing Islam, the recommendability of his prayer. All these are legal rulings, but they are not included in the Ash'ari definition, because the definition says hukm is the address related to the actions of obligated persons, and the child is not obligated, so this definition is not comprehensive. 'For it is said: It is hukm'—from this, the author transmitted a response from some persons and then refuted it. Response: Our definition is comprehensive, because the addresses related to the actions of a child are, through the child, related to his guardian. For example, if paying zakat from the child's wealth is obligatory, then its performance is obligatory upon the guardian, not upon the child, and the guardian is obligated. Therefore the actions of the child become actions of the obligated person. Hence our definition is comprehensive. Refutation: The author refuted this response as follows: First, we do not accept that all actions of the child are, through him, referred to the guardian, because there are many types that are related to the child's action but do not revert to the guardian, like the recommendability of the child's prayer, the validity of his sale and purchase. These rulings have no connection with the guardian. And the rulings that do revert to the guardian are not exactly the same rulings that relate to the child; rather, they are a separate ruling apart from the child's action. For example, the obligation of zakat is in the child's wealth—this is an independent ruling. The ruling that goes to the guardian is not the obligation of zakat but the performance of zakat, and this is a separate independent ruling. Therefore your statement that the child's actions revert to the guardian is incorrect. 'Then it should be said'—From here, the author transmitted his own opinion that if in the definition instead of 'al-mukallafin' the restriction 'al-ibad' was placed, and it was said 'the speech of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of the servants', then it would be correct, because 'servants' includes both obligated and non-obligated persons, e.g., children, etc. would also be included, and the objection of non-comprehensiveness would be removed. 'What is established by qiyas is excluded from it'—From here, the third objection is transmitted. Objection (3): The definition of hukm given by the Ash'aris is not comprehensive, because the ruling that is established by qiyas is excluded from it, since it is not established by the speech of Allah, whereas it is also a ruling. 'Unless it is said: It is known by qiyas...' From here, a response is given. Response: Your objection would be correct if a ruling were established by qiyas, but no ruling is established by qiyas; rather, by qiyas it is known that the speech of Allah has also occurred in the analogized case. That is, qiyas reveals the occurrence of the speech of Allah in the analogized case; it does not establish a new ruling, because qiyas is a manifestation of the ruling, not a establisher of the ruling. Therefore your objection is not correct.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the Ash'ari definition of hukm (legal ruling) as 'the speech of Allah related to the actions of the obligated persons.' The commentator, following the matn, presents three objections along with responses. The first objection is a point of terminology: the Ash'aris define hukm as the divine speech itself (eternal), while the Hanafi fuqaha define hukm as the effect of that speech (contingent). This makes the Ash'ari definition a definition through opposites. The second objection concerns comprehensiveness: the Ash'ari definition excludes rulings pertaining to non-obligated persons like children. The text presents a response (attributed to some scholars) that such rulings revert to the guardian, but the author refutes this by giving examples (child's prayer, sale) that do not relate to the guardian. The author then suggests replacing 'al-mukallafin' with 'al-ibad' to include children. The third objection is that rulings established by qiyas (analogy) are not covered since they are not directly from divine speech. The response clarifies that qiyas does not create new rulings but manifests the ruling already present in the divine speech; thus the objection is invalid. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi usul concern for precise terminology and comprehensive definitions.

Key Terms
حکم (hukm): In this passage, hukm is a legal ruling. The Ash'aris define it as divine speech; the Hanafi fuqaha define it as the effect of that speech (obligation, prohibition, etc.).
مکلف (mukallaf): An obligated person, responsible for fulfilling legal duties.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning to extend a ruling from a case with explicit text to a similar case without text.
عباد (al-ibad): Servants; includes both obligated (mukallaf) and non-obligated (e.g., children) persons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what change would make the Ash'ari definition comprehensive?
A) Replace 'al-mukallafin' with 'al-ibad'
B) Add 'and what is established by qiyas'
C) Remove the word 'actions'
D) Define hukm as the effect of speech

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm as the effect of divine address is more comprehensive than the Ash'ari definition, as it includes rulings for all actions of all people and rulings manifested by qiyas.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Hukm: Contingent Attribute or Eternal Address?
Analyzing the Ash'ari definition of hukm and responding to fuqaha's objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Ash'ari definitions of hukm and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) regarding naskh (abrogation).

Core Idea
Hukm in Hanafi usul is a contingent attribute of actions; in Ash'ari usul, it is the eternal address of Allah — a difference that echoes in the theory of abrogation.

This lesson examines a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh: the nature of the shari' ruling. The Ash'ari school defines hukm as Allah's eternal address (khatab), while Hanafi fuqaha' define it as what is established by that address — contingent attributes like obligation and prohibition. This disagreement is not merely semantic; it has profound consequences for how we understand naskh and divine attributes. The passage presents the Ash'ari definition, objections from the fuqaha', and two nuanced responses.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on hukm
Identify how Hanafi fuqaha' define hukm: as what is established by the address (ma thabata bil-khitab), i.e., attributes like wujub and hurma that are contingent (hadith) and attach to the actions of the mukallaf.
This is the operative definition in fiqh works, where hukm is always about the ruling on an action.
2
Identify the Ash'ari definition and the source of dispute
The Ash'ari define hukm as the very address of Allah (nafs al-khatab), which is eternal (qadim) as an attribute of Allah. This contrasts with the Hanafi understanding because the address is not the same as the ruling it produces.
The Ash'ari definition is common in kalam works; the fuqaha' object that it defines a contingent (hukm as used in fiqh) by an eternal.
3
Follow the Ash'ari proof (dalil aqli)
The Ash'ari argue that hukm must be eternal because it is an attribute of Allah; the address (khatab) is one of Allah's attributes, and the ruling is that address itself. They support this by citing that ijab (commanding) and tahrim (prohibiting) are acts of Allah that are eternal.
This rational proof is based on the nature of divine attributes.
4
Analyse the Hanafi responses
The text gives two responses: (1) The term 'khatab' in the definition can be reinterpreted as 'what is addressed' (ma khutiba bihi), which is contingent, making the definition of something contingent by something contingent. (2) Alternatively, 'hukm' in the Ash'ari definition actually means 'ijab' and 'tahrim', which are indeed eternal attributes of Allah, so the definition is of an eternal by an eternal.
The first response uses a rational indication (qarina aqliyya) to reinterpret the term; the second redefines what 'hukm' refers to in the Ash'ari context.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If hukm is contingent, rulings can change and be abrogated (naskh). If hukm is eternal, rulings are immutable — abrogation would only be an unveiling of a previously hidden eternal ruling or a change in the subject's obligation, not a change in the ruling itself.
This difference affects how each school explains naskh and the relationship between different revealed rulings.

ہے حکم سے ما حکم بہ (یعنی جس چیز کا حکم لگایا جائے ) کا اسی طرح مراد لیا جاتا ہے خطاب کے ساتھ ماخوطب بہ کو قرینہ عقلیہ کی وجہ سے بیشک نہیں ہے وجوب نفس کلام اللہ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ بیشک حکم وہ ایجاب و تحریم اور ان کی مثل ہے اور اس حکم کا اطلاق کرنا و جوب اور حرمت پر تسامح ہے تیرا جواب یہ ہے جو علامہ محقق عضد الملۃ والدین کا ہے کہ حکم نفس خطاب اللہ ہے پس ایجاب وہ فقط اس کا قول افعل ہے اور نہیں ہے فعل کے لئے اس سے کوئی صفت حقیقیہ پس بیشک قول نہیں ہے اس کے متعلق کے لئے کوئی صفت بوجہ متعلق ہو جانے اس کے معدوم کے ساتھ اور وہ انعل جب نسبت کی جائے حاکم کی طرف نام رکھا جاتا ہے ایجاب اور جب نسبت کی جائے اس کی طرف جس میں حکم ہے اور وہ فعل ہے نام رکھا جاتا ہے وجوب اور وہ دونوں متحد میں ذات کے اعتبار سے مختلف ہیں صفات کے اعتبار سے اسی وجہ سے تو دیکھے گا ان کو کہ بناتے ہیں وہ حکم کی اقسام وجوب اور حرمت کو کبھی اور کبھی ایجاب اور تحریم کو اور بھی وجوب اور تحریم کو جیسا کہ اصول ابن حاجب میں ہے۔ دوسرا ا مراض یہ ہے کہ بیشک یہ تعریف نہیں ہوتی منعکس بوجہ ان احکام کے نکل جانے کے جو متعلق ہوتے ہیں بچوں کے افعال کے ساتھ اس لئے اولی بات یہ ہے کہ کہا جائے المتعلق با فعال العباد اور تحقیق جواب دیئے گئے ہیں اس اعتراض کے ان کی کتابوں میں کہ وہ احکام کہ جن کا وہم کیا جاتا ہے ان کے متعلق ہونے کا بچے کے فعل کے ساتھ سوائے اس کے کہ نہیں کہ وہ متعلق ہوتے ہیں ولی کے فعل کے ساتھ مثال کے طور پر واجب ہوتا ہے ولی پر صیبی کے مان سے حقوق کو ادا کرنا۔ اور رد کیا ہے مصنف نے اولا بائیں طور کہ نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی بیچ کے جواز میں اور اس کے اسلام کے صحیح ہونے میں اور نماز کے بارے میں اور اس کے مندوب ہونے میں اور ثانیا یہ کہ متعلق ہو نا حق کا صیبی کے مال کے ساتھ یا اسکے ذمہ کے ساتھ ایک حکم شرعی ہے اور ولی کا ادا کرنا دوسر احکم ہے جو مرتب ہوتا ہے اس پر ۔
کیا حکم کی یہ تعریف متعارف بین الاصولیین ہے؟
تشریح: قولہ پر وعلیہ ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شاری ماتن کی عبارت کی وضاحت کرنا ہے کہ مائن نے برد
علیہ سے اشاعرہ کی حکم کی تعریف پر چند اعتراض کئے ہیں اور ان میں سے کچھ کا جواب بھی دیا ہے اور وہ اعتراض یہ ہیں ۔ اعتراض: ۔ یہاں حکم کی وہ تعریف کرنا مقصود تھی جو فقہاء کے ہاں مصطلح اور متعارف ہے حالانکہ اشاعرہ نے جو تعریف کی ہے وہ فقہاء کی اصطلاح کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں حکم، مامثبت بالخطاب یعنی ما حکم یہ کا نام ہے اور ما حکم یہ وجوب اور حرمت وغیرہ ہیں اور یہ فعل مکلف کی صفات میں سے ہیں اور یہ حادث ہیں لیکن اشاعرہ نے حکم کی تعریف نفس خطاب کے ساتھ کی ہے جو کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفات میں سے ہے اور یہ قدیم ہے لہذا یہ تعریف درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ حادث کی تعریف قدیم کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے جو کہ تعریف بالمباین ہے۔

و ہذا مما اور دفی کتب الشافعیہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے ماتن پر تعریض کی ہے کہ ماتن کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ یہ اعتراض ماتن نے خود کیا ہے حالانکہ یہ اعتراض تو شوافع کی کتب میں بھی موجود ہے ماتن نے اپنی طرف سے نہیں کیا لیکن شاریخ کی اس تعریض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اصل میں مائن یہ اعتراض کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ ما قبل میں گذرا معتزلہ نے اشاعرہ پر چند اعتراضات کئے تھے ایک اعتراض یہ تھا کہ حکم تو تمہارے نزدیک حادث ہے اور خطاب اللہ تو قدیم ہے تو حادث کی تعریف قدیم سے لازم آئی تو اشاعرہ نے اس کا جواب دیا تھا کہ حکم بھی قدیم ہے جس طرح خطاب قدیم ہے تو قدیم کی تعریف قدیم کے ساتھ ہورہی ہے نہ کہ حادث کی تعریف قدیم کے ساتھ تو اس پر ماتن نے اعتراض کیا کہ یہاں اس حکم کی تعریف ہو رہی ہے جو ماخوذ فی الفقہ ہے اور فقہاء کے نزدیک حکم ما ثبت بالخطاب ( وجوب حرمت وغیرہ ) کو کہتے ہیں اور یہ تو حادث ہیں تو اشاعرہ کا حکم کو قدیم کہنا یہ فقہاء کی اصطلاح اور مقصود کے خلاف ہے اب ناظرین آپ خود انصاف فرمائیں کہ مائن کا اعتراض شوافع کی کس کتاب میں موجود ہے اور شاریخ کا یہ تعریض کرنا کس طرح درست ہو سکتا ہے بلکہ یہ صرف سینہ زوری ہے اور اس میں کوئی وزن نہیں ہے۔
الاول انہ کما ارید:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے پہلے والے اعتراض کے تین جواب دئے ہیں جواب (۱):۔ جس طرح آپ حکم سے مراد ما حکم یہ لے رہے ہیں اسی طرح خطاب سے مراد بھی ما خوطب یہ ہے نہ کہ نفس خطاب اور ماخوطب به فعل مکلف کی صفت ہے اور یہ حادث ہے لہذا یہ تعریف حادث کی حادث کے ساتھ ہے نہ کہ حادث کی قدیم کے ساتھ لہذا تعریف درست ہے باقی رہی یہ بات کہ ہم نے خطاب سے مراد ما خوطب بہ کیوں لیا تو اس پر قرینہ عقلیہ موجود ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ حکم سے مراد آپ نے وجوب لیا ہے اور وجوب نفس خطاب کا نام نہیں بلکہ ما خوطب یہ کا نام ہے۔ الثانی ان الحکم ہوالا پیجاب:۔ سے دوسرا جواب ہے۔
جواب (۲):۔ آپ کا یہ کہنا غلط ہے کہ حکم سے مراد و جوب ہے بلکہ حکم سے مراد ایجاب اور تحریم ہے اور ایجاب و تحریم اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفات میں سے ہیں جس کی وجہ سے یہ قدیم ہیں لہذا یہ تعریف قدیم کی قدیم کے ساتھ ہے نہ کہ حادث کی قدیم کے ساتھ تو تعریف درست ہوئی۔
The passage begins with a discussion on the definition of hukm: 'The ruling (hukm) is used to refer to what is ruled upon (ma hukim bihi), and similarly khatab is used to refer to what is addressed (ma khutiba bihi) due to a rational indication (qarina aqliyya). Indeed, the obligation (wujub) is not the very speech of Allah. The second response: Indeed, hukm is ijab and tahrim and their like. Applying hukm to wujub and hurma is tolerance (tasamuh). Your response is that of 'Allama Muhaqqiq 'Adud al-Milla wa al-Din: Hukm is the very speech of Allah. So ijab is only His statement 'if'al' (do), and there is no real attribute for the action. The word [؟] when attributed to the ruler is called ijab, and when attributed to that which has the ruling (the action) is called wujub. They are identical in essence but differ in attributes. Hence you see that they sometimes classify the types of hukm as wujub and hurma, and sometimes as ijab and tahrim, and sometimes as wujub and tahrim, as in Usul Ibn Hajib. The second objection: This definition is not convertible (mun'akis) because it excludes rulings related to children's actions. The better thing is to say 'what relates to the actions of servants' (al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-'ibad). Responses have been given in their books: those rulings that are thought to relate to a child's action actually relate to the guardian's action, e.g., it is obligatory on the guardian to fulfill the rights from the child's wealth. The author refuted first by saying that the child's transaction is not valid, nor his Islam nor his prayer being mandub. Second: The relation of the right to the child's wealth or his liability is one shari' ruling, and the guardian's fulfillment is another ruling built upon it. Is this definition of hukm well-known among usuliyyun? Commentary: 'Upon it'—this is the first part of the sharh's phrase. The author (matn) makes several objections to the Ash'ari definition of hukm and gives some answers. The objections: The definition intended here is the one customary among fuqaha', but the Ash'ari definition contradicts it because in fuqaha' terminology, hukm is 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), i.e., wujub, hurma, etc., which are attributes of the legally responsible person's actions and are contingent (hadith). The Ash'ari define hukm as the very address (nafs al-khitab), which is an attribute of Allah and is eternal (qadim). So the definition is invalid because it defines a contingent thing by an eternal thing, which is a definition by what is different. The commentator's critique of the matn: 'And this is from what is found in the books of the Shafi'is.' This suggests that the matn's objection is not original but found in Shafi'i books. The response: The matn intends to object to the Ash'ari response that hukm is qadim like khitab. The matn says that in fiqh, hukm is hadith. The first response from the sharh: 'al-awwal innahu kama urid': Just as you take hukm to mean ma hukim bihi, similarly take khitab to mean ma khutiba bihi, which is an attribute of the action and is hadith. So the definition is of something contingent by something contingent. There is a rational indication for this: you took hukm to mean wujub, and wujub is not the name of the very speech but of what is addressed. The second response: 'al-thani anna al-hukm huwa al-ijab': Your saying that hukm means wujub is wrong; rather hukm means ijab and tahrim, which are attributes of Allah and thus eternal. So the definition is of an eternal by an eternal.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage deals with a core usul al-fiqh dispute: the definition of hukm (Islamic ruling). The Ash'aris define hukm as 'the address of Allah regarding the actions of the accountable' (khatab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin), which they consider eternal (qadim) because it is an attribute of Allah. The Hanafi fuqaha' define hukm as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bil-khitab), such as obligation (wujub) and prohibition (hurma), which are attributes of the actions of the accountable, and thus are contingent (hadith). The author (the matn) objects that the Ash'ari definition defines the contingent (hukm in the Hanafi sense) by the eternal (khatab), which is invalid. The sharh provides two responses. First response: The term 'khatab' in the definition can be interpreted as 'what is addressed' (ma khutiba bihi) rather than 'the address itself', making both terms contingent. The rational indication (qarina aqliyya) is that when ulema speak of hukm in fiqh, they mean the attribute of the action, which is contingent. Second response: Alternatively, the Ash'ari term 'hukm' actually means 'ijab' (the act of commanding) and 'tahrim' (prohibiting), which are attributes of Allah and thus eternal. So the definition is consistent. The passage also addresses an objection regarding the applicability of rulings to children's actions, with the response that rulings technically apply to guardians. The commentator critiques the matn's originality, noting similar arguments in Shafi'i texts.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): In this passage, the term is contested: for Hanafi fuqaha', it means the attributes of actions (wujub, hurma) that are contingent. For Ash'aris, it means the address of Allah (khatab) which is eternal.
الخطاب (al-khatab): The address of Allah, specifically the Quran and Sunnah. In the first response, khatab is interpreted as 'what is addressed' (ma khutiba bihi) for consistency.
الإيجاب (al-ijab): The act of commanding; an eternal attribute of Allah according to the Ash'ari view in the second response.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fuqaha' as presented in the passage, what is hukm?
A) It is the eternal speech of Allah.
B) It is the attribute of the action (e.g., wujub) established by the address, which is contingent.
C) It is the legal capacity of the mukallaf.
D) It is the same as ijab and tahrim, which are attributes of Allah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm as a contingent attribute of actions allows for abrogation and reflects a jurisprudence-focused approach, while the Ash'ari definition as eternal speech preserves divine transcendence.
